Khul' for a Minor: Third Party Contracts and Legal Strategies
Rulings on third party contracting khul' for minor, and legal strategies to make khul' valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on third-party khul' for a minor and apply the legal strategies (hiyal) that make khul' valid while preserving the husband's right to recover the mahr.

Core Idea
A valid khul' for a minor requires either her later acceptance or a lawful strategy; the Hanafi school permits hiyal but invalidates those based on falsehood.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles the practical difficulty of dissolving a minor's marriage through khul'. When the minor cannot consent, the Hanafi jurists devise several legal strategies (hiyal) that involve contracts like hawala and acknowledgment. Understanding these strategies clarifies the school's approach to necessity in family law and the limits of permissible legal fictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline problem
A minor wife lacks full legal capacity to contract khul' herself. How can the marriage be dissolved without her immediate consent? The passage first addresses a third party (ajnabi) contracting khul' without guaranteeing the compensation.
The text presumes the minor understands the contract, the husband, and the dower.
2
Analyze the third-party khul' ruling
There is a dispute: some say the khul' is suspended on the minor's acceptance after puberty; others say it is not suspended (i.e., immediately effective). The Hanafi position is that it is suspended, though a contrary view exists.
This ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Maliki alternative
The author mentions that Imam Malik allows the father to contract khul' if it is in the daughter's best interest (e.g., the husband does not treat her well). This is noted but not adopted.
Maliki position is provided as a comparative reference.
4
Break down each hila step by step
Three legal strategies are presented: (a) third party khul' followed by hawala to that third party; (b) hawala of the mahr to the father, conditional on solvency; (c) father's acknowledgment of receipt of mahr and iddah expenses followed by a ba'in divorce. Work through the contract mechanics of each.
Pay attention to the roles of the third party, the father, and the judge.
5
Evaluate the limits of hiyal
The third hila (father's acknowledgment) is criticized because if the father lies, the husband is not discharged before Allah. This strategy works only in the outward sense (zahir) and is not a legitimate hila.
The critique from Jami' al-Fusulayn warns against falsehood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان العاقد أجنبياً ولم يضمن البدل إن كانت الصغيرة تعقل العقد والزوج والصداق أنه ما هو يتوقف على إجازتها، وقيل لا يتوقف، ومذهب مالك أن الأب إذا علم أن الخلع خير لها بأن كان الزوج لا يحسن عشرتها فالخلع على صداقها صحيح، فإن قضى به قاض نفذ قضاؤه؛ كذا في البزازية. وفيها: وإذا أراد أن يصح خلع الصغيرة على وجه يسقط المهر والمتعة عن زوجها يخالع أجنبي مع زوجها على مال قدر المهر والمتعة فيجب البدل على للزوج ثم يحيل الزوج بما عليه من الصداق والمتعة لمن له ولاية قبض صداقها على ذلك الأجنبي فيبرأ الزوج عن المهر ويكون في ذمة ذلك الرجل ا هـ. وفيها من موضع آخر: وحيلة أخرى أن يحيل الزوج بالصداق على الأب فيبرأ الزوج منه وينتقل إلى ذمة الأب والأب يملك قبول الحوالة إذا كان المحتال عليه املأ من المحيل والغالب كون الأب املأ من الزوج، كذا لو كان المحتال عليه مثل المحيل في الملاءة؛ ذكره في الجامع الصغير. وذكر اسحق الولوالجي أنه لا يملك قبولها لو مثله في الملاءة ولو كان المخالع ولياً غير الأب جعله القاضي وصياً. حتى يملك قبولها. وذكر الحاكم حيلة أخرى وهو أن يقرب الأب بقبض صداقها ونفقة عدتها ثم يطلقها الزوج بائناً. وهذا خاص بالأب لصحة إقراره بالقبض بخلاف سائر الأولياء ويبرأ الزوج في الظاهر لإقرار الأب لا في إقرار غيره ويكتب إقرار الأب بقبض حقها وطلاق الزوج بائناً ا هـ. وتعقبه في جامع الفصولين بأن الأب إذا كان كاذباً في الإقرار لم عند الله يبرأ الزوج. ويحرم عليه فلم تكن هذه الحيلة شرعية ولذا قال في الظاهر ا هـ.
And if the contracting party is a third party and he did not guarantee the compensation, if the minor understands the contract, the husband, and the dower, then it is suspended on her acceptance; and it is said it is not suspended. The school of Malik is that if the father knows that khul' is better for her, such as when the husband does not treat her well, then khul' on her dower is valid; if a judge rules by it, his ruling is enforced. This is from al-Bazzaziyyah. And in it: If one wants to validate the khul' of a minor in a way that drops the mahr and mut'ah from her husband, a third party makes khul' with her husband for a property equal to the mahr and mut'ah, so the compensation becomes obligatory on the husband, then the husband transfers (hawala) what is upon him of the dower and mut'ah to the one who has authority to receive her dower, i.e., that third party, so the husband is discharged from the mahr and it becomes in the liability of that man. End quote. And from another place in it: Another legal strategy is that the husband transfers the dower to the father, so the husband is discharged from it and it transfers to the father's liability, and the father can accept the hawala if the transferee is more solvent than the transferor, and usually the father is more solvent than the husband; likewise if the transferee is equal in solvency. This is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Ishaq al-Walwaliji mentioned that he cannot accept it if he is equal in solvency. And if the contracting guardian is other than the father, the judge appoints him as a guardian so that he can accept it. And al-Hakim mentioned another strategy: that the father acknowledges receipt of her dower and iddah maintenance, then the husband divorces her irrevocably (ba'in). This is specific to the father because his acknowledgment of receipt is valid, unlike other guardians. The husband is discharged in the outward sense due to the father's acknowledgment, not due to the acknowledgment of others. And he writes the father's acknowledgment of receiving her right and the husband's irrevocable divorce. End quote. And it was criticized in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if the father is lying in his acknowledgment, then according to Allah the husband is not discharged, and it is forbidden for him; so this strategy is not legitimate, and for this reason he said 'in the outward sense'. End quote.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq continues the discussion of khul' for a minor wife, now focusing on two topics: (1) the ruling when a third party (ajnabi) contracts khul' without guarantee, and (2) legal strategies (hiyal shar'iyya) to make khul' valid and avoid loss of mahr for the husband. For the third party, there is a dispute: some say it is suspended on the minor's acceptance after puberty, others say it is not suspended. The author also mentions the Maliki position that the father can validly contract khul' if it is in the daughter's best interest. Then, several hiyal are presented from the book al-Bazzaziyyah to achieve a valid khul' that discharges the husband from the mahr. The first strategy: a third party contracts khul' with the husband for a payment equal to the mahr and mut'ah, then the husband transfers (hawala) his debt of dower and mut'ah to that third party, thereby discharging himself. The second strategy: the husband transfers the dower debt to the father, who can accept the transfer if he is more solvent (or equal). The third strategy: the father acknowledges receipt of the dower and iddah expenses, then the husband gives an irrevocable divorce; this discharges the husband only in the outward sense (zahir), and if the father is lying, the discharge is not valid before Allah. The author notes criticism from Jami' al-Fusulayn that this strategy is not legitimate if the father lies.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem (consisting of one or more lawful acts) to achieve a permissible result that would otherwise be difficult or impossible.
حوالة (hawala): Transfer of a debt from one person (transferor) to another (transferee) who becomes liable, with the consent of the creditor.
إجازة (ijazah): Acceptance or ratification, specifically of a contract, here by the minor after reaching majority.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt; legally binding if truthful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what makes the third hila (father's acknowledgment) specific to the father?
A) The father is more knowledgeable about khul'.
B) The father's acknowledgment of receipt is considered valid, unlike other guardians.
C) The father can force the daughter to accept.
D) The father is the only one who can guarantee the payment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits lawful stratagems to achieve a valid khul' for a minor, but any strategy involving falsehood is impermissible and does not discharge the husband before Allah.

Khul' of a Minor Boy vs. Minor Girl: A Legal Distinction
Distinction between khul' of a minor boy and a minor girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the validity of khul' when performed by a guardian on behalf of a minor boy versus a minor girl, and state the legal consequence for each.

Core Idea
Khul' on behalf of a minor boy is void; on behalf of a minor girl, divorce occurs but compensation is not binding.

In Hanafi fiqh, the legal capacity of minors affects the validity of divorce proceedings. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a critical asymmetry: a guardian can effect talaq on a minor girl through khul', but cannot do so for a minor son. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying khul' in guardianship cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Cases
The text contrasts khul' for a minor son (الصغير) and a minor daughter (الصغيرة). Note the key terms: 'صغير' (minor boy) and 'صغيرة' (minor girl).
2
Extract the Ruling for the Minor Boy
The passage states: 'if he makes khul' for his minor son, it is not valid' and 'no occurrence at all.' This means the khul' does not effect any divorce and the marriage remains intact.
The guardian cannot initiate divorce on behalf of a minor son via khul'.
3
Extract the Ruling for the Minor Girl
For the minor girl, 'the payment is not obligatory while the divorce occurs.' The divorce takes effect, but the compensation (mal) is not binding on her because she did not consent.
The girl's guardian can validly give khul', but the girl is not liable for the payment unless she later accepts.
4
Understand the Legal Basis
The difference stems from the minor boy lacking capacity to initiate divorce; his guardian's khul' is ineffective. For the minor girl, she can be divorced by her husband, and the guardian's action can effect divorce, but the compensation is not binding due to lack of consent.
This is based on the principle that a minor cannot be held financially liable without acceptance.
5
Summarize the Practical Consequence
Practically, a minor boy cannot be divorced via khul' by his guardian; a minor girl can be divorced via khul' but the financial compensation is not obligatory on her. This asymmetry is critical for guardians making decisions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالأنثى لأنه لو خلع ابنه الصغير لا يصح ولا يتوقف خلع الصغير على إجازة الولي ا هـ. و حاصله أنه في الصغيرة لا يلزم المال مع وقوع الطلاق وفي الصغير لا وقوع أصلاً.
Just as the female [case], because if he makes khul' for his minor son, it is not valid, and the khul' of a minor is not suspended on the acceptance of the guardian. End quote. Its summary is that for the minor girl, the payment is not obligatory while the divorce occurs, and for the minor boy, there is no occurrence at all.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq draws a clear distinction between the khul' of a minor boy and a minor girl. The author states that if a father makes khul' on behalf of his minor son, the divorce is entirely invalid and does not take effect. This is in contrast to the minor girl: in her case, the divorce can occur (even if the payment may not be obligatory on her if she did not accept). The key point is the difference in legal capacity: a minor girl can be subject to divorce (talaq) initiated by her husband, but a minor boy cannot validly divorce his wife through khul' because he lacks the capacity to initiate divorce. The guardian (father) acts on his behalf, but even so, the khul' is not valid for a minor son. The summary emphasizes: for the minor girl, the divorce takes place but the payment (mal) is not binding on her unless she later accepts; for the minor boy, no divorce occurs at all.

Key Terms
صغير (saghir): A minor male who has not reached puberty; he is legally incapable of effecting divorce, and his guardian cannot make khul' on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on khul' performed for a minor boy (saghir) by his father?
A) It is valid if the father guarantees the compensation.
B) It is suspended until the boy accepts.
C) It is invalid and does not effect divorce at all.
D) It is valid and the father must pay the compensation.

Key Takeaway
Khul' on behalf of a minor boy is void; on behalf of a minor girl, divorce occurs but compensation is not binding without her consent.

Khul' with a Guarantee: Who Bears the Mahr?
Ruling on khul' with a guarantee and subsequent mahr liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a father guarantees a separate sum (e.g., one thousand dirhams) for khul', and distinguish it from when he guarantees the mahr itself, identifying who is liable for the mahr in each case.

Core Idea
A father's guarantee in khul' does not automatically cover the mahr; the husband remains liable unless the guarantee explicitly covers the mahr.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced case from al-Bahr al-Raiq where khul' is performed with a father guaranteeing a sum of one thousand dirhams. The passage clarifies an important distinction: whether the father guarantees a separate compensation or the mahr itself leads to different liabilities. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion about who owes the mahr after khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the scenario: khul' with a fixed sum (e.g., one thousand dirhams) where a father acts as guarantor for that sum.
The father is the guarantor (damin) for the compensation, not necessarily for the mahr.
2
State the initial ruling from Fath al-Qadir
According to Fath al-Qadir, the father owes the sum, the wife takes her mahr from the husband, and the husband takes recourse on the father for the mahr.
This ruling treats the guarantee as covering the mahr effectively.
3
Analyze the author's critique
Ibn Nujaym (al-Bahr al-Raiq) criticizes this as incorrect and distinguishes two cases: guarantee of a separate sum vs. guarantee of the mahr itself.
The author's correction is based on what exactly the father guaranteed.
4
Apply the distinction
If the father guaranteed a separate sum, he owes that sum to the husband; the husband still owes the mahr to the wife, and the husband has no recourse on the father for the mahr. If the father guaranteed the mahr itself, the wife can take the mahr from the father or the husband with recourse.
The key is the object of the guarantee.
5
Note the wife's option and final ruling
The passage suggests the wife has a choice to take her mahr from either the husband or the father when the father guaranteed the mahr. The mufta bihi is the refined view of Ibn Nujaym.
This corrects the earlier unconditional statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو بألف على أنه ضامن طلقت والألف عليه أي على الأب الملتزم لأن اشتراط بدل الخلع على الأجنبي صحيح فعلى الأب أولى، ولا يسقط مهرها لأنه لم يدخل تحت ولاية الأب فإذا بلغت تأخذ نصف الصداق إن كان قبل الدخول وكله إن كان بعده من الزوج ويرجع هو على الأب الضامن أو ترجع على الأب ولا يرجع هو على الزوج، ولو كان المهر عيناً أخذته من الزوج كله إن كان بعد الدخول، ونصفه إن كان قبله ويرجع الزوج على الأب الضامن بقيمته؛ كذا في فتح القدير وليس بصحيح لأن هذا حكم ما إذا خالعها على صداقها على أنه ضامن له فحينئذ إذا رجعت به على الزوج رجع الزوج به على الأب لضمانه، والكلام هنا إنما هو فيما إذا خالعها على الألف على أنه ضامن لها وحكمه لزوم الألف عليه للزوج، وإذا رجعت على الزوج بمهرها فلا رجوع له على أبيها لأنه لم يضمن له الصداق مع أن في جامع الفصولين في مسألة ما إذا خالعها أبوها على مهرها وضمنه أنها ترجع على الأب لا على الزوج، هذا لو ضمن مهرها للزوج وإلا فلا شك أن المهر لا يسقط بهذا الخلع لصغرها ا هـ. والظاهر أنها مخيرة إن شاءت رجعت على زوجها أو أبيها.
His saying: 'And if [it is] with one thousand on the condition that he is a guarantor, she is divorced and the thousand is upon him, i.e., upon the father who accepted the liability, because stipulating the compensation of khul' upon a third party is valid, so upon the father is more proper. And her mahr is not dropped because it is not under the father's guardianship. So when she reaches majority, she takes half the dower if before consummation, and all of it if after, from the husband; and he (the husband) takes recourse on the father the guarantor, or she takes recourse on the father; and he (the husband) does not take recourse on the husband. And if the mahr is an 'ayn (specific property), she takes it from the husband entirely if after consummation, half if before, and the husband takes recourse on the father for its value.' This is from Fath al-Qadir, but it is not correct because this is the ruling for when he made khul' with her on her dower on the condition that he is guarantor for it; then if she takes recourse on the husband, the husband takes recourse on the father due to his guarantee. But the discussion here is when he made khul' with her for one thousand on the condition that he is guarantor for her, and its ruling is that the thousand is obligatory on him to the husband, and if she takes recourse on the husband for her mahr, he has no recourse on her father because he (the father) did not guarantee the dower for him. Moreover, in Jami' al-Fusulayn, in the issue of when her father makes khul' on her mahr and guarantees it, she takes recourse on the father, not on the husband. This is if he guaranteed her mahr to the husband; otherwise, there is no doubt that the mahr is not dropped by this khul' due to her minority. End quote. And it appears that she has a choice: if she wishes, she can take recourse on her husband or on her father.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a specific scenario: khul' for a sum (e.g., one thousand dirhams) with a guarantor (damin). It begins by quoting Fath al-Qadir, which states that if the father guarantees the thousand, he must pay it to the husband, and the wife still takes her mahr from the husband (not the father). The husband can then take recourse on the father. The author (Ibn Nujaym) then criticizes this as incorrect. He distinguishes between two cases: (1) when the father guarantees the mahr itself (i.e., khul' on her mahr with guarantee) and (2) when the father guarantees a separate sum (like a thousand) as compensation for khul'. In the first case, the wife can take her mahr from the husband, and the husband takes recourse on the father. In the second case, the father owes the thousand to the husband, but the wife still takes her mahr from the husband, and the husband has no recourse on the father for the mahr because the father did not guarantee the mahr. The author then cites Jami' al-Fusulayn to support that in the first case (khul' on mahr with guarantee), the wife takes recourse on the father, not the husband. Finally, the author says it appears that the wife has a choice: she can take her mahr from either her husband or her father.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): A guarantor who assumes liability for the payment of the compensation (badal) in khul'.
ألف (alf): One thousand dirhams (or possibly dinars) as a specified sum of compensation in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected view in al-Bahr al-Raiq, if a father guarantees a sum of one thousand dirhams as compensation for his daughter's khul' (but does not guarantee her mahr), who is liable for the mahr?
A) The father must pay the mahr because he is the guarantor.
B) The husband must pay the mahr, and the husband has recourse on the father for it.
C) The husband must pay the mahr, and the father owes the thousand to the husband separately.
D) The mahr is automatically waived.

Key Takeaway
The father's guarantee of a separate sum in khul' does not transfer liability for the mahr; the husband remains obligated for the mahr unless the guarantee explicitly covers it.

Father's Khul' for Minor Daughter: Validity and Guarantee
States the rule for father's khul' with guarantee and explains the fate of the mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a father's khul' for his minor daughter when he guarantees the compensation and identify the effects on the mahr.

Core Idea
A father's khul' for his minor daughter is valid upon guarantee; the daughter retains her right to mahr and may claim it from the husband or father.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling regarding a father performing khul' on behalf of his minor daughter. The key condition is that the father must guarantee the compensation. The daughter's mahr is preserved, and she has a choice upon maturity to claim it from either her father or husband.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
Khul' is a divorce with compensation, performed here by the father for his minor daughter.
The father acts as guardian and also as guarantor.
2
State the ruling with guarantee
The father states he is a guarantor (ḍāmin). The khul' is valid, divorce occurs, and the compensation (e.g., 1000 dirhams) is owed by the father.
Stipulating compensation upon a stranger is valid, so upon the father it is more appropriate.
3
Note the effect on mahr
The daughter's mahr is not forfeited because it is not under the father's guardianship. After maturity, she takes half if before consummation, full if after, from the husband. The husband then recovers from the father; or she may claim directly from the father.
If the mahr is a specific item, the husband recovers its value.
4
Contrast without guarantee
Without guarantee, the compensation is not binding on the daughter, and the mahr remains intact. There is dispute about whether divorce occurs at all.
The relied-upon view requires guarantee for validity.

بالأنثى لأنه لو خلع ابنه الصغير لا يصح ولا يتوقف خلع الصغير على إجازة الولي ا هـ. و حاصله أنه في الصغيرة لا يلزم المال مع وقوع الطلاق وفي الصغير لا وقوع أصلاً. قوله : (ولو بألف على أنه ضامن طلقت والألف عليه أي على الأب الملتزم لأن اشتراط بدل الخلع على الأجنبي صحيح فعلى الأب أولى، ولا يسقط مهرها لأنه لم يدخل تحت ولاية الأب فإذا بلغت تأخذ نصف الصداق إن كان قبل الدخول وكله إن كان بعده من الزوج ويرجع هو على الأب الضامن أو ترجع على الأب ولا يرجع هو على الزوج، ولو كان المهر عيناً أخذته من الزوج كله إن كان بعد الدخول، ونصفه إن كان قبله ويرجع الزوج على الأب الضامن بقيمته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير وليس بصحيح لأن هذا حكم ما إذا خالعها على صداقها على أنه ضامن له فحينئذ إذا رجعت به على الزوج رجع الزوج به على الأب لضمانه، والكلام هنا إنما هو فيما إذا خالعها على الألف على أنه ضامن لها وحكمه لزوم الألف عليه للزوج، وإذا رجعت على الزوج بمهرها فلا رجوع له على أبيها لأنه لم يضمن له الصداق مع أن في جامع الفصولين في مسألة ما إذا خالعها أبوها على مهرها وضمنه أنها ترجع على الأب لا على الزوج، هذا لو ضمن مهرها للزوج وإلا فلا شك أن المهر لا يسقط بهذا الخلع لصغرها ا هـ. والظاهر أنها مخيرة إن شاءت رجعت على زوجها أو أبيها. وفي البزازية : خالعها أبوها أو كائناً أجنبي على صداقها إن ضمن المخالع تم ووقع من كان العاقد وبعد البلوغ آخذت الزوج بنصفه لو قبل الدخول وبكله لو بعده وقال شمس الأئمة ترجع به على الأب لا على الزوج وإذا لم يضمن الأب لا شك أن الصداق لا يسقط، وهل تقع البينونة؟ وإن قبلت الصغيرة وهي أهل للقبول وقع اتفاقاً، وإن لم تقبل إن كان المخالع أجنبياً ولم يضمن لا يقع اتفاقاً، وتكلموا أنه هل يتوقف على إجازتها إذا بلغت قيل لا يتوقف وإن كان العاقد أباً ولم يضمن للزوج قال بكر : اختلفت المشايخ في الوقوع وقال الإمام الحلواني : فيه روايتان . وفي حيل الأصل أنه لا يقع ما لم يضمن الأب الدرك له. وفي كشف الغوامض: إن الطلاق يقع بقبول الأب على قول محمد بن سلمة وإن لم يضمن البدل أي الصداق ولا يجب البدل على الأب ولا عليها وعنه أن الخلع واقع بقبول الأب والبدل عليه وإن لم يضمن وفي طلاق
.
قوله: (وليس بصحيح) قال الرملي : كلام الكمال لكنك نقصته فإنه عمم الكلام أولاً صحيح وقال فالخلع واقع سواء خلعها الأب على مهرها وضمنه أو ألف مثلاً فتجب الألف عليه. ثم ذكر هذا الحكم الذي سلمت أنه صحيح مطابق لما إذا ضمن المهر وهو راجع إليه وأنت أرجعته إلى الأخير من القسمين وحكمت عليه بأنه غير صحيح فأخطأت من وجهين أحدهما ما ذكرنا، والثاني أن اللائق بالأدب مع الشيخ أن يقال وهو مشكل أو لعله سبق قلم اه . شيخ الإسلام على المقدسي رحمه الله تعالى وفي النهر بعد سوق كلام البحر وأنى يفهم هذا مع قوله في الفتح «سواء خلعها الأب

الأصل في خلع الأب على صداقها قبل الدخول بها أن الخلع جائز ولها نصف الصداق ويضمن الأب للزوج نصف الصداق. قالوا : كيف صح الخلع على صداقها وهو ملكها ولا ولاية له في إبطال ملكها؟ وكيف يصح ضمان الصداق للزوج وهو عليه؟ ولأي معنى يضمن الأب نصف الصداق للزوج وقد ضمن الزوج ذلك لها ؟ أجابوا عن ذلك بأن الخلع أضيف إلى مهرها وذلك ملكها كان مضافاً إلى مالها والإضافة إلى مال الغير بأن خالع على عبد كإضافة الشراء إلى مال غيره، فلما إضافة الشراء فلأن . يصح الخلع وهو أقرب إلى الجواز أولى، لكن في باب الشراء يجب تسليم البدل على العاقد وفي الخلع لا يجب إلا بضمان لرجوع الحقوق إلى من يقع له العقد غير أنه إذا ضمن رجع إليه الحقوق بالضمان فإذا خلع وضمن صح وضمن البدل وقع الطلاق بقبوله ووجب نصف المهر وسقط النصف ويجب للزوج على الأب نصفه بضمانه تسليم كل المهر إلى الزوج، وإن كانت مدخولة فلها جميع المهر عليه والأب يضمن للزوج كله لأنه ضمن تسليم الكل فلم يقدر فيضمن مثله ا هـ .
ولا فرق في حكم ضمانه بين الصغيرة والكبيرة التي لم تأذن له ولكن إذا أجازته وقع وبرىء من الصداق واعتبر هذا الخلع معاوضة بين الزوج والمخالع وطلاقاً بلا بدل في حقها، فإذا بلغ الخبر إليها فأجازت نفذ عليها وبرىء الزوج، وإن لم تجز رجعت عليه بمهرها والزوج يرجع على الأب بحكم الضمان وتقدير هذا الخلع كان المخالع قال له إذا بلغها الخبر وأجازت كان البدل عليها، وإن لم تجزه فالبدل علي وما يجب على الأب من الضمان إنما يجب بالعقد لا بحكم الكفالة؛ كذا في البزازية : ولذا قال في فتح القدير : المراد بالضمان هنا التزام المال لأن اشتراط بدل الخلع على الأجنبي بخلاف بدل العتق لا يجوز اشتراطه على الأجنبي لأنه يحصل به للعبد ما لم يكن حاصلاً له وهو إثبات الأهلية وهو القوة عن الإسقاط بخلاف إسقاط الملك في الخلع لا يحصل عنه للمرأة ما لم يكن حاصلاً قبله فصار الأب والأجنبي مثلها فإنه لم يحصل له شيء بخلاف العبد فإنه حصل له ما ذكرنا، والعوض ذلك
على مهرها وضمنه أو ألف مثلاً فيجب الألف عليه ثم قال : ولا يسقط مهرها يعني فيما إذا وقع الخلع عليه كما هو ظاهر وبالجملة فأولى بالإنسان حفظ اللسان ا هـ قوله : (وقال شمس الأئمة ترجع به على الأب لا على الزوج قال في التتارخانية عقب هذا قال . رحمه الله : ومن مشايخنا من قال تأويل المسألة إذا خالعها على مال مثل صداقها أما إذا خالعها على الصداق لا يجوز أصلاً. قال رحمه الله : والأصح أن الخلع على صداقها وعلى مثل صداقها سواء قوله : (وقال الإمام الحلواني الخ) عبارة التتارخانية في هذا المحل وذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني فيه روايتين على رواية الشروط يقع الطلاق ولا يسقط صداقها. وعلى رواية الحيل لا يقع الطلاق. قال شمس الأئمة: ما ذكر في الشروط محمول على ما إذا ضمن الأب بدل الخلع توفيقاً بين رواية الشروط وبين رواية كتاب الحبل.
Regarding the female because if he divorces his minor son it is not valid, and the divorce of the minor does not depend on the guardian's permission. Its summary is that in the case of the minor girl, the money is not binding while divorce occurs, and in the case of the minor boy, there is no occurrence at all. His statement: (Even if it is for a thousand, on condition that he is a guarantor, she is divorced and the thousand is upon him, i.e., upon the father who has undertaken it, because stipulating the compensation of khul' upon a stranger is valid, so upon the father it is more appropriate. And her mahr is not forfeited because it is not under the father's guardianship. When she reaches puberty, she takes half the dowry if before consummation, and all of it if after, from the husband, and he (the husband) recovers from the father guarantor, or she recovers from the father and he does not recover from the husband. If the mahr was a specific item, she takes it all from the husband if after consummation, and half of it if before, and the husband recovers from the father guarantor its value. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. But this is not correct, because this ruling applies when he divorced her for her dowry on condition that he is guarantor for it. Then when she recovers it from the husband, the husband recovers it from the father due to his guarantee. The discussion here is only regarding when he divorced her for a thousand on condition that he is guarantor for her, and its ruling is that the thousand is binding upon him for the husband. And when she recovers her mahr from the husband, he (the husband) does not have recourse against her father because he did not guarantee the dowry for him, even though in Jami' al-Fusulayn in the issue of when her father divorces her for her mahr and guarantees it, she recovers from the father, not the husband. This is if he guaranteed her mahr to the husband; otherwise, there is no doubt that the mahr is not forfeited by this khul' due to her minority. The apparent is that she has a choice: if she wishes, she can recover from her husband or her father. In al-Bazzaziyya: If her father or a stranger performs khul' for her dowry, if the one performing khul' guarantees, it is complete and occurs regardless of who made the contract, and after puberty she takes half from the husband if before consummation, and all if after. Shams al-A'imma said: She recovers it from the father, not the husband. If the father does not guarantee, there is no doubt that the dowry is not forfeited. Does separation (baynuna) occur? If the minor girl accepts (and she is competent to accept), it occurs by agreement. If she does not accept, if the one performing khul' is a stranger and did not guarantee, it does not occur by agreement. They discussed whether it depends on her ratification when she reaches puberty. Some said it does not depend. If the contracting party is the father and he did not guarantee to the husband, Bakr said: The scholars differed on its occurrence. Imam al-Halwani said: There are two narrations. In Hiyal al-Asl, it does not occur unless the father guarantees recourse (darak) for him. In Kashf al-Ghawamid: Divorce occurs by the father's acceptance according to the statement of Muhammad ibn Salama, even if he does not guarantee the compensation (i.e., the dowry), and the compensation is not obligatory upon the father nor upon her. And from him (another narration) that the khul' occurs by the father's acceptance and the compensation is upon him even if he did not guarantee. And in Talaq...

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity and effects of a father performing khul' on behalf of his minor daughter. The author from al-Bahr al-Raiq comments on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The key issue is whether the father's action is valid, and what happens to the mahr and the compensation. The passage begins by distinguishing between a minor son and daughter: khul' of a minor son is void, but for a minor daughter, divorce occurs but the compensation is not binding on her unless the father guarantees it. The matn states that if the father performs khul' for a thousand dirhams as a guarantor, the divorce is effective and the thousand is owed by the father. The mahr is not forfeited because it is not under the father's authority; upon maturity, the daughter claims her mahr from the husband, and the husband recovers from the father. However, the author criticizes a statement in Fath al-Qadir, saying the ruling there applies when the khul' is for the dowry itself with guarantee, but here it is for a separate sum. The author then reconciles different views: Shams al-A'imma holds that she recovers from the father only, not the husband. A distinction is made between the father and a stranger: if a stranger performs khul' without guarantee, it is invalid; if the father does so, there is disagreement. Imam al-Halwani reports two narrations: one (from al-Shurut) that divorce occurs without forfeiting mahr, and another (from al-Hiyal) that divorce does not occur. The preferred view reconciles them by conditioning the father's guarantee. The passage also explains the rationale: khul' is like a sale (though not exactly), and guarantee is necessary to transfer liability. The relied-upon position is that the father's khul' is valid if he guarantees, and the daughter has a choice to claim mahr from either the father or husband. Additionally, if the daughter ratifies the khul' after maturity, it is binding and the father is discharged from liability.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce by redemption where the wife gives compensation to the husband to obtain release.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or undertaking by the father to pay the compensation if the daughter does not.
صداق (sadaq (mahr)): The dower or bridal gift that the husband owes the wife by the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon condition for a father's khul' for his minor daughter to be valid?
A) The daughter must be present and consent.
B) The father must guarantee the compensation.
C) The khul' must be for the exact amount of mahr.
D) The husband must agree.

Key Takeaway
The father's khul' for his minor daughter is valid if he guarantees compensation; the daughter retains her right to mahr.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
7 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Khul' Without Guarantee and Its Reconciliation
Details the different positions within the Hanafi school on the requirement of guarantee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two narrations reported by Imam al-Halwani regarding father's khul' without guarantee and explain how the relied-upon position reconciles them.

Core Idea
Imam al-Halwani reports two narrations on father's khul' without guarantee: one validates divorce without forfeiting mahr, the other invalidates; guarantee resolves the conflict.

This lesson delves into the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether a father's khul' for his minor daughter is valid when he does not guarantee the compensation. Key figures include Shams al-A'imma, Imam al-Halwani, and Muhammad ibn Salama. The preferred view conditions validity on guarantee, reconciling the conflicting reports from al-Shurut and al-Hiyal.

Guided Path
1
State the central issue
Whether the father's khul' for his minor daughter without guarantee is valid and whether divorce occurs.
2
Present the first narration (from al-Shurut)
Divorce occurs but mahr is not forfeited. The daughter recovers mahr from father, not husband (Shams al-A'imma's view).
This narration is transmitted by al-Halwani.
3
Present the second narration (from al-Hiyal)
Divorce does not occur unless father guarantees (darak). Supported by some early scholars.
This is from the book al-Hiyal.
4
Explain the reconciliation
The relied-upon position requires guarantee for validity. With guarantee, divorce occurs and compensation binds father. Without guarantee, divorce does not occur (preferred view).
This reconciles both narrations.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Courts may differ on validity without guarantee. The mufta bihi requires guarantee.

بالأنثى لأنه لو خلع ابنه الصغير لا يصح ولا يتوقف خلع الصغير على إجازة الولي ا هـ. و حاصله أنه في الصغيرة لا يلزم المال مع وقوع الطلاق وفي الصغير لا وقوع أصلاً. قوله : (ولو بألف على أنه ضامن طلقت والألف عليه أي على الأب الملتزم لأن اشتراط بدل الخلع على الأجنبي صحيح فعلى الأب أولى، ولا يسقط مهرها لأنه لم يدخل تحت ولاية الأب فإذا بلغت تأخذ نصف الصداق إن كان قبل الدخول وكله إن كان بعده من الزوج ويرجع هو على الأب الضامن أو ترجع على الأب ولا يرجع هو على الزوج، ولو كان المهر عيناً أخذته من الزوج كله إن كان بعد الدخول، ونصفه إن كان قبله ويرجع الزوج على الأب الضامن بقيمته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير وليس بصحيح لأن هذا حكم ما إذا خالعها على صداقها على أنه ضامن له فحينئذ إذا رجعت به على الزوج رجع الزوج به على الأب لضمانه، والكلام هنا إنما هو فيما إذا خالعها على الألف على أنه ضامن لها وحكمه لزوم الألف عليه للزوج، وإذا رجعت على الزوج بمهرها فلا رجوع له على أبيها لأنه لم يضمن له الصداق مع أن في جامع الفصولين في مسألة ما إذا خالعها أبوها على مهرها وضمنه أنها ترجع على الأب لا على الزوج، هذا لو ضمن مهرها للزوج وإلا فلا شك أن المهر لا يسقط بهذا الخلع لصغرها ا هـ. والظاهر أنها مخيرة إن شاءت رجعت على زوجها أو أبيها. وفي البزازية : خالعها أبوها أو كائناً أجنبي على صداقها إن ضمن المخالع تم ووقع من كان العاقد وبعد البلوغ آخذت الزوج بنصفه لو قبل الدخول وبكله لو بعده وقال شمس الأئمة ترجع به على الأب لا على الزوج وإذا لم يضمن الأب لا شك أن الصداق لا يسقط، وهل تقع البينونة؟ وإن قبلت الصغيرة وهي أهل للقبول وقع اتفاقاً، وإن لم تقبل إن كان المخالع أجنبياً ولم يضمن لا يقع اتفاقاً، وتكلموا أنه هل يتوقف على إجازتها إذا بلغت قيل لا يتوقف وإن كان العاقد أباً ولم يضمن للزوج قال بكر : اختلفت المشايخ في الوقوع وقال الإمام الحلواني : فيه روايتان . وفي حيل الأصل أنه لا يقع ما لم يضمن الأب الدرك له. وفي كشف الغوامض: إن الطلاق يقع بقبول الأب على قول محمد بن سلمة وإن لم يضمن البدل أي الصداق ولا يجب البدل على الأب ولا عليها وعنه أن الخلع واقع بقبول الأب والبدل عليه وإن لم يضمن وفي طلاق
.
قوله: (وليس بصحيح) قال الرملي : كلام الكمال لكنك نقصته فإنه عمم الكلام أولاً صحيح وقال فالخلع واقع سواء خلعها الأب على مهرها وضمنه أو ألف مثلاً فتجب الألف عليه. ثم ذكر هذا الحكم الذي سلمت أنه صحيح مطابق لما إذا ضمن المهر وهو راجع إليه وأنت أرجعته إلى الأخير من القسمين وحكمت عليه بأنه غير صحيح فأخطأت من وجهين أحدهما ما ذكرنا، والثاني أن اللائق بالأدب مع الشيخ أن يقال وهو مشكل أو لعله سبق قلم اه . شيخ الإسلام على المقدسي رحمه الله تعالى وفي النهر بعد سوق كلام البحر وأنى يفهم هذا مع قوله في الفتح «سواء خلعها الأب

الأصل في خلع الأب على صداقها قبل الدخول بها أن الخلع جائز ولها نصف الصداق ويضمن الأب للزوج نصف الصداق. قالوا : كيف صح الخلع على صداقها وهو ملكها ولا ولاية له في إبطال ملكها؟ وكيف يصح ضمان الصداق للزوج وهو عليه؟ ولأي معنى يضمن الأب نصف الصداق للزوج وقد ضمن الزوج ذلك لها ؟ أجابوا عن ذلك بأن الخلع أضيف إلى مهرها وذلك ملكها كان مضافاً إلى مالها والإضافة إلى مال الغير بأن خالع على عبد كإضافة الشراء إلى مال غيره، فلما إضافة الشراء فلأن . يصح الخلع وهو أقرب إلى الجواز أولى، لكن في باب الشراء يجب تسليم البدل على العاقد وفي الخلع لا يجب إلا بضمان لرجوع الحقوق إلى من يقع له العقد غير أنه إذا ضمن رجع إليه الحقوق بالضمان فإذا خلع وضمن صح وضمن البدل وقع الطلاق بقبوله ووجب نصف المهر وسقط النصف ويجب للزوج على الأب نصفه بضمانه تسليم كل المهر إلى الزوج، وإن كانت مدخولة فلها جميع المهر عليه والأب يضمن للزوج كله لأنه ضمن تسليم الكل فلم يقدر فيضمن مثله ا هـ .
ولا فرق في حكم ضمانه بين الصغيرة والكبيرة التي لم تأذن له ولكن إذا أجازته وقع وبرىء من الصداق واعتبر هذا الخلع معاوضة بين الزوج والمخالع وطلاقاً بلا بدل في حقها، فإذا بلغ الخبر إليها فأجازت نفذ عليها وبرىء الزوج، وإن لم تجز رجعت عليه بمهرها والزوج يرجع على الأب بحكم الضمان وتقدير هذا الخلع كان المخالع قال له إذا بلغها الخبر وأجازت كان البدل عليها، وإن لم تجزه فالبدل علي وما يجب على الأب من الضمان إنما يجب بالعقد لا بحكم الكفالة؛ كذا في البزازية : ولذا قال في فتح القدير : المراد بالضمان هنا التزام المال لأن اشتراط بدل الخلع على الأجنبي بخلاف بدل العتق لا يجوز اشتراطه على الأجنبي لأنه يحصل به للعبد ما لم يكن حاصلاً له وهو إثبات الأهلية وهو القوة عن الإسقاط بخلاف إسقاط الملك في الخلع لا يحصل عنه للمرأة ما لم يكن حاصلاً قبله فصار الأب والأجنبي مثلها فإنه لم يحصل له شيء بخلاف العبد فإنه حصل له ما ذكرنا، والعوض ذلك
على مهرها وضمنه أو ألف مثلاً فيجب الألف عليه ثم قال : ولا يسقط مهرها يعني فيما إذا وقع الخلع عليه كما هو ظاهر وبالجملة فأولى بالإنسان حفظ اللسان ا هـ قوله : (وقال شمس الأئمة ترجع به على الأب لا على الزوج قال في التتارخانية عقب هذا قال . رحمه الله : ومن مشايخنا من قال تأويل المسألة إذا خالعها على مال مثل صداقها أما إذا خالعها على الصداق لا يجوز أصلاً. قال رحمه الله : والأصح أن الخلع على صداقها وعلى مثل صداقها سواء قوله : (وقال الإمام الحلواني الخ) عبارة التتارخانية في هذا المحل وذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني فيه روايتين على رواية الشروط يقع الطلاق ولا يسقط صداقها. وعلى رواية الحيل لا يقع الطلاق. قال شمس الأئمة: ما ذكر في الشروط محمول على ما إذا ضمن الأب بدل الخلع توفيقاً بين رواية الشروط وبين رواية كتاب الحبل.
Regarding the female because if he divorces his minor son it is not valid, and the divorce of the minor does not depend on the guardian's permission. Its summary is that in the case of the minor girl, the money is not binding while divorce occurs, and in the case of the minor boy, there is no occurrence at all. His statement: (Even if it is for a thousand, on condition that he is a guarantor, she is divorced and the thousand is upon him, i.e., upon the father who has undertaken it, because stipulating the compensation of khul' upon a stranger is valid, so upon the father it is more appropriate. And her mahr is not forfeited because it is not under the father's guardianship. When she reaches puberty, she takes half the dowry if before consummation, and all of it if after, from the husband, and he (the husband) recovers from the father guarantor, or she recovers from the father and he does not recover from the husband. If the mahr was a specific item, she takes it all from the husband if after consummation, and half of it if before, and the husband recovers from the father guarantor its value. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. But this is not correct, because this ruling applies when he divorced her for her dowry on condition that he is guarantor for it. Then when she recovers it from the husband, the husband recovers it from the father due to his guarantee. The discussion here is only regarding when he divorced her for a thousand on condition that he is guarantor for her, and its ruling is that the thousand is binding upon him for the husband. And when she recovers her mahr from the husband, he (the husband) does not have recourse against her father because he did not guarantee the dowry for him, even though in Jami' al-Fusulayn in the issue of when her father divorces her for her mahr and guarantees it, she recovers from the father, not the husband. This is if he guaranteed her mahr to the husband; otherwise, there is no doubt that the mahr is not forfeited by this khul' due to her minority. The apparent is that she has a choice: if she wishes, she can recover from her husband or her father. In al-Bazzaziyya: If her father or a stranger performs khul' for her dowry, if the one performing khul' guarantees, it is complete and occurs regardless of who made the contract, and after puberty she takes half from the husband if before consummation, and all if after. Shams al-A'imma said: She recovers it from the father, not the husband. If the father does not guarantee, there is no doubt that the dowry is not forfeited. Does separation (baynuna) occur? If the minor girl accepts (and she is competent to accept), it occurs by agreement. If she does not accept, if the one performing khul' is a stranger and did not guarantee, it does not occur by agreement. They discussed whether it depends on her ratification when she reaches puberty. Some said it does not depend. If the contracting party is the father and he did not guarantee to the husband, Bakr said: The scholars differed on its occurrence. Imam al-Halwani said: There are two narrations. In Hiyal al-Asl, it does not occur unless the father guarantees recourse (darak) for him. In Kashf al-Ghawamid: Divorce occurs by the father's acceptance according to the statement of Muhammad ibn Salama, even if he does not guarantee the compensation (i.e., the dowry), and the compensation is not obligatory upon the father nor upon her. And from him (another narration) that the khul' occurs by the father's acceptance and the compensation is upon him even if he did not guarantee. And in Talaq...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity and effects of a father performing khul' on behalf of his minor daughter. The author from al-Bahr al-Raiq comments on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The key issue is whether the father's action is valid, and what happens to the mahr and the compensation. The passage begins by distinguishing between a minor son and daughter: khul' of a minor son is void, but for a minor daughter, divorce occurs but the compensation is not binding on her unless the father guarantees it. The matn states that if the father performs khul' for a thousand dirhams as a guarantor, the divorce is effective and the thousand is owed by the father. The mahr is not forfeited because it is not under the father's authority; upon maturity, the daughter claims her mahr from the husband, and the husband recovers from the father. However, the author criticizes a statement in Fath al-Qadir, saying the ruling there applies when the khul' is for the dowry itself with guarantee, but here it is for a separate sum. The author then reconciles different views: Shams al-A'imma holds that she recovers from the father only, not the husband. A distinction is made between the father and a stranger: if a stranger performs khul' without guarantee, it is invalid; if the father does so, there is disagreement. Imam al-Halwani reports two narrations: one (from al-Shurut) that divorce occurs without forfeiting mahr, and another (from al-Hiyal) that divorce does not occur. The preferred view reconciles them by conditioning the father's guarantee. The passage also explains the rationale: khul' is like a sale (though not exactly), and guarantee is necessary to transfer liability. The relied-upon position is that the father's khul' is valid if he guarantees, and the daughter has a choice to claim mahr from either the father or husband. Additionally, if the daughter ratifies the khul' after maturity, it is binding and the father is discharged from liability.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce by redemption where the wife gives compensation to the husband to obtain release.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or undertaking by the father to pay the compensation if the daughter does not.
صداق (sadaq (mahr)): The dower or bridal gift that the husband owes the wife by the marriage contract.
رواية (riwayah): Narration or transmission of a legal opinion within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position, what is the condition for a father's khul' for his minor daughter to be valid?
A) The daughter must accept.
B) The father must guarantee compensation.
C) The khul' must be witnessed.
D) The mahr must be specified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has conflicting narrations on father's khul' without guarantee; the relied-upon position requires guarantee for validity.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Father's Khul' and Guarantee of Mahr
Ruling with proof on father's khul' and guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a father performs khul' on his daughter's dowry, explain the role of the guarantee, and identify the correct position in the internal Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A father's khul' on his daughter's dowry is valid if he guarantees the substitute, analogous to a purchase on another's behalf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a central question: can a father validly perform khul' on his daughter's actual dowry? The author explains that with the father's guarantee (damān), the khul' is valid, drawing an analogy to purchase. We will examine the ruling, objections, and the internal dispute about whether khul' on the actual dowry differs from an equivalent amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Read the opening sentence: the father's khul' before consummation is permissible (jā'iz). The daughter gets half the dowry, and the father guarantees half to the husband.
2
Understand the objection
Critics ask: how can the father use her property without authority? And how can he guarantee the dowry when it is the husband's obligation?
3
See the Hanafi response with qiyas
The answer uses qiyas to purchase: adding a contract to another's property is valid. In purchase, the buyer must deliver the price; in khul', guarantee makes the father responsible.
The guarantee is an initial undertaking of property (iltizām al-māl), not suretyship (kafāla).
4
Distinguish the nature of guarantee
The passage clarifies that the guarantee is a direct obligation from the contract, not a surety. This is because khul' does not give the woman anything new (unlike manumission).
5
Resolve the internal Hanafi dispute
Imam al-Halwani reconciles two narrations: one where divorce occurs but dowry remains, another where divorce does not occur. The reconciliation: the first applies when the father guaranteed the substitute.
The correct view is that khul' on the actual dowry and on an equivalent amount are the same.

العتق لا يجوز اشتراطه على الأجنبي لأنه يحصل به للعبد ما لم يكن حاصلاً له وهو إثبات الأهلية وهو القوة عن الإسقاط بخلاف إسقاط الملك في الخلع لا يحصل عنه للمرأة ما لم يكن حاصلاً قبله فصار الأب والأجنبي بالإنسان حفظ اللسان ا هـ قوله : (وقال شمس الأئمة ترجع به على الأب لا على الزوج قال في التتارخانية عقب هذا قال . رحمه الله : ومن مشايخنا من قال تأويل المسألة إذا خالعها على مال مثل صداقها أما إذا على رواية الشروط يقع الطلاق ولا يسقط صداقها. وعلى رواية الحيل لا يقع الطلاق. قال شمس الأئمة: ما ذكر في الشروط محمول على ما إذا ضمن الأب بدل الخلع توفيقاً بين رواية الشروط وبين رواية كتاب الحبل. : وبهذا علم الفرق بين ما يصح التزامه وما لا يصح. ومن صور الالتزام أيضاً ما في جامع الفصولين لو زوج الأب بنته الكبيرة فطلبوا منه وقت الدخول أن يهب للزوج شيئاً من مهرها ينيغي أن يهب بإذنها وأن يضمن للزوج عنها فيقول إن أنكرت الإذن بالهبة وغرمتك ما وهبته فأنا ضامن ما وهبته، ويصح هذا الضمان لإضافته إلى سبب الوجوب لأن من زعم الأب والزوج أنها كاذبة في الإنكار وأن ما أخذته دين عليها للزوج فالأب ضمن بدين في المحيط أن المتعاقدين من يدخلان تحت حكم الإيجابين وإن كان المخاطب في الخلع المرأة فالمعتبر قبولها، سواء كان البدل مبهماً أو معيناً، أضاف البدل إلى نفسه أو لم يضفه، لأنها العاقدة، وإن كان المخاطب هو إلى المرأة، ولو قال على عبدي هذا وألفي هذه ففعل وقع الخلع لأنه هو العاقد لما أضاف المال إلى نفسه ولو قال لها الزوج خلعتك على دار فلان فالقبول إليها، ولو قال لصاحب العبد خلعت امرأتي بعبدك والمرأة حاضرة فالقبول لصاحب العبد، ولو قال رجل للزوج اخلعها على ألف فلان هذا أو على عبد فلان أو على ألف على أن فلاناً ضامن لها فالقبول لفلان ولو قالت اخلعني على ألف على أن فلاناً ضامن له ففعل وقع الخلع فإن ضمن فلان أخذ الزوج من أيهما شاء وإلا فمنها فقط ا هـ . وفي البزازية : الخلع إذا جرى بين الزوج والمرأة فإليها القبول كان البدل مرسلاً أو مطلقاً أو مضافاً إلى المرأة أو الأجنبي إضافة ملك أو ضمان، ومتى جرى بين الأجنبي والزوج فتى كان البدل مرسلاً فالقبول إليها، وإن أضيف إلى الأجنبي إضافة ملك أو ضمان فإلى الأجنبي لا إلى المرأة اهـ. وأما الوكيل به فقال في الخانية : وكيل المرأة بالخلع إذا قبل الخلع يتم الخلع وهل يطالب الوكيل ببدل الخلع فالمسألة على وجهين : إن كان الوكيل أرسل البدل إرسالاً بأن قال للزوج اخلع امرأتك بألف درهم أو على هذه الألف وأشار إلى ألف للمرأة كان البدل على المرأة ولا يطالب به الوكيل وإن أضاف الوكيل البدل إلى نفسه إضافة ملك أو ضمان بأن قال اخلع امرأتك على ألفي هذه أو على هذه الألف وأشار إلى نفسه أو قوله : (وإن كان المخاطب هو الأجنبي الظاهر أن يقال هو الزوج قوله: (وفي البزازية الخلع إذا جرى الخ) قال الرملي : المرسل كقولها اخلعني على هذا العبد أو على هذا الألف أو على هذه
The foundation regarding the father's khul' on her dowry before consummation is that the khul' is permissible and she gets half the dowry, and the father guarantees to the husband half the dowry. They said: How is the khul' valid on her dowry while it is her property and he has no authority to nullify her property? And how is the guarantee of the dowry to the husband valid while it is upon him? And for what meaning does the father guarantee half the dowry to the husband while the husband has guaranteed that to her? They answered that the khul' is added to her dower and that is her property, it was added to her property, and adding to the property of another, such as khul' on a slave, is like adding a purchase to the property of another. Since the addition of purchase... so the khul' is valid and it is closer to permissibility, but in the chapter of purchase, delivery of the substitute is obligatory on the contractor, while in khul' it is not obligatory except by guarantee because rights revert to the one for whom the contract is made. However, if he guarantees, rights revert to him by the guarantee. So if he performs khul' and guarantees, it is valid, and he guarantees the substitute, and divorce occurs by his acceptance, and half the dower becomes obligatory, and half is dropped, and the husband is owed by the father half of it because of his guarantee of delivering the entire dower to the husband. If she was consummated, then she gets all the dower from him, and the father guarantees the whole to the husband because he guaranteed delivery of the whole, so it is not possible for him to pay less; he guarantees its equivalent. There is no difference in the ruling of his guarantee between a minor and an adult who did not permit him, but if she permits it, it takes effect and he is free from the dowry, and this khul' is considered a exchange between the husband and the one performing khul', and a divorce without substitute in her right. So if the news reaches her and she permits, it is binding on her and the husband is free. If she does not permit, she sues him for her dower, and the husband has recourse to the father by virtue of the guarantee. The estimation of this khul' is that the one performing khul' said to him: if the news reaches her and she permits, then the substitute is on her; if she does not permit, then the substitute is on me. What is obligatory on the father of the guarantee is only obligatory by the contract, not by virtue of suretyship; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Hence it was said in Fath al-Qadir: the meaning of guarantee here is undertaking of the property, because stipulating the substitute of khul' on a stranger is unlike the substitute of manumission, which is not permissible to stipulate on a stranger because through it the slave obtains something he did not have, which is the establishment of legal capacity and the power of waiver. Unlike the removal of ownership in khul', the woman does not obtain something she did not have before, so the father and the stranger are like her, for he does not obtain anything. Unlike the slave, for he obtains what we mentioned. And the substitute is on her dower, and he guaranteed it, or one thousand dirhams, etc., so the one thousand is obligatory on him. Then he said: her dower does not fall, meaning in the case where the khul' occurs on it, as is apparent. In summary, the best for a person is to guard his tongue. His statement: (And Shams al-A'imma said: she returns against the father, not against the husband. In al-Tatarkhaniyya after this it said: He said, may Allah have mercy on him: Some of our teachers said the interpretation of the issue is if he performed khul' on property equal to her dower. But if he performed khul' on the dower itself, it is not valid at all. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: The most correct is that khul' on her dower and on equal to her dower are the same. His statement: (And Imam al-Halwani said...) The expression of al-Tatarkhaniyya in this place: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned two narrations regarding it: according to the narration of conditions, divorce occurs and her dower does not fall; according to the narration of legal stratagems, divorce does not occur. Shams al-A'imma said: What is mentioned in the conditions is interpreted as the case when the father guaranteed the substitute of khul', reconciling between the narration of conditions and the narration of the book of stratagems. And by this the difference is known between what can be validly undertaken and what cannot. From the forms of undertaking also what is in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if a father marries off his adult daughter, and they ask him at the time of consummation to give a gift to the husband from her dower, it is appropriate that he give it with her permission, and that he guarantee to the husband on her behalf, saying: if she denies permission for the gift and I compensate you for what I gave, then I am guarantor for what I gave. This guarantee is valid because it is connected to the cause of obligation, since the father and the husband claim she is lying in her denial and that what she took is a debt upon her to the husband, so the father guaranteed an obligatory debt, so it is valid. And it is apparent from the end of his speech that the guarantee here means suretyship, not initial undertaking of property, as is not hidden. And he indicated by his saying 'it is not binding on her' that the father is an unauthorized agent (fuduli) in khul' of a minor girl, so the permissibility of khul' by an unauthorized agent is derived from it. The summary, as in al-Muhit, is that the two contracting parties are those who enter under the rule of the two offers. Even if the addressee in khul' is the wife, her acceptance is considered, whether the substitute is ambiguous or specific, whether he adds the substitute to himself or not, because she is the contracting party. If the addressee is the outsider, if he adds the substitute to himself then his acceptance is considered because he undertook delivery of that. If he does not add it to himself nor to anyone, then her acceptance is considered because she is the principal in it. So if an outsider said to the husband: divorce your wife for this house and this thousand, then the acceptance is to the wife. If he said: for this slave of mine and this thousand of mine, then he did so, the khul' occurs because he is the contractor when he added the property to himself. If the husband said to her: I divorce you for the house of so-and-so, the acceptance is to her. If he said to the owner of the slave: I divorce my wife with your slave, and the wife is present, then the acceptance is to the owner of the slave. If a man said to the husband: divorce her for this thousand of so-and-so, or for the slave of so-and-so, or for a thousand with so-and-so as guarantor for it, then the acceptance is to so-and-so. If she said: divorce me for a thousand with so-and-so as guarantor for it, then he did so, the khul' occurs. If so-and-so guarantees, the husband takes from whichever he wishes; otherwise only from her. In al-Bazzaziyya: When khul' occurs between husband and wife, the acceptance is to her, whether the substitute is unrestricted, absolute, or added to the woman or to the outsider as an addition of ownership or guarantee. When it occurs between the outsider and the husband, if the substitute is unrestricted, the acceptance is to her; if it is added to the outsider as an addition of ownership or guarantee, then to the outsider, not to the woman. As for the agent: in al-Khaniyya: the wife's agent for khul', if he accepts the khul', the khul' is completed. Is the agent asked for the substitute of khul'? The issue has two aspects: if the agent sent the substitute as an unrestricted sending, such as saying to the husband: divorce your wife for one thousand dirhams or for this thousand, and he pointed to a thousand belonging to the woman, then the substitute is on the woman and the agent is not asked for it. If the agent added the substitute to himself as an addition of ownership or guarantee, such as saying: divorce your wife for this thousand of mine, or for this thousand, and he pointed to himself, or his statement: (And if the addressee is the outsider, it is apparent that it should be said: it is the husband. His statement: (In al-Bazzaziyya: when khul' occurs...) al-Ramli said: the unrestricted is like her saying: divorce me for this slave, or for this thousand, or for this
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of khul' when performed by the father on behalf of his daughter. The author states the basic rule: the father's khul' on his daughter's dowry before consummation is permissible; she receives half the dowry, and the father guarantees half the dowry to the husband. The passage then addresses objections raised against this ruling: how can the father validly perform khul' on property that belongs to his daughter? He has no authority to nullify her ownership. And how can he guarantee the dowry to the husband while it is actually the husband's obligation? The answer is that the khul' is added to her dower, which is her property. This addition to another's property is similar to adding a purchase to another's property—it is valid. In purchase, the substitute must be delivered by the contractor, but in khul' it is not obligatory without a guarantee. The father's guarantee makes him liable. If the father guarantees, he becomes responsible for delivering the substitute, and the khul' is valid. After khul', divorce occurs upon acceptance, half the dower is owed, and the father must pay that half to the husband. If the daughter was consummated, she gets the full dower and the father guarantees the full amount. The ruling applies equally whether the daughter is a minor or an adult who did not permit, but if she later permits, the khul' takes effect and the father is freed from liability. The passage then discusses the nature of the guarantee: it is a contractual undertaking, not a suretyship (kafala). It cites Fath al-Qadir explaining that the guarantee here is an initial undertaking of property (iltizam al-mal), not a surety, because stipulating the khul' substitute on a stranger is permissible, unlike the substitute for manumission. The reason is that manumission gives the slave something new (legal capacity), while khul' does not give the woman anything she didn't have; she merely loses her right to the dower. The passage then mentions an internal Hanafi dispute: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani reports two narrations—one where divorce occurs and her dower does not drop, and another where divorce does not occur. The author reconciles them by saying the first narration applies when the father guaranteed the substitute. The correct view is that khul' on the actual dower and on a similar amount are the same. The commentary then moves to the issue of acceptance (qabul) in khul'. When an outsider (ajnabi) is involved, the acceptance is directed to the party who added the substitute to themselves. If the outsider adds the property to himself, his acceptance is needed; otherwise, the wife's acceptance suffices. Detailed scenarios are given, such as when the outsider says 'divorce your wife for this house' (acceptance to wife) vs. 'for my slave' (acceptance to outsider). The passage also covers the case of an agent (wakil) and whether he is personally liable for the substitute. If the agent merely relays the offer without adding the substitute to himself, the substitute is on the woman. If he adds it to himself, he is liable. This commentary is based on earlier authoritative works like al-Bazzaziyya, al-Tatarkhaniyya, and Fath al-Qadir, and demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting narrations and extending rulings by analogy.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): A form of divorce initiated by the wife (or her guardian) in exchange for a compensation paid by the wife to the husband, often her dower or a part of it.
الضمان (al-damān): A guarantee or undertaking to deliver a substitute or compensate in case of non-delivery. In this context, it is an initial undertaking of property (iltizām al-māl) rather than suretyship (kafāla).
الصداق (al-sadāq): The dower or mahr that the husband gives to the wife as a marriage gift. In this passage, it is the property used as the substitute in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a father performs khul' on his minor daughter's dowry before consummation, what is the legal effect of the guarantee?
A) The father is a surety (kafīl) for the daughter's debt.
B) The father undertakes an initial obligation to pay the substitute, making the khul' valid.
C) The guarantee is void because the father has no authority over the daughter's property.
D) The guarantee only becomes effective if the daughter later ratifies the khul'.

Key Takeaway
The father's khul' on his daughter's dowry is valid because his guarantee transforms the transaction into a direct obligation, not a surety.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Acceptance in Khul' When an Outsider is Involved
Procedural rules on acceptance in khul' with outsider involvement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who must accept the khul' when an outsider offers the substitute, and apply the rule that acceptance belongs to the party who adds the substitute to himself.

Core Idea
In khul', if an outsider adds the substitute to himself, his acceptance is required; otherwise, the wife's acceptance suffices.

This passage continues the commentary on khul' by focusing on the rules of acceptance (qabūl). When an outsider (ajnabī) is involved, the Hanafi school has precise rules: the person who undertakes the substitute by adding it to himself must accept the khul'. We will examine scenarios including the outsider, the agent (wakīl), and the unauthorized agent (fuḍūlī).

Guided Path
1
Recall the default rule
In khul' between husband and wife, the wife's acceptance is the default, because she is the principal contracting party.
2
Identify the exception
When an outsider (ajnabi) addresses the husband directly and adds the substitute to himself (e.g., 'divorce her for my slave'), his acceptance is needed because he undertakes delivery.
3
Apply to various scenarios
The passage details scenarios: if the outsider says 'on this house' (pointing to wife's property), wife's acceptance; if 'on my slave', outsider's acceptance.
4
Understand the agent's liability
A wife's agent for khul' is not personally liable if he merely relays the offer without adding the substitute to himself. If he adds it to himself, he is liable.
5
Recognize the fuḍūlī principle
The father performing khul' on a minor without permission is like a fuḍūlī (unauthorized agent). The khul' is suspended (mawqūf) upon the daughter's ratification.

The foundation regarding the father's khul' on her dowry before consummation is that the khul' is permissible and she gets half the dowry, and the father guarantees to the husband half the dowry. They said: How is the khul' valid on her dowry while it is her property and he has no authority to nullify her property? And how is the guarantee of the dowry to the husband valid while it is upon him? And for what meaning does the father guarantee half the dowry to the husband while the husband has guaranteed that to her? They answered that the khul' is added to her dower and that is her property, it was added to her property, and adding to the property of another, such as khul' on a slave, is like adding a purchase to the property of another. Since the addition of purchase... so the khul' is valid and it is closer to permissibility, but in the chapter of purchase, delivery of the substitute is obligatory on the contractor, while in khul' it is not obligatory except by guarantee because rights revert to the one for whom the contract is made. However, if he guarantees, rights revert to him by the guarantee. So if he performs khul' and guarantees, it is valid, and he guarantees the substitute, and divorce occurs by his acceptance, and half the dower becomes obligatory, and half is dropped, and the husband is owed by the father half of it because of his guarantee of delivering the entire dower to the husband. If she was consummated, then she gets all the dower from him, and the father guarantees the whole to the husband because he guaranteed delivery of the whole, so it is not possible for him to pay less; he guarantees its equivalent. There is no difference in the ruling of his guarantee between a minor and an adult who did not permit him, but if she permits it, it takes effect and he is free from the dowry, and this khul' is considered a exchange between the husband and the one performing khul', and a divorce without substitute in her right. So if the news reaches her and she permits, it is binding on her and the husband is free. If she does not permit, she sues him for her dower, and the husband has recourse to the father by virtue of the guarantee. The estimation of this khul' is that the one performing khul' said to him: if the news reaches her and she permits, then the substitute is on her; if she does not permit, then the substitute is on me. What is obligatory on the father of the guarantee is only obligatory by the contract, not by virtue of suretyship; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. Hence it was said in Fath al-Qadir: the meaning of guarantee here is undertaking of the property, because stipulating the substitute of khul' on a stranger is unlike the substitute of manumission, which is not permissible to stipulate on a stranger because through it the slave obtains something he did not have, which is the establishment of legal capacity and the power of waiver. Unlike the removal of ownership in khul', the woman does not obtain something she did not have before, so the father and the stranger are like her, for he does not obtain anything. Unlike the slave, for he obtains what we mentioned. And the substitute is on her dower, and he guaranteed it, or one thousand dirhams, etc., so the one thousand is obligatory on him. Then he said: her dower does not fall, meaning in the case where the khul' occurs on it, as is apparent. In summary, the best for a person is to guard his tongue. His statement: (And Shams al-A'imma said: she returns against the father, not against the husband. In al-Tatarkhaniyya after this it said: He said, may Allah have mercy on him: Some of our teachers said the interpretation of the issue is if he performed khul' on property equal to her dower. But if he performed khul' on the dower itself, it is not valid at all. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: The most correct is that khul' on her dower and on equal to her dower are the same. His statement: (And Imam al-Halwani said...) The expression of al-Tatarkhaniyya in this place: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani mentioned two narrations regarding it: according to the narration of conditions, divorce occurs and her dower does not fall; according to the narration of legal stratagems, divorce does not occur. Shams al-A'imma said: What is mentioned in the conditions is interpreted as the case when the father guaranteed the substitute of khul', reconciling between the narration of conditions and the narration of the book of stratagems. And by this the difference is known between what can be validly undertaken and what cannot. From the forms of undertaking also what is in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if a father marries off his adult daughter, and they ask him at the time of consummation to give a gift to the husband from her dower, it is appropriate that he give it with her permission, and that he guarantee to the husband on her behalf, saying: if she denies permission for the gift and I compensate you for what I gave, then I am guarantor for what I gave. This guarantee is valid because it is connected to the cause of obligation, since the father and the husband claim she is lying in her denial and that what she took is a debt upon her to the husband, so the father guaranteed an obligatory debt, so it is valid. And it is apparent from the end of his speech that the guarantee here means suretyship, not initial undertaking of property, as is not hidden. And he indicated by his saying 'it is not binding on her' that the father is an unauthorized agent (fuduli) in khul' of a minor girl, so the permissibility of khul' by an unauthorized agent is derived from it. The summary, as in al-Muhit, is that the two contracting parties are those who enter under the rule of the two offers. Even if the addressee in khul' is the wife, her acceptance is considered, whether the substitute is ambiguous or specific, whether he adds the substitute to himself or not, because she is the contracting party. If the addressee is the outsider, if he adds the substitute to himself then his acceptance is considered because he undertook delivery of that. If he does not add it to himself nor to anyone, then her acceptance is considered because she is the principal in it. So if an outsider said to the husband: divorce your wife for this house and this thousand, then the acceptance is to the wife. If he said: for this slave of mine and this thousand of mine, then he did so, the khul' occurs because he is the contractor when he added the property to himself. If the husband said to her: I divorce you for the house of so-and-so, the acceptance is to her. If he said to the owner of the slave: I divorce my wife with your slave, and the wife is present, then the acceptance is to the owner of the slave. If a man said to the husband: divorce her for this thousand of so-and-so, or for the slave of so-and-so, or for a thousand with so-and-so as guarantor for it, then the acceptance is to so-and-so. If she said: divorce me for a thousand with so-and-so as guarantor for it, then he did so, the khul' occurs. If so-and-so guarantees, the husband takes from whichever he wishes; otherwise only from her. In al-Bazzaziyya: When khul' occurs between husband and wife, the acceptance is to her, whether the substitute is unrestricted, absolute, or added to the woman or to the outsider as an addition of ownership or guarantee. When it occurs between the outsider and the husband, if the substitute is unrestricted, the acceptance is to her; if it is added to the outsider as an addition of ownership or guarantee, then to the outsider, not to the woman. As for the agent: in al-Khaniyya: the wife's agent for khul', if he accepts the khul', the khul' is completed. Is the agent asked for the substitute of khul'? The issue has two aspects: if the agent sent the substitute as an unrestricted sending, such as saying to the husband: divorce your wife for one thousand dirhams or for this thousand, and he pointed to a thousand belonging to the woman, then the substitute is on the woman and the agent is not asked for it. If the agent added the substitute to himself as an addition of ownership or guarantee, such as saying: divorce your wife for this thousand of mine, or for this thousand, and he pointed to himself, or his statement: (And if the addressee is the outsider, it is apparent that it should be said: it is the husband. His statement: (In al-Bazzaziyya: when khul' occurs...) al-Ramli said: the unrestricted is like her saying: divorce me for this slave, or for this thousand, or for this
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of khul' when performed by the father on behalf of his daughter. The author states the basic rule: the father's khul' on his daughter's dowry before consummation is permissible; she receives half the dowry, and the father guarantees half the dowry to the husband. The passage then addresses objections raised against this ruling: how can the father validly perform khul' on property that belongs to his daughter? He has no authority to nullify her ownership. And how can he guarantee the dowry to the husband while it is actually the husband's obligation? The answer is that the khul' is added to her dower, which is her property. This addition to another's property is similar to adding a purchase to another's property—it is valid. In purchase, the substitute must be delivered by the contractor, but in khul' it is not obligatory without a guarantee. The father's guarantee makes him liable. If the father guarantees, he becomes responsible for delivering the substitute, and the khul' is valid. After khul', divorce occurs upon acceptance, half the dower is owed, and the father must pay that half to the husband. If the daughter was consummated, she gets the full dower and the father guarantees the full amount. The ruling applies equally whether the daughter is a minor or an adult who did not permit, but if she later permits, the khul' takes effect and the father is freed from liability. The passage then discusses the nature of the guarantee: it is a contractual undertaking, not a suretyship (kafala). It cites Fath al-Qadir explaining that the guarantee here is an initial undertaking of property (iltizam al-mal), not a surety, because stipulating the khul' substitute on a stranger is permissible, unlike the substitute for manumission. The reason is that manumission gives the slave something new (legal capacity), while khul' does not give the woman anything she didn't have; she merely loses her right to the dower. The passage then mentions an internal Hanafi dispute: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani reports two narrations—one where divorce occurs and her dower does not drop, and another where divorce does not occur. The author reconciles them by saying the first narration applies when the father guaranteed the substitute. The correct view is that khul' on the actual dower and on a similar amount are the same. The commentary then moves to the issue of acceptance (qabul) in khul'. When an outsider (ajnabi) is involved, the acceptance is directed to the party who added the substitute to themselves. If the outsider adds the property to himself, his acceptance is needed; otherwise, the wife's acceptance suffices. Detailed scenarios are given, such as when the outsider says 'divorce your wife for this house' (acceptance to wife) vs. 'for my slave' (acceptance to outsider). The passage also covers the case of an agent (wakil) and whether he is personally liable for the substitute. If the agent merely relays the offer without adding the substitute to himself, the substitute is on the woman. If he adds it to himself, he is liable. This commentary is based on earlier authoritative works like al-Bazzaziyya, al-Tatarkhaniyya, and Fath al-Qadir, and demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting narrations and extending rulings by analogy.

Key Terms
القبول (al-qabūl): The acceptance of the khul' offer by the contracting party. It is the second part of the contract after the offer (ījāb).
الأجنبي (al-ajnabī): An outsider, not the husband or wife, who may offer the substitute in khul'.
الوكيل (al-wakīl): An agent appointed by the wife to perform khul'.
الفضولي (al-fuḍūlī): An unauthorized agent who acts without prior permission; the contract is suspended until ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if an outsider says to the husband: 'Divorce your wife for my slave,' who must accept the khul'?
A) The wife, because she is the spouse.
B) The outsider, because he added the substitute to himself.
C) The husband, because he is being addressed.
D) No acceptance is needed because the offer is clear.

Key Takeaway
In khul', the acceptance belongs to the party who undertakes the substitute—if an outsider adds it to himself, he must accept; otherwise, the wife's acceptance suffices.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
