Who Accepts the Offer in Khul'? The General Principle
Ruling statement: rules of acceptance in khul' between wife, husband, and third party.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who has the right of acceptance in a khul' contract and apply the rule distinguishing when a third party becomes the acceptor.

Core Idea
The wife is the primary acceptor; a third party becomes acceptor only if he explicitly attaches the consideration to himself.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the key rule of acceptance in khul'. While the wife is always the natural party, a third party can step in if he takes responsibility for the compensation. Understanding who accepts determines the validity and obligations of the khul' contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracting parties
Determine who is involved: the wife, husband, a third party (ajnabi), or an agent.
The wife is always a party; the third party may become a direct party.
2
Apply the default rule
The text states that the wife's acceptance is considered unless someone else adds the consideration to himself.
This is the baseline: her acceptance is primary.
3
Classify the third party's role
If the third party says 'on my slave' or 'on my thousand', he attaches the consideration to himself and becomes the acceptor. If he does not attach, the wife's acceptance is needed.
The key is the phrase indicating ownership or guarantee by the third party.
4
Work through examples
Apply the rule to the scenarios: 'for this house and this thousand' (wife accepts), 'for my slave and my thousand' (third party accepts), 'for the slave of so-and-so' (third party not attached, wife accepts).
Each example reinforces the distinction.

Book of Divorce, Chapter of Khul'. ... It is not obligatory upon other than the one who receives the compensation, so it becomes like the price of a sale, except that a sale is invalidated by invalid conditions while khul' is not invalidated by them, end. And by this the difference is known between what is valid to undertake and what is not. Among forms of undertaking also is what is in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if a father marries off his adult daughter and they ask him at the time of consummation to give the husband something from her dowry, he should give with her permission and guarantee for her to the husband by saying, 'If she denies permission for the gift and I make you liable for what I gave, then I am guarantor of what I gave.' This guarantee is valid because it is attached to a cause of obligation, since the father and husband suppose she is lying in denial and what she took is a debt upon her to the husband, so the father guarantees an obligatory debt, so it is valid, end. The apparent from the end of his speech is that guarantee here means surety, not undertaking wealth initially as is not hidden. And he indicated by his saying 'it is not valid upon her' that the father is a volunteer (fuduli) in khul' of the minor girl, so it is understood from it the permissibility of khul' by a volunteer. Its summary as in al-Muhit is that the two contracting parties are those who fall under the ruling of the two offers; although the addressed in khul' is the woman, her acceptance is considered, whether the consideration is ambiguous or specified, whether he attached the consideration to himself or not, because she is the contracting party. And if the addressed is a third party and he attaches the consideration to himself, his acceptance is considered because he undertook to deliver that; if he did not attach it to himself nor to anyone, then her acceptance is considered because she is the original. So if a third party says to the husband 'Divorce your wife by khul' for this house and this thousand,' the acceptance is to the woman; if he says 'for my slave this and my thousand this,' and he does it, the khul' occurs because he is the contracting party since he attached the wealth to himself. If the husband says to her 'I divorce you by khul' for the house of so-and-so,' the acceptance is to her. If he says to the owner of the slave 'I divorced my wife by khul' with your slave' while the woman is present, the acceptance is to the owner of the slave. If a man says to the husband 'Divorce her by khul' for this thousand of so-and-so' or 'for the slave of so-and-so' or 'for a thousand on condition that so-and-so is guarantor for it,' the acceptance is to so-and-so. If she says 'Divorce me by khul' for a thousand on condition that so-and-so is guarantor for it,' and he does, the khul' occurs; if so-and-so guarantees, the husband may take from whichever he wishes; otherwise only from her, end. And if it occurs between the third party and the husband, if the consideration is unrestricted, the acceptance is to her; if it is attached to the third party by ownership or guarantee, then to the third party, not to the woman, end. As for the agent regarding it, he said in al-Khaniyyah: The agent of the woman for khul' if he accepts the khul', the khul' is complete. Is the agent demanded for the khul' consideration? If the agent attached the consideration to himself by ownership or guarantee by saying 'Divorce your wife by khul' for this thousand of mine' or 'for this thousand' pointing to himself, or his saying '(And if the addressed is the third party, the apparent is that it is the husband) his saying: (And in al-Bazzaziyyah: khul' if it occurs...)' said al-Ramli: unrestricted (mursal) is like her saying 'Divorce me by khul' for this slave' or 'for this thousand' or 'for this...' It is likening one's married wife to a permanently prohibited female, prohibiting intercourse and its preliminaries, by saying 'You are to me like the back of my mother' ... for a thousand on condition that I am the guarantor, the consideration is upon the agent and the woman is not demanded for it, and the agent may recourse against the woman before and after payment even if the woman did not order him to guarantee, unlike the agent of marriage on behalf of the husband if he guarantees the dowry for the woman and the guarantee was not by order of the principal, then he does not recourse against the principal, end. Neither of two agents acts alone in this unlike divorce. And the agent for divorce does not own khul' and divorce for wealth if she is consummated, on the correct view, because it leads to evil, unlike her otherwise because it leads to good. If a man claims he is her agent for khul' and he performs khul' with him for a thousand, then the woman denies agency, if the volunteer (fuduli) guarantees the wealth to the husband, the divorce occurs and the wealth is upon him; otherwise if the husband does not claim agency, it does not occur; if he claims it, it occurs but the wealth is not compelled; as in al-Muhit. If he authorizes him to perform khul' after a month and the period passes without the agent performing khul', the agent is not forced to perform khul' even if the woman requests, and the agent is not dismissed by the passing of the period. Imam Muhammad mentioned that authorization of a minor or insane person on behalf of an adult sane person for khul' is valid. One person does not suffice as agent from both sides, such as a woman authorizing a man for khul' and the husband also authorizes him, whether the consideration is named or not; and about it is valid? as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And Allah Almighty knows best what is correct.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe (sharh) on the rulings of khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation). It clarifies who has the right of acceptance when the khul' is conducted between different parties. The key principle is that the wife is the primary contracting party; her acceptance is needed unless a third party explicitly attaches the consideration to himself, in which case that party becomes the acceptor. The passage distinguishes between various scenarios: whether the consideration is specified or ambiguous, attached to the wife, to a third party, or to an agent. It also covers the guarantee (daman) and agency (wakalah) intricacies. The author cites sources like Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Muhit, al-Bazzaziyyah, and al-Khaniyyah. The overall ruling is that khul' is valid even if it involves invalid conditions, unlike a sale. This is a detailed legal discussion for advanced students.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife with compensation to the husband.
البدل (al-badal): The consideration (compensation) given by the wife or a third party for khul'.
الوكيل (al-wakil): Agent authorized by the wife or husband to execute khul'. Not directly covered in this lesson, but relevant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The ajnabi, because he spoke the offer.
B) The wife, because the money belongs to her.
C) The husband, because he is the one divorcing.

Key Takeaway
In khul', the wife's acceptance is primary unless a third party explicitly attaches the consideration to himself by ownership or guarantee, in which case that third party becomes the acceptor.

Agency in Khul': Liability and Special Cases
Ruling statement: agency rules in khul' including liability, recourse, joint agency, false agency, and authorization of minors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when an agent is liable for the khul' consideration, apply the rules of recourse, and handle special cases such as joint agency, false claims, and authorization of minors.

Core Idea
An agent's liability hinges on wording: attaching the consideration to himself makes him liable; otherwise, the wife bears it.

This section from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq focuses on the agent's role in khul'. The agent may become personally liable based on how he phrases the offer. It also covers important exceptions: two agents cannot act alone, a false claim of agency has specific consequences, and surprisingly, a minor or insane person can be authorized to perform khul' on behalf of an adult.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agent's wording
Determine if the agent sent the consideration unrestricted (mursal) or attached it to himself by ownership or guarantee.
Key phrases: 'for a thousand dirhams' (unrestricted) vs 'for my thousand' (attached).
2
Determine liability
If attached to the agent, he is liable for the consideration. If unrestricted, the wife is liable.
The agent's liability is primary; the wife is not demanded.
3
Apply the recourse rule
If the agent pays even without the wife's order, he can recover from her. This is different from a marriage agent's guarantee.
The text explicitly states the agent may recourse before and after payment, even if the woman did not order the guarantee.
4
Handle special cases
Two agents cannot act alone in khul' (unlike divorce). A false claimant of agency: if he guarantees the consideration, divorce occurs and he owes the money; otherwise, no effect. Authorization of a minor or insane person by an adult is valid per Imam Muhammad.
These are distinct rulings that must be memorized.

عبد فلان أو على ألف على أن فلاناً ضامن لها فالقبول لفلان ولو قالت اخلعني على ألف على أن فلاناً ضامن له ففعل وقع الخلع فإن ضمن فلان أخذ الزوج من أيهما شاء وإلا فمنها فقط ا هـ . وفي البزازية : الخلع إذا جرى بين الزوج والمرأة فإليها القبول كان البدل مرسلاً أو مطلقاً أو مضافاً إلى المرأة أو الأجنبي إضافة ملك أو ضمان، ومتى جرى بين الأجنبي والزوج فتى كان البدل مرسلاً فالقبول إليها، وإن أضيف إلى الأجنبي باب الظهار
١٥٧
هو تشبيه المنكوحة بمحرمة عليه على التأبيد حرم الوطء ودواعيه بأنت علي كظهر على ألف على أني ضامن كان البدل على الوكيل ولا تطالب به المرأة وللوكيل أن يرجع على المرأة قبل الأداء وبعده وإن لم تكن المرأة أمرته بالضمان بخلاف الوكيل بالنكاح من قبل الزوج إذا ضمن المهر للمرأة ولم يكن الضمان بأمر الموكل فإنه لا يرجع على الموكل اهـ. ولا ينفرد أحد الوكيلين به بخلاف الطلاق والوكيل بالطلاق لا يملك الخلع والطلاق على مال إن كانت مدخولة على الصحيح لأنه خلاف إلى شر بخلاف غيرها فإنه إلى خير. ولو زعم رجل أنه وكيلها بالخلع فخالعها معه على ألف ثم أنكرت المرأة التوكيل فإن ضمن الفضولي المال للزوج وقع الطلاق وعليه المال وإلا إن لم يدع الزوج التوكيل لم يقع، وإن ادعاه وقع ولا يجبر المال؛ كذا في المحيط. ولو وكله بأن يخالعها بعد شهر فمضت المدة ولم يخالعها الوكيل لا يجبر الوكيل على الخلع وإن طلبت المرأة وبمضي المدة لا ينعزل الوكيل. وذكر الإمام محمد أن توكيل الصبي والمعتوه عن البالغ العاقل بالخلع صحيح الواحد لا يصلح في الخلع وكيلاً من الجانبين بأن وكلت رجلاً بالخلع فوكله الزوج أيضاً، سواء كان البدل مسمى أو لا، وعن يصح؛ كذا في البزازية والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بالصواب.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Khul'. ... It is not obligatory upon other than the one who receives the compensation, so it becomes like the price of a sale, except that a sale is invalidated by invalid conditions while khul' is not invalidated by them, end. And by this the difference is known between what is valid to undertake and what is not. Among forms of undertaking also is what is in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if a father marries off his adult daughter and they ask him at the time of consummation to give the husband something from her dowry, he should give with her permission and guarantee for her to the husband by saying, 'If she denies permission for the gift and I make you liable for what I gave, then I am guarantor of what I gave.' This guarantee is valid because it is attached to a cause of obligation, since the father and husband suppose she is lying in denial and what she took is a debt upon her to the husband, so the father guarantees an obligatory debt, so it is valid, end. The apparent from the end of his speech is that guarantee here means surety, not undertaking wealth initially as is not hidden. And he indicated by his saying 'it is not valid upon her' that the father is a volunteer (fuduli) in khul' of the minor girl, so it is understood from it the permissibility of khul' by a volunteer. Its summary as in al-Muhit is that the two contracting parties are those who fall under the ruling of the two offers; although the addressed in khul' is the woman, her acceptance is considered, whether the consideration is ambiguous or specified, whether he attached the consideration to himself or not, because she is the contracting party. And if the addressed is a third party and he attaches the consideration to himself, his acceptance is considered because he undertook to deliver that; if he did not attach it to himself nor to anyone, then her acceptance is considered because she is the original. So if a third party says to the husband 'Divorce your wife by khul' for this house and this thousand,' the acceptance is to the woman; if he says 'for my slave this and my thousand this,' and he does it, the khul' occurs because he is the contracting party since he attached the wealth to himself. If the husband says to her 'I divorce you by khul' for the house of so-and-so,' the acceptance is to her. If he says to the owner of the slave 'I divorced my wife by khul' with your slave' while the woman is present, the acceptance is to the owner of the slave. If a man says to the husband 'Divorce her by khul' for this thousand of so-and-so' or 'for the slave of so-and-so' or 'for a thousand on condition that so-and-so is guarantor for it,' the acceptance is to so-and-so. If she says 'Divorce me by khul' for a thousand on condition that so-and-so is guarantor for it,' and he does, the khul' occurs; if so-and-so guarantees, the husband may take from whichever he wishes; otherwise only from her, end. In al-Bazzaziyyah: Khul' if it occurs between the husband and the woman, the acceptance is to her, whether the consideration is unrestricted (mursal) or absolute (mutlaq) or attached to the woman or a third party by ownership or guarantee. And if it occurs between the third party and the husband, if the consideration is unrestricted, the acceptance is to her; if it is attached to the third party by ownership or guarantee, then to the third party, not to the woman, end. As for the agent regarding it, he said in al-Khaniyyah: The agent of the woman for khul' if he accepts the khul', the khul' is complete. Is the agent demanded for the khul' consideration? The issue has two aspects: if the agent sent the consideration unrestricted by saying to the husband 'Divorce your wife by khul' for a thousand dirhams' or 'for this thousand' pointing to the woman's thousand, the consideration is upon the woman and the agent is not demanded for it. If the agent attached the consideration to himself by ownership or guarantee by saying 'Divorce your wife by khul' for this thousand of mine' or 'for this thousand' pointing to himself, or his saying '(And if the addressed is the third party, the apparent is that it is the husband) his saying: (And in al-Bazzaziyyah: khul' if it occurs...)' said al-Ramli: unrestricted (mursal) is like her saying 'Divorce me by khul' for this slave' or 'for this thousand' or 'for this...' [on page 157] Book of Divorce, Chapter of Zihar. Chapter of Zihar. 157. It is likening one's married wife to a permanently prohibited female, prohibiting intercourse and its preliminaries, by saying 'You are to me like the back of my mother' ... for a thousand on condition that I am the guarantor, the consideration is upon the agent and the woman is not demanded for it, and the agent may recourse against the woman before and after payment even if the woman did not order him to guarantee, unlike the agent of marriage on behalf of the husband if he guarantees the dowry for the woman and the guarantee was not by order of the principal, then he does not recourse against the principal, end. Neither of two agents acts alone in this unlike divorce. And the agent for divorce does not own khul' and divorce for wealth if she is consummated, on the correct view, because it leads to evil, unlike her otherwise because it leads to good. If a man claims he is her agent for khul' and he performs khul' with him for a thousand, then the woman denies agency, if the volunteer (fuduli) guarantees the wealth to the husband, the divorce occurs and the wealth is upon him; otherwise if the husband does not claim agency, it does not occur; if he claims it, it occurs but the wealth is not compelled; as in al-Muhit. If he authorizes him to perform khul' after a month and the period passes without the agent performing khul', the agent is not forced to perform khul' even if the woman requests, and the agent is not dismissed by the passing of the period. Imam Muhammad mentioned that authorization of a minor or insane person on behalf of an adult sane person for khul' is valid. One person does not suffice as agent from both sides, such as a woman authorizing a man for khul' and the husband also authorizes him, whether the consideration is named or not; and about it is valid? as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And Allah Almighty knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe (sharh) on the rulings of khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation). It clarifies who has the right of acceptance when the khul' is conducted between different parties. The key principle is that the wife is the primary contracting party; her acceptance is needed unless a third party explicitly attaches the consideration to himself, in which case that party becomes the acceptor. The passage distinguishes between various scenarios: whether the consideration is specified or ambiguous, attached to the wife, to a third party, or to an agent. It also covers the guarantee (daman) and agency (wakalah) intricacies. The author cites sources like Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Muhit, al-Bazzaziyyah, and al-Khaniyyah. The overall ruling is that khul' is valid even if it involves invalid conditions, unlike a sale. This is a detailed legal discussion for advanced students.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): Agent authorized by the wife or husband to execute khul'.
الإرسال (al-irsal): Sending the consideration unrestricted, without attaching it to oneself or another.
الإضافة (al-idafah): Attaching the consideration to oneself (by ownership or guarantee).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An agent says to the husband: 'Divorce your wife by khul' for a thousand dirhams on condition that I am the guarantor.' The husband does so. Who is liable for the thousand?
A) The agent, because he attached the consideration by guarantee.
B) The wife, because she is the principal.
C) The husband, because he accepted.
D) The agent and wife jointly.

Key Takeaway
An agent's liability in khul' is determined by his wording: attaching the consideration to himself makes him both acceptor and debtor, with recourse rights against the wife.

The Legal Definition of Zihar and Its Essential Conditions
Defining the legal reality of zihar and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define zihar according to the Hanafi school and identify its essential conditions.

Core Idea
Zihar is likening one's wife to a permanently prohibited relative, making marital relations unlawful until expiation.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice that the Qur'an prohibited, but the law gave it a specific mechanism. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq dissects the Hanafi definition of zihar, clarifying what constitutes it and what does not. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying the rules of expiation and marital rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core elements of zihar
The passage defines zihar as a husband likening his wife (or a part representing her) to a permanently prohibited relative. Note the two key components: the wife (al-mushabbah) and the relative (al-mushabbah bih).
The comparison can be explicit or implicit.
2
Understand the condition of permanence (taʾbīd)
The likened-to relative must be permanently prohibited. This means the prohibition cannot be removed by any change in circumstances (e.g., a sister of the wife is only temporarily prohibited while the wife is in marriage).
Contrast with Magian woman: though Islamically prohibited, her prohibition is not permanent because she can accept Islam.
3
Recognize the scope of the husband
The husband must be Muslim (excluding dhimmi), but he may be intoxicated, coerced, or mute (using gestures). The wife is unrestricted: she can be any wife (entered upon or not, adult or minor, sane or insane, Muslim or Kitabiyyah).
This shows the law's concern for the act's effect on the marital bond, not the husband's capacity.
4
Distinguish explicit and implicit zihar
Zihar can be explicit (saying 'you are like my mother's back') or implicit, such as telling another woman 'you are like my wife' after having pronounced zihar on the first wife, because it implies the forbidden comparison.
Implicit zihar only works if the context (e.g., previous zihar) makes the intention clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التأييد) أراد بالمنكوحة ما يصح إضافة الطلاق إليه من الزوجة وهو أن يشبهها أو عضواً منها يعبر به عنها أو جزءاً شائعاً منها لما سيأتي. وأراد بالمشبه به عضواً يحرم إليه النظر من عضو محرمة عليه على التأبيد لما سنذكره أيضاً. وأراد بالزوج المسلم لأظهار للذمي عندنا. وأطلقه فشمل السكران والمكره والأخرس بإشارته كما في التتارخانية وقيد بالمنكوحة احترازاً عن الأمة والأجنبية على ما سيصرح به، ولم يقيدها بشيء ليشمل المدخولة وغيرها الكبيرة والصغيرة الرتقاء وغيرها العاقلة والمجنونة المسلمة والكتابية وقيد بالتأبيد لأنه لو شبهها بأخت امرأته لا يكون مظاهراً لأن حرمتها موقتة بكون امرأته في عصمته وكذا المطلقة ثلاثاً. وأطلق الحرمة فشمل الحرمة نسباً وصهرية ورضاعاً، وأراد بالتأبيد تأبيد الحرمة باعتبار وصف لا يمكن زواله لا باعتبار وصف يمكن زواله فإن المجوسية محرمة على التأبيد، ولو قال كظهر مجوسية لا يكون ظهاراً - ذكره في جوامع الفقه - لأن التأبيد باعتبار دوام الوصف وهو غير لازم لجواز إسلامها بخلاف الأمية والأختية وغيرهما كذا في فتح القدير. والتحقيق أن حرمة المجوسية ليست بمؤبدة بل هي موقتة بإسلامها أو بصيرورتها كتابية فلا حاجة إلى ما ذكره كما لا يخفى ولذا علل في المحيط بأنها ليست بمحرمة على التأييد وضم إلى المجوسية المرتدة. وشمل كلامه التشبيه الصريح والضمني فدخل ما لو ظاهر من امرأته ثم قال للأخرى أنت علي مثل هذه ينوي الظاهر فإنه يكون مظاهراً ولو بعد موتها وبعد التكفير باعتبار تضمن قوله لها أنت علي كظهر أمي فالتشبيه فيها باعتبار خصوص وجه الشبه المراد لا باعتبار نفس التشبيه بها، وكذا لو كانت امرأة رجل آخر ظاهر زوجها منها فقال أنت علي مثل فلانة ينوي ولو كان بعد موتها وكذا لو ظاهر من امرأته ثم قال لأخرى أشركتك في صح ذلك [؟] ظهارها . فالحاصل أن حقيقة الظهار الشرعي تشبيه الزوجة أو جزء شائع منها أو ما يعبر به عن الكل بما لا يحل النظر إليه من المحرمة على التأبيد كذا قالوا
He intended by 'the wife' what is valid for adding divorce to from the wife, which is that he likens her or a limb of her that expresses her, or a common part of her, as will come. And he intended by 'the likened-to' a limb whose sight is prohibited from a permanently prohibited relative, as we will also mention. And he intended by 'the Muslim husband' to exclude the dhimmi according to us. And he made it absolute, so it includes the intoxicated, the coerced, and the mute by his gesture as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And he restricted it to 'the wife' as a precaution against the slave-woman and the ajnabiyyah, as will be stated. And he did not restrict it to anything else to include the entered-upon and others, the adult and young, the prepubescent and others, the sane and insane, the Muslim and the Kitabiyyah. And he restricted by 'permanently' because if he likens her to his wife's sister, he is not a mazahir because her prohibition is temporary due to his wife being in his bond, and likewise the threefold divorcee. And he made 'prohibition' absolute, so it includes prohibition by lineage, affinity, and fosterage. And he intended by 'permanently' the permanence of prohibition by virtue of an attribute that cannot be removed, not by virtue of an attribute that can be removed. For the Magian woman is permanently prohibited, and if he says 'like the back of a Magian woman,' it is not zihar — as mentioned in Jami' al-Fiqh — because the permanence is based on the continuity of the attribute, which is not necessary due to possibility of her Islam, contrary to the mother, sister, and others, as in Fath al-Qadir. And the verification is that the prohibition of the Magian woman is not permanent; rather it is temporary until her Islam or her becoming a Kitabiyyah, so there is no need for what he mentioned, as is not hidden. For this reason, it is stated in al-Muhit that she is not permanently prohibited, and the apostate is added to the Magian. And his speech includes explicit and implicit likening, so it includes if he pronounces zihar from his wife then says to another 'you are to me like this one' intending zihar, then he is a mazahir, even after her death and after expiation, because his statement to her 'you are to me like the back of my mother' is implied. So the likening is by virtue of the specific aspect of likeness intended, not the likening itself. And likewise if there is a woman of another man whose husband pronounced zihar from her, and he says 'you are to me like so-and-so' intending, even after her death. And likewise if he pronounced zihar from his wife then said to another 'I have shared with you in the validity of that zihar'[?]. So the conclusion is that the legal reality of zihar is the husband's likening of his wife or a common part of her or what expresses the whole to what is not permissible to look at from a permanently prohibited relative, as they said.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling that establishes the legal reality of zihar. It begins by specifying the wife (al-mankūḥah) as the object of comparison: she must be a woman to whom divorce can be validly added. The comparison can be to her entire body, a limb that represents her, or a common part of her. The subject of comparison (al-mushabbah bih) must be a permanently prohibited relative (muḥarramah ʿalā al-taʾbīd), specifically a member whose sight is forbidden. The husband must be Muslim; a dhimmi is excluded according to the Hanafi school. The ruling applies to intoxicated, coerced, and mute persons (the latter by gesture). The wife is unrestricted by age, sanity, religion (Muslim or Kitābiyyah), or whether the marriage has been consummated. The condition of permanence (taʾbīd) is crucial: if the comparison is to a temporarily prohibited relative (like a sister of the wife or a threefold divorcee), it is not zihar. The prohibition includes all types: lineage, affinity, and fosterage. The author then refines the concept of permanence: it must be based on an attribute that cannot be removed. For example, a Magian woman is considered permanently prohibited only if the attribute of being Magian is deemed permanent, but since she can convert to Islam or become Kitābiyyah, comparing one's wife to a Magian woman does not constitute zihar. The passage also covers implicit zihar, such as saying to another woman 'you are like my wife' after pronouncing zihar on the first wife, which is valid because it implies the forbidden likening. The conclusion summarizes that zihar is likening the wife or a part of her to a permanently prohibited relative.

Key Terms
الظهار (al-ẓihār): The husband's likening of his wife to a permanently prohibited relative, which makes it unlawful for him to have intercourse with her until he performs expiation.
التأبيد (al-taʾbīd): Permanence of prohibition based on an attribute that cannot be removed, such as being a mother or sister by lineage.
المشبه به (al-mushabbah bih): The relative to whom the wife is compared; must be a permanently prohibited woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the likened-to relative (al-mushabbah bih) in zihar according to the Hanafi school?
A) She must be a living relative.
B) She must be a permanently prohibited relative by lineage, fosterage, or affinity.
C) She must be a Muslim relative.
D) She must be a relative with whom marriage is temporarily prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Zihar is established only when a husband compares his wife to a permanently prohibited relative; if the prohibition can be removed, it is not zihar.

The Likened-To Must Be a Woman: Condition for Zihar
Condition that the comparison must be to a woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that the likened-to in zihar must be a woman and evaluate the argument against comparisons to male body parts.

Core Idea
Zihar requires the likened-to to be a woman — comparing to a man does not activate the ruling.

In zihar, the husband likens his wife to a forbidden woman. But what if he compares her to a man's body part? The Hanafi school clarifies a crucial condition: the likened-to must be from the genus of women. This lesson explores the reasoning and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and condition
State the Hanafi ruling: if a husband says 'you are to me like the back of my father or my son,' it is not zihar because the likened-to must be a woman.
2
Examine the dalil
The proof is the custom of the Law (urf al-shar'): zihar was only transmitted with a woman as the likened-to.
This is a dalil naqli based on normative practice.
3
Analyze the opposing view
Some scholars, as in al-Muhit, analogize that a male private part is like a mother's in permanent prohibition, so it should be zihar.
But this analogy is rejected because it misses the condition of femininity.
4
Determine the tarjih
The Hanafi position (al-Bada'i') is relied upon; the opinion in al-Muhit is not adopted. The practical consequence: no expiation for the husband.
This is the mufta bihi.

Source Text

ولو قالوا من محرم دون محرمة صفة لشخص المتناول للذكر والأنثى لكان أولى لأنه لو قال أنت علي كفرج أبي أو قريبي كان يوجب فظاهر منها قبل عرض الإسلام عليها صح لكونه من أهل الكفارة قوله: (والتحقيق أن حرمة المجوسية الخ) قال في النهر : وعندي أن التحقيق ما في فتح القدير ألا ترى قولهم أن اللعان حرمة مؤبدة ولو شبهها بامرأته الملاعنة لا يصير مظاهراً كما في الجوامع أيضاً لأن هذا الوصف يمكن زواله بأن يكذب نفسه كما سيأتي قوله : (ولو قالوا من محرم الخ) قال في النهر قال في البدائع : من شرائط الظهار التي ترجع على المظاهر به أن يكون من جنس النساء حتى لو قال لها أنت علي كظهر أبي أو ابني لا يصح الظهار لأنه عرف بالشرع والشرع إنما هو ورد بها فيما إذا كان المظاهر به امرأة ا ا هـ. وبه عرف جواب ما في المحيط : لو شبهها بفرج أبيه وقريبه ينبغي أن يكون مظاهراً إذ فرجهما في الحرمة كفرج أمه ; كذا في المحيط. وينبغي عدم التقييد بالأب والقريب لأن فرج الرجل الأجنبي محرم على التأبيد أيضا. وأشار بقوله «بمحرمة» إلى أن المشبه الرجل لأنه لو كان المرأة بأن قالت أنت علي كظهر أمي أو أنا عليك كظهر أمك فالصحيح كما في المحيط أنه ليس بشيء فلا حرمة ولا كفارة ومنهم من أوجب عليها الكفارة. ثم اختلفوا هل هي كفارة يمين أو ظهار؟ ورجح ابن الشحنة أنها كفارة يمين، وذكر ابن وهبان تفريعاً على القول بوجوب الكفارة أنها تجب بالحنث إن كانت كفارة يمين وإن كانت كفارة ظهار فإن كان تعليقاً يجب متى تزوجت به، وإن كانت في نكاحه تجب للحال ما لم يطلقها لأنه لا يحل لها العزم على منعه من الجماع .اهـ.
And if they said 'from a mahram' without specifying female, as a description of a person covering male and female, it would be better, because if he says 'you are to me like the private part of my father or my relative' it would obligate zihar, then he pronounces zihar from her before presenting Islam to her, it is valid because he is among the people of expiation. His saying: 'and the verification that the prohibition of the Magian woman...' He said in al-Nahr: In my view, the verification is what is in Fath al-Qadir; do you not see their saying that li'an is a permanent prohibition, yet if he likens her to his wife who is the subject of li'an, he does not become a mazahir, as in al-Jawami' also, because this attribute can be removed by his retraction, as will come. His saying: 'and if they said from a mahram...' He said in al-Nahr: Al-Bada'i said: among the conditions of zihar that relate to the person likened to is that he be of the genus of women, so that if he says to her 'you are to me like the back of my father or my son,' zihar is not valid because it is known by the Law, and the Law only came with it when the likened-to is a woman. end quote. And by this is known the answer to what is in al-Muhit: if he likens her to the private part of his father or relative, it should be that he is a mazahir, since their private part in prohibition is like that of his mother; as in al-Muhit. And one should not restrict to father and relative, because the private part of an ajnabi male is also permanently prohibited. And he indicated by his saying 'by a female mahram' that the likener is the man, because if it were the woman, she saying 'you are to me like the back of my mother' or 'I am to you like the back of your mother,' the correct position as in al-Muhit is that it is nothing, so no prohibition and no expiation, and among them are those who obligated expiation on her. Then they differed: is it the expiation of an oath or of zihar? And Ibn al-Shihnah favored that it is the expiation of an oath. And Ibn Wahban mentioned, based on the opinion that expiation is obligatory, that it becomes obligatory upon breaking the oath if it is the expiation of an oath, and if it is the expiation of zihar, then if it is a conditional statement, it becomes obligatory whenever she marries him, and if it is in his nikah, it becomes immediately obligatory as long as he does not divorce her, because it is not permissible for her to resolve to prevent him from intercourse. End quote.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the condition that the likened-to relative in zihar must be a woman. The author first discusses the wording of the definition: if the text had said 'from a mahram' without specifying female, it would include male, which would be problematic. He brings the ruling from al-Bada'i' that the likened-to must be of the genus of women, based on the custom (urf) of the Law. If a husband compares his wife to a man's private part (e.g., father's or relative's), according to al-Muhit it might be considered zihar because the prohibition is similar to that of the mother's private part, but the author notes that this is not restricted; any male's private part is permanently prohibited. However, the relied-upon position is that it is not zihar because the person likened to is not a woman. The passage then addresses the case of a woman pronouncing zihar on her husband. The correct view is that it is invalid and no expiation is required, though some scholars hold that she must give expiation. There is further dispute on whether that expiation is for an oath or for zihar. The preferred view (Ibn al-Shihnah) is that it is the expiation of an oath. The discussion also includes contingencies for conditional and immediate cases.

Key Terms
المشبه به من جنس النساء (al-mushabbah bih min jins al-nisāʾ): The person or thing to which the wife is likened must be a woman; comparing to a man does not count.
كفارة اليمين (kaffārat al-yamīn): The expiation for breaking an oath, which is feeding or clothing ten poor people, or fasting three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'You are to me like my father's private part.' According to the Hanafi school, this is:
A) Zihar, requiring expiation.
B) Not zihar.
C) A valid divorce.
D) Li'an.

Key Takeaway
The likened-to in zihar must be a woman; comparing to a male does not constitute zihar.

The Case of a Woman Pronouncing Zihar
Ruling on woman's zihar and expiation type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a woman pronounces zihar on her husband and explain whether expiation is required and of what type.

Core Idea
A woman's zihar is invalid — no prohibition or expiation in the correct view, but some require the expiation of an oath.

What happens if a wife says to her husband 'you are to me like my mother's back'? Can a woman pronounce zihar? The Hanafi school holds that such a statement has no effect. This lesson examines the dispute and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A woman says to her husband a statement that would be zihar if said by a man to a woman.
2
State the correct view
The correct position (as in al-Muhit) is that it is nothing — no prohibition and no expiation.
3
Note the opposing view
Some scholars obligated expiation on the woman, but they differed on the type: oath expiation or zihar expiation.
4
Follow the tarjih
Ibn al-Shihnah favored that it is the expiation of an oath (kaffarat yamin).
5
Apply the contingencies
If it is oath expiation, it becomes due upon breaking the implied oath. If zihar expiation, then whether conditional or immediate, different timings apply.
Ibn Wahban's detail.

Intra-Hanafi Disputes on Specific Comparisons in Zihar
Intra-Hanafi disputes on zihar comparisons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zihar when comparing a wife to a woman with whom a relative has committed zina, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Comparing one's wife to a woman from zina is zihar per Abu Yusuf (mufta bihi), not per Muhammad.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses three specific scenarios within the Hanafi school where there is disagreement on whether a comparison constitutes zihar. The first scenario involves comparing the wife to a woman with whom the husband's father or son has committed zina. The second scenario involves comparing the wife to the mother or daughter of a woman with whom the husband himself has committed zina. The third scenario involves prior kissing of an ajnabiyyah before comparing the wife to her daughter. The passage also critiques a statement in al-Dirayah, calling it a slip of the pen. We will explore the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and identify the mufta bihi (operative) ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify what act is being discussed (the husband's comparison of his wife to another woman) and what the ruling hinges on (whether the compared-to woman is a permanent mahram).
The default rule: zihar is triggered only when the wife is likened to a woman who is permanently prohibited in marriage.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
For the first scenario (mazniyyah of father/son), note that Muhammad says it is not zihar because the woman is not a permanent mahram, while Abu Yusuf says it is zihar. The text says Abu Yusuf's view is correct.
The dispute hinges on whether the prohibition from zina is considered permanent.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the mufta bihi view (Abu Yusuf), the husband becomes a mazahir and must perform expiation; according to Muhammad, no expiation is required.
This affects whether the husband must perform kaffarah before resuming marital relations.
4
Recognize the correction of al-Dirayah
The passage points out an error in al-Dirayah where it stated that comparing to the mother of a woman with whom the father/son committed zina is zihar. The author explains this is a slip of the pen, and the correct ruling follows the earlier positions.
The correction shows the importance of textual accuracy in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية: ولو شبهها بمزنية الأب أو الابن قال محمد: لا يكون ظهاراً. وقال أبو يوسف يكون ظهاراً. وهو الصحيح. ولو شبهها بأم امرأة أو ابنة امرأة قد زنى بها يكون ظهاراً .اهـ. ولو قبل أجنبية بشهوة ثم شبه زوجته بابنتها لم يكن مظاهراً عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف؛ كذا في الولوالجية. فلذا زاد في النهاية لفظة اتفاقاً في التعريف وتبعه الشارح وغيره. وما في الدراية أنه لو شبهها بأم امرأة زنى بها أبوه أو ابنه كان مظاهراً مشكل لأن غايته أن تكون كأم زوجة أبيه أو حلال؛ كذا في فتح القدير والظاهر أنه سبق قلم وقد ظهر لي أنه لا حاجة إلى قيد ابْنِه وهي صححه فرجها في الحرمة كفرج أمه واندفع ما في البحر حيث نقل ما في المحيط وجزم به ولم ينقله بحثاً وأنت قد علمت ما هو الواقع
And in al-Khaniyyah: If he likens her to a woman with whom his father or son has committed zina, Muhammad said: It is not zihar. And Abu Yusuf said: It is zihar. And it (i.e., Abu Yusuf's view) is correct. And if he likens her to the mother of a woman or the daughter of a woman with whom he has committed zina, it is zihar. End quote. And if he kissed an ajnabiyyah with desire, then likened his wife to her daughter, he is not a mazahir according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf; as in al-Walwaljiyyah. Thus, in al-Nihayah, the word 'by agreement' was added to the definition, and the commentator and others followed him. And what is in al-Dirayah that if he likens her to the mother of a woman with whom his father or son has committed zina, it is zihar, is problematic because at most she would be like the mother of his father's wife or a permissible (woman); as in Fath al-Qadir. And evidently it is a slip of the pen, and it has become clear to me that there is no need for the restriction of 'his son' and she corrects it: her private part in prohibition is like his mother's private part. And what is in al-Bahr is refuted where it transmitted what is in al-Muhit and affirmed it and did not transmit it as a discussion, and you have known what is the reality.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents intra-Hanafi disputes on specific comparisons. The first case: if a husband compares his wife to a woman with whom his father or son has committed zina (a 'mazniyyah'), Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it is not zihar, while Abu Yusuf holds it is zihar, and the text says the latter is correct. The reason is that such a woman is not a permanent mahram; she is only forbidden due to the act of zina, which does not establish permanent prohibition. Abu Yusuf apparently considers the zina as creating a disrespect akin to a mahram. The second case: comparing the wife to the mother or daughter of a woman with whom the husband himself has committed zina is unanimously zihar. The third case: if a man kisses an ajnabiyyah with desire, then later compares his wife to that woman's daughter, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is not zihar, while Abu Yusuf says it is. The author notes that this dispute led the author of al-Nihayah to add the word 'by agreement' to the definition to exclude such cases. The passage then critiques a statement in al-Dirayah that considering such a comparison as zihar is problematic, calling it a slip of the pen. The author explains that the correct view aligns with the earlier positions.

Key Terms
المزنية (al-mazniyyah): A woman with whom zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) has been committed, specifically by the husband's father or son.
سبق قلم (sabq qalam): A slip of the pen; a mistake in writing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man compares his wife to a woman with whom his father has committed zina, what is the ruling?
A) It is not zihar according to all scholars.
B) It is zihar according to Abu Yusuf (the mufta bihi view).
C) It is zihar only if the woman is a mahram.
D) It is a valid divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether comparing one's wife to a woman from zina constitutes zihar; the relied-upon position (Abu Yusuf) considers it zihar.

The Ruling on Likening One's Wife to Blood and Pork – A Textual Correction
Critical refinement on the ruling for likening to blood/pork

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the utterance 'you are to me like blood and pork' depending on intention, and explain why the correct transmission from al-Khaniyyah differs from a common misquotation.

Core Idea
Likening to blood or pork is not zihar; without intention it has no effect, and even with zihar intention it is not zihar.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq resolves a textual confusion: a widely circulated statement from al-Khāniyyah claimed that saying 'you are to me like blood and pork' is īlā' if no intention is specified. However, the author checks the original manuscript and finds that the word 'lā' (not) was omitted – the correct text says it is not īlā'. This lesson clarifies the actual ruling and explains why this correction matters for the Hanafi law of ṭalāq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
An objection was raised against the author of Kanz al-Daqā’iq based on a quote from al-Khāniyyah that the utterance 'you are to me like blood and pork' constitutes īlā' if no intention is specified. Recognize why this would contradict the established Hanafi position.
2
Examine the original text
Look at the actual manuscript of al-Khāniyyah. The correct text reads: '...the correct (view) is that if he intended nothing, it is not īlā'. And if he intended divorce, it is divorce, and if he intended ẓihār, it is not ẓihār.' Note the inclusion of 'lā' (not).
3
Understand the correction
The earlier transmission had dropped the word 'lā', causing the confusion. The corrected text aligns with the Hanafi principle that ẓihār requires likening to a permanently prohibited female relative, and īlā' requires a vow of abstinence. Blood and pork are not relatives, so the utterance has no effect without intention.
4
Apply the broader principle
The passage also confirms that likening one's wife to the back of a woman who is not permanently prohibited (like a Magian, apostate, or another man's wife) is not ẓihār, and likening to a man is also not ẓihār. This reinforces the rule that ẓihār is specific to comparisons with female mahram relatives.
5
Confirm the supporting evidence
The author cites multiple sources (al-Shurnubalāliyyah, al-Tātārkhāniyyah, al-Tahdhīb) that agree with the corrected text and the principle. This shows the strength of the Hanafi position and the importance of verifying textual transmissions.
The final part about the slip of the pen in al-Dirāyah is tangential but shows meticulous scholarship.

نعم يرد على المصنف ما في الخانية أنت علي كالدم والخنزير فالصحيح أنه إذا نوى طلاقاً أو ظهاراً فكما نوى وإن لم ينو شيئاً كان إيلاء ا.هـ. قلت: لا يخفى أنه إن سلم ما ه في الخانية أشكل ما في البدائع وكان مقوياً لما في المحيط وإلا يسلم لم يتوجه الإيراد على المصنف لكن الذي رأيته في نسخة الخانية التي عندي مخالف لما نقله في النهر ونصه : ولو قال لامرأته أنت علي كالميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير اختلفت الروايات فيه والصحيح أنه لم ينو شيئاً لا يكون إيلاء، وإن نوى الطلاق يكون طلاقاً، وإن نوى الظهار لا يكون ظهاراً ا هـ. بحروفه. وهكذا قال في الشرنبلالية قال في الخانية : وإن نوى ظهاراً لا يكون ظهاراً. وكذلك في التتارخانية نقل عبارة الخانية كما نقلناه. فعلم أن النسخة التي نقل عنها في النهر سقط منها لفظة «لا» فأورد ما أورد لكن رأيت في الخانية أيضاً ما نصه ولو شبهها بظهر امرأة لا تحل له في الجملة كالمجوسية والمرتدة ومنكوحة الغير لا يكون ظهاراً، وكذا التشبيه بالرجل أي رجل كان ا هـ . وكذلك صرح في التتارخانية عن التهذيب بأنه لو شبهها بالرجل لم يكن مظاهراً. وبه تأيد ما في البدائع وبما علمت من النقل السابق اندفع الإشكال والله تعالى الموفق قوله : (والظاهر أنه سبق (قلم الضمير يعود إلى ما في الدراية. قال في النهر : وكأنه لأن المشكل يمكن الجواب عنه وهذا لا يمكن الجواب عنه. وعندي أن الضمير يرجع في شبهها إلى الزاني المستفاد من الزنا وعليه فلا إشكال إذ الخلاف المذكور إنما هو فيما إذا
Yes, it is objected against the author (al-Musannif) by what is in al-Khaniyyah: 'you are to me like blood and pork,' and the correct (view) is that if he intends divorce or zihar, then it is as he intended, and if he intended nothing, it is ila'. End quote. I said: It is not hidden that if what is in al-Khaniyyah is accepted, what is in al-Bada'i' becomes problematic, and it would strengthen what is in al-Muhit, otherwise it is not accepted, and the objection does not apply to the author. But what I saw in the copy of al-Khaniyyah that I have is contrary to what al-Nahr transmitted from it. Its text: 'And if he says to his wife: you are to me like carrion, blood, and pork, the narrations differ about it, and the correct (view) is that if he intended nothing, it is not ila'. And if he intended divorce, it is divorce, and if he intended zihar, it is not zihar.' End quote verbatim. And similarly it is said in al-Shurnubalaliyyah: 'In al-Khaniyyah: And if he intends zihar, it is not zihar.' And likewise in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, the wording of al-Khaniyyah is transmitted as we have quoted. So it is known that the copy from which al-Nahr transmitted had the word 'la' dropped, so he raised the objection. But I saw in al-Khaniyyah also its text: 'And if he likens her to the back of a woman who is not permissible for him at all, like the Magian, the apostate, and the wife of another, it is not zihar, and likewise likening to a man, any man.' End quote. And likewise it is explicitly stated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Tahdhib that if he likens her to a man, he is not a mazahir. And thus the position in al-Bada'i' is supported, and by what you know from the previous transmission, the problem is resolved. And Allah is the grantor of success. His saying: 'and it is apparent that it is a slip of the pen' – the pronoun refers to what is in al-Dirayah. He said in al-Nahr: 'It is as if because the problematic (case) can be answered, and this cannot be answered.' And in my view, the pronoun refers in 'he likened her' to the adulterer derived from zina, and thus there is no problem, for the mentioned dispute is only when...
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement dealing with the ruling on likening one's wife to blood or pork. The author notes an objection raised against the matn author based on a statement in al-Khaniyyah that if the intention is nothing, it is ila'. However, after checking the actual manuscript of al-Khaniyyah, the author finds that the correct text states that if no intention is specified, it is not ila' either, and if zihar is intended, it is not zihar. The earlier transmission had dropped the word 'la', causing confusion. The passage also confirms that comparing one's wife to the back of a woman who is not permanently prohibited (Magian, apostate, or another man's wife) is not zihar, and comparing to a man is also not zihar. This supports the earlier view from al-Bada'i'. The final part deals with correcting a slip of the pen in al-Dirayah regarding the comparison to a woman involved in zina, clarifying that the dispute is only when the likening is to the adulteress herself, not to the mother of the woman with whom zina was committed.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlāʾ): A vow by the husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for four months or more, which leads to a revocable divorce if he does not return.
الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير (al-maytah wa al-dam wa laḥm al-khinzīr): carrion, blood, and pork – items that are najis (ritually impure) and not permissible to eat, but not mahram persons.
الظهار (al-ẓihār): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where the husband says to his wife 'you are to me like the back of my mother' – in Islam it is prohibited and requires expiation if the husband wishes to resume relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the corrected text of al-Khaniyyah, if a husband says 'you are to me like blood and pork' without any intention, what is the ruling?
A) It is considered ẓihār and requires expiation.
B) It is considered īlā' and requires waiting four months.
C) It has no legal effect.
D) It is an invalid utterance.

Key Takeaway
Likening one's wife to blood or pork has no legal effect unless divorce is intended, and it never constitutes ẓihār, because ẓihār requires comparison to a permanently prohibited female relative.

The Four Pillars of Zihar
Defines the four essential components of zihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four pillars of zihar and state the conditions for each pillar.

Core Idea
Zihar rests on four pillars: subject, object, comparison, and expression.

The Hanafi jurists define zihar by its essential components (arkan). This lesson walks through each pillar and its conditions so you can determine when a zihar declaration is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject (al-mushabbah)
The subject is the husband. He must be adult, sane, and Muslim because he must be capable of expiation.
The subject is the one making the comparison.
2
Identify the object (al-mushabbah with fatha)
The object is the wife or a part of her that represents the whole. She must be a lawful wife.
A slave wife is included; an enslaved concubine is not.
3
Identify the object of comparison (al-mushabbah bihi)
This must be a body part that is permanently prohibited to look at from a permanently prohibited woman (e.g., mother's back).
If compared to a temporary prohibition, it is not zihar.
4
Identify the expression (adawat al-tashbih)
The words used. Explicit (sarih) like 'like my mother's back' does not require intent; figurative (kinayah) requires intent.
Some phrases like 'you are from me a muzahira' are invalid per Abu Yusuf.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فتحرير رقبة من قبل أن يتماسا [المجادلة : ٣] لكن لما لم يكن أهلاً للكفارة لم يصح ظهاره . قال بعضهم : والعجب من الشافعي أنه قيد الرقبة بالإيمان ولم يجوز أن يملك الكافر المؤمن وصحح ظهاره فكان تناقضاً. And the conclusion is that here there are four pillars: the subject, the object, the object of comparison, and the tool of comparison. As for the first, which is the subject (with kasra on the ba), he is the husband: adult, sane, Muslim. And [there follows discussion of comparing to an adulterer, etc.]. As for the second, which is the object (with fatha on the ba), it is the married wife or a part of her that expresses the whole or a substantial portion. As for the third, which is the object of comparison, it is a limb that is not permissible to look at from a woman who is permanently prohibited to him. As for the fourth, which is the indicator of it, it is the pillar and is explicit and figurative; the explicit is 'like my mother's back,' and 'from me,' and 'with me,' and 'together with me' like 'upon.' And I have not seen a ruling if he says 'you are like my mother's back' without the addition, that it is not zihar because it is possible he intended that she is like his mother's back to someone else and I am from you... and it should be... and 'I have declared zihar from you' is from the explicit. In al-Tatar Khaniyya from Abu Yusuf: if he said 'you are from me a muzahira,' it is invalid. And its condition regarding the woman is that she be a wife, even a slave, so it is not valid from his slave, nor from his divorced wife, nor from a stranger unless he connects it to marriage as will come. And regarding the man, it is that he be capable of expiation, so it is not valid from a dhimmi, a minor, or an insane person because the disbeliever is not capable of expiation. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: the dhimmi is obliged to perform the kaffarah of zihar if he declares zihar, and regarding its validity there is a narration from Abu Yusuf; the scholars transmitted it from al-Shafi'i. And the conclusion is that Allah Most High restricted with 'from you' in the first verse: 'those who declare zihar among you' and when He began to explain the expiation He did not restrict with 'from you,' so He said 'those who declare zihar from their wives' but when he is not capable of expiation, his zihar is not valid. Some said: it is astonishing from al-Shafi'i that he restricted the slave to faith and did not permit the disbeliever to own a believing slave, yet he validated his zihar, which is a contradiction. Some Shafi'is responded: we specify for his expiation feeding, and it does not follow from the validity of zihar that the declaring person be capable of all types, as evidenced by our position that he is not capable of other than fasting. And if a Muslim declares zihar then apostatizes, his zihar remains according to Abu Hanifa such that if he returns to Islam, he may not approach except with expiation. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it does not remain because the apostate is not capable of its ruling, which is expiation. And the truth is that the state is one of the continuation of its ruling, which is prohibition, not the state of its inception; disbelief does not negate prohibition, and its ruling is the prohibition of intercourse and its precursors until expiation. His statement: 'He forbids intercourse and its precursors by 'you are to me like my mother's back' until he expiates.' As for the prohibition of intercourse, it is by the Book and Sunnah. As for the prohibition of precursors, their inclusion under the text indicating the prohibition of intercourse is from His statement 'before they touch each other' because there is no cause to carry it metaphorically to intercourse when the literal meaning is possible, and intercourse is prohibited because it is one of the individuals of 'touch,' so all are prohibited by the text. So in Fath: its timing is valid contrary to divorce; it removes the problem so that the prohibition does not extend from yesterday to divorce and zihar from that day and after. His statement: 'And it should be that he is not a muzahir.' In al-Nahr: there is consideration; rather, he should be a muzahir, so ponder it. End. And al-Ramli said: it is not zihar unless he intends zihar because the deletion of the adverb when it is known is permissible, and if he intends it, it is valid. Ponder his statement: 'The verification is contrary to what he claimed is the verification.' He responded in al-Nahr that touching without desire...
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and conditional exposition of zihar's pillars and the necessary qualifications of the husband. It first enumerates the four pillars (arkan): (1) the subject (al-mushabbah) – the husband, who must be adult, sane, and Muslim; (2) the object (al-mushabbah bihi) – the wife or a part of her that represents the whole; (3) the object of comparison (al-mushabbah bihi) – a permanently prohibited body part (like the mother's back); (4) the expression (adawat al-tashbih) – the words used. The text then discusses each pillar in detail, noting that the expression can be explicit (sarih) like 'like my mother's back' or figurative (kinayah). It mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf that some expressions are invalid. The conditions for the wife are that she must be a wife (even an enslaved), but not a divorced or unrelated woman unless linked to marriage. For the husband, he must be capable of expiation (ahl al-kaffarah), so zihar from a dhimmi, minor, or insane person is invalid. However, there is a narration that a dhimmi is obliged to perform kaffarah if he declares zihar, and a dispute is noted regarding its validity between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage then delves into a detailed discussion about the apostate's zihar: according to Abu Hanifa, the zihar remains even after apostasy, and upon return to Islam, he must expiate before resuming relations. The two disciples hold that apostasy invalidates the zihar. The text supports Abu Hanifa's view by saying the zihar creates a prohibition that persists regardless of the person's faith status; the condition is only for the inception (insha') not the continuation (baqa'). Finally, the passage explains why the prohibition extends to sexual precursors (like kissing), citing the verse 'before they touch each other' – because 'touch' includes all acts of intimacy, so all are prohibited until expiation.

Key Terms
المشبه (بكسر الباء) (al-mushabbah (kasr)): The subject of the comparison: the husband who utters the zihar declaration.
المشبه (بفتح الباء) (al-mushabbah (fath)): The object of the comparison: the wife (or a part of her) being compared.
المشبه به (al-mushabbah bihi): The object of resemblance: the permanently prohibited body part (e.g., mother's back).
أداة التشبيه (adawat al-tashbih): The expression or words used to make the comparison.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four pillars of zihar according to this passage?
A) The husband (subject)
B) The wife (object)
C) The intention (niyyah)
D) The expression (tool of comparison)

Key Takeaway
A valid zihar requires four pillars: a qualified husband, his wife, a comparison to a permanently prohibited body part, and a verbal expression.

Talaq — Divorce

Disputes on Zihar's Validity: Dhimmi and Apostate
Explains conditions for the husband and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a dhimmi's zihar is invalid in the Hanafi school and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on apostasy's effect on zihar.

Core Idea
Zihar requires the husband to be capable of expiation; this excludes dhimmis and, in a dispute, affects apostasy.

While the pillars define the structure of zihar, the husband's legal capacity (ahliyyah) is crucial. This lesson examines the condition that the husband must be 'ahl al-kaffarah' and two disputes: whether a dhimmi can perform zihar and whether apostasy invalidates an existing zihar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi condition for the husband
The husband must be capable of performing expiation (kaffarah): adult, sane, Muslim. This excludes minors, insane, and non-Muslims.
This is from the zahir al-riwayah.
2
Analyze the dhimmi case and the inter-madhhab dispute
Shafi'i holds that a dhimmi's zihar is valid because he is addressed by the law and can feed the poor. Hanafi rejects this, citing the verse 'from you' and the need for capability for the specific ritual expiation.
The author notes a narration from Abu Yusuf that might oblige kaffarah, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that zihar is invalid.
3
Analyze the apostate case and the intra-Hanafi dispute
If a Muslim declares zihar then apostatizes: Abu Hanifa says the prohibition remains; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is void because the apostate cannot expiate. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
The reasoning: the condition of capability applies only at inception (insha'), not continuation (baqa').
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a dhimmi declares zihar: no effect in Hanafi; valid and requires feeding in Shafi'i. If a Muslim apostatizes after zihar: prohibition persists until expiation upon return (Abu Hanifa); prohibition lifts immediately (Sahibayn).
The author prefers Abu Hanifa's view.

شاسع وأما الثالث وهو المشبه به عضو لا يحل النظر إليه من محرمة عليه تأبيداً. وأما الرابع وهو الدال عليه وهو ركنه وهو صريح وكناية، فالصريح علي كظهر أمي ومني وعندي ومعي كعلى ولم أر حكم ما إذا قال أنت كظهر أمي بدون إضافة أن لا يكون مظاهراً لاحتمال أنه قصد أنها كظهر أمه على غيره وأنا منك مظاهر له وينبغي وظاهرت منك من الصريح وفي التتارخانية وعن أبي يوسف: لو قال أنت مني مظاهرة أنه يكون باطلاً. وشرطه في المرأة كونها زوجة ولو أمة فلا يصح من أمته ولا من مبانته ولا من أجنبية إلا إذا أضافه إلى التزوج كما سيأتي. وفي الرجل كونه من أهل الكفارة فلا يصح من ذمي وصبي ومجنون لأن الكافر ليس من أهل الكفارة. وفي التتارخانية : يلزم الذمي كفارة الظهار إذا ظاهر وفي صحته عن أبي يوسف نظر إنما نقله المشايخ عن الشافعي. والحاصل أنه تعالى قيد بقوله منكم في الآية الأولى وهو قوله تعالى الذين يظاهرون منكم من هن أمهاتهم أن أمهاتهم إلا اللائي ولدنهم وأنهم ليقولون منكراً من القول وزورا وإن الله لعفو غفور [المجادلة : ٢] ولما شرع في بيان الكفارة لم يقيده بقوله «منكم» فقال والذين يظاهرون من نسائهم ثم يعودون لما قالوا فتحرير رقبة من قبل أن يتماسا [المجادلة : ٣] لكن لما لم يكن أهلاً للكفارة لم يصح ظهاره . قال بعضهم : والعجب من الشافعي أنه قيد الرقبة بالإيمان ولم يجوز أن يملك الكافر المؤمن وصحح ظهاره فكان تناقضاً. ورده بعض الشافعية بأنا عيناً لكفارته الإطعام ولا يلزم من صحة الظهار أن يكون المظاهر أهلاً لكل الأنواع بدليل عندنا أنه ليس أهلاً لغير الصوم ولو ظاهر المسلم ثم ارتد والعياذ بالله بقي ظهاره عند أبي حنيفة حتى لو أسلم لا يحل القربان إلا بالكفارة، وعندهما لا يبقى لأن المرتد ليس أهلاً لحكمه وهو الكفارة، وله أن الحال حال بقاء حكمه وهو الحرمة لا حال الانعقاد والكفر ليس بمنافٍ للحرمة وحكمه حرمة الوطء ودواعيه إلى غاية الكفارة. قوله : (حرم الوطء ودواعيه بأنت علي كظهر أمي حتى يكفر) أما حرمة الوطء فبالكتاب والسنة، وأما حرمة الدواعي فإن دخولها تحت النص المفيد لحرمة الوطء وهو قوله تعالى من قبل أن يتماسا [المجادلة : ٣] لأنه لا موجب فيه للحمل على المجاز وهو الوطء لإمكان الحقيقة، ويحرم الجماع لأنه من أفراد التماس فيحرم الكل بالنص؛ كذا في فتح يصح توقيته بخلاف الطلاق يدفع الإشكال فلا تتعدى الحرمة من أمس إلى الطلاق والظهار من أنه اليوم وما بعده قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يكون مظاهراً قال في النهر : فيه نظر بل ينبغي أن يكون مظاهراً فتدبره ا هـ. وقال الرملي : لا يكون ظهاراً ما لم ينو الظهار لأن حذف الظرف عند العلم به جائز وإذا نواه صح تأمل قوله : ( فالتحقيق خلاف ما زعم أنه التحقيق أجاب في النهر بأن المس بغير شهوة البحر الرائق ج ٤ م ١١
And the conclusion is that here there are four pillars: the subject, the object, the object of comparison, and the tool of comparison. As for the first, which is the subject (with kasra on the ba), he is the husband: adult, sane, Muslim. And [there follows discussion of comparing to an adulterer, etc.]. As for the second, which is the object (with fatha on the ba), it is the married wife or a part of her that expresses the whole or a substantial portion. As for the third, which is the object of comparison, it is a limb that is not permissible to look at from a woman who is permanently prohibited to him. As for the fourth, which is the indicator of it, it is the pillar and is explicit and figurative; the explicit is 'like my mother's back,' and 'from me,' and 'with me,' and 'together with me' like 'upon.' And I have not seen a ruling if he says 'you are like my mother's back' without the addition, that it is not zihar because it is possible he intended that she is like his mother's back to someone else and I am from you... and it should be... and 'I have declared zihar from you' is from the explicit. In al-Tatar Khaniyya from Abu Yusuf: if he said 'you are from me a muzahira,' it is invalid. And its condition regarding the woman is that she be a wife, even a slave, so it is not valid from his slave, nor from his divorced wife, nor from a stranger unless he connects it to marriage as will come. And regarding the man, it is that he be capable of expiation, so it is not valid from a dhimmi, a minor, or an insane person because the disbeliever is not capable of expiation. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: the dhimmi is obliged to perform the kaffarah of zihar if he declares zihar, and regarding its validity there is a narration from Abu Yusuf; the scholars transmitted it from al-Shafi'i. And the conclusion is that Allah Most High restricted with 'from you' in the first verse: 'those who declare zihar among you' and when He began to explain the expiation He did not restrict with 'from you,' so He said 'those who declare zihar from their wives' but when he is not capable of expiation, his zihar is not valid. Some said: it is astonishing from al-Shafi'i that he restricted the slave to faith and did not permit the disbeliever to own a believing slave, yet he validated his zihar, which is a contradiction. Some Shafi'is responded: we specify for his expiation feeding, and it does not follow from the validity of zihar that the declaring person be capable of all types, as evidenced by our position that he is not capable of other than fasting. And if a Muslim declares zihar then apostatizes, his zihar remains according to Abu Hanifa such that if he returns to Islam, he may not approach except with expiation. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it does not remain because the apostate is not capable of its ruling, which is expiation. And the truth is that the state is one of the continuation of its ruling, which is prohibition, not the state of its inception; disbelief does not negate prohibition, and its ruling is the prohibition of intercourse and its precursors until expiation. His statement: 'He forbids intercourse and its precursors by 'you are to me like my mother's back' until he expiates.' As for the prohibition of intercourse, it is by the Book and Sunnah. As for the prohibition of precursors, their inclusion under the text indicating the prohibition of intercourse is from His statement 'before they touch each other' because there is no cause to carry it metaphorically to intercourse when the literal meaning is possible, and intercourse is prohibited because it is one of the individuals of 'touch,' so all are prohibited by the text. So in Fath: its timing is valid contrary to divorce; it removes the problem so that the prohibition does not extend from yesterday to divorce and zihar from that day and after. His statement: 'And it should be that he is not a muzahir.' In al-Nahr: there is consideration; rather, he should be a muzahir, so ponder it. End. And al-Ramli said: it is not zihar unless he intends zihar because the deletion of the adverb when it is known is permissible, and if he intends it, it is valid. Ponder his statement: 'The verification is contrary to what he claimed is the verification.' He responded in al-Nahr that touching without desire...
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and conditional exposition of zihar's pillars and the necessary qualifications of the husband. It first enumerates the four pillars (arkan): (1) the subject (al-mushabbah) – the husband, who must be adult, sane, and Muslim; (2) the object (al-mushabbah bihi) – the wife or a part of her that represents the whole; (3) the object of comparison (al-mushabbah bihi) – a permanently prohibited body part (like the mother's back); (4) the expression (adawat al-tashbih) – the words used. The text then discusses each pillar in detail, noting that the expression can be explicit (sarih) like 'like my mother's back' or figurative (kinayah). It mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf that some expressions are invalid. The conditions for the wife are that she must be a wife (even an enslaved), but not a divorced or unrelated woman unless linked to marriage. For the husband, he must be capable of expiation (ahl al-kaffarah), so zihar from a dhimmi, minor, or insane person is invalid. However, there is a narration that a dhimmi is obliged to perform kaffarah if he declares zihar, and a dispute is noted regarding its validity between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage then delves into a detailed discussion about the apostate's zihar: according to Abu Hanifa, the zihar remains even after apostasy, and upon return to Islam, he must expiate before resuming relations. The two disciples hold that apostasy invalidates the zihar. The text supports Abu Hanifa's view by saying the zihar creates a prohibition that persists regardless of the person's faith status; the condition is only for the inception (insha') not the continuation (baqa'). Finally, the passage explains why the prohibition extends to sexual precursors (like kissing), citing the verse 'before they touch each other' – because 'touch' includes all acts of intimacy, so all are prohibited until expiation.

Key Terms
أهل الكفارة (ahl al-kaffarah): A person capable of performing expiation (adult, sane, Muslim).
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state.
المرتد (al-murtadd): One who leaves Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a dhimmi declares zihar?
A) The zihar is valid and he must feed sixty poor.
B) The zihar is valid only if his wife is also a dhimmi.
C) The zihar is invalid because he is not capable of expiation.
D) The zihar is valid but he must free a slave.

Key Takeaway
The condition that the husband be capable of expiation creates a clear boundary: non-Muslims cannot perform valid zihar, and apostasy does not undo an already established prohibition.

Definition and Pillars of Dhihar
Definition of dhihar pillars and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dhihar, identify its four pillars (musabbih, mushabbah, mushabbah bihi, dal), and distinguish explicit from implicit wording.

Core Idea
Dhihar is a forbidden comparison that prohibits intercourse until kaffarah is performed.

Dhihar is a pre-Islamic practice that Islam reformed into a prohibited act requiring expiation. This lesson unpacks the four pillars of dhihar as described in the passage: who makes the comparison, who is compared, what they are compared to, and the wording used. Understanding these pillars is essential for recognizing a valid dhihar declaration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars (arkan) of dhihar
From the text, list the four components: the person making the comparison (al-musabbih), the person being compared (al-mushabbah), the thing compared to (al-mushabbah bihi), and the wording (al-dal).
The text explicitly names these pillars in order.
2
Define explicit (sarih) wording for dhihar
The text gives examples: 'you are like my mother's back', 'from me', etc. Determine which phrases are unambiguous in indicating dhihar.
Implicit wording may require intention.
3
Describe the condition regarding the woman
The woman must be a wife (even a slave wife). The text lists invalid cases: slave concubine, irrevocably divorced woman, and stranger unless linked to marriage.
This condition is essential for validity.
4
Explain the condition regarding the man
The man must be eligible for kaffarah (ahl al-kaffarah). Thus dhihar is invalid from a dhimmi, child, or insane person.
Eligibility for kaffarah is key to the Hanafi position.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and condition ruling for dhihar. The author first discusses the four pillars of dhihar: the person making the comparison (musabbih), the person being compared (mushabbah), the thing compared to (mushabbah bihi), and the wording (dal). The explicit wording includes phrases like 'you are like my mother's back'. Then the conditions are stated: the woman must be a wife (not a slave without marriage, not a divorced woman, not a stranger unless linked to marriage). The man must be legally capable of performing kaffarah, so dhihar from a dhimmi, child, or insane person is not valid. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf in al-TatarKhaniyya states that a dhimmi is obligated to perform kaffarah if he does dhihar, but its validity from him is considered problematic, as the scholars attribute this view to al-Shafi'i. The passage then delves into the Quranic evidence: the first verse restricts with 'among you' (minhum), implying dhihar is only valid for Muslims, but the second verse on kaffarah does not repeat this restriction, leading to disagreement. A Shafi'i objection is presented: they require the slave to be Muslim for kaffarah but do not require the muzzahir to be Muslim. The Hanafi response is that the kaffarah for a dhimmi is specifically feeding, not freeing a slave, and validity of dhihar does not require eligibility for all types of kaffarah, as the dhimmi is not eligible for fasting according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الظهار (al-dhihar): A prohibited comparison making intercourse forbidden until kaffarah.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation: freeing a slave, fasting two months, feeding sixty poor.
المظاهر (al-muzzahir): The man who declares dhihar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a condition for the validity of dhihar?
A) The woman must be a free Muslim.
B) The man must be eligible for kaffarah.
C) The declaration must be made in Arabic.
D) The woman must consent to the declaration.

Key Takeaway
Dhihar is valid only if the man is eligible for kaffarah and the woman is his wife.

The Dispute Over Dhihar from a Dhimmi
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of dhihar from a dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on dhihar from a dhimmi, citing the Quranic evidence and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school restricts dhihar to Muslims because kaffarah requires faith; the Shafi'i school extends it to dhimmis.

The passage delves into a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether a non-Muslim (dhimmi) can perform a valid dhihar. The Hanafi school argues that dhihar is invalid from a dhimmi because he is not eligible for kaffarah, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it valid. This lesson traces the Quranic verses cited and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi condition for the man
The passage states: 'In the man, he must be from among those eligible for kaffarah, so it is not valid from a dhimmi.' This is the core condition.
Eligibility for kaffarah requires faith (iman).
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
The first verse (58:2) restricts with 'among you' (minhum). The second verse (58:3) on kaffarah does not repeat the restriction.
Hanafis argue the restriction in the first verse carries over; Shafi'is argue it does not.
3
Contrast the Shafi'i position
Shafi'is hold that the kaffarah verse is general, so dhihar is valid from a dhimmi, and he performs kaffarah by feeding (since freeing a Muslim slave is not possible for him).
Shafi'is also argue that requiring the slave to be Muslim but not the muzzahir is consistent.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that kaffarah is an act of worship requiring faith; a dhimmi is not obligated for worship. Feeding is a financial act, but the overall obligation remains an act of worship.
The Hanafi school maintains the mufta bihi view that dhihar from a dhimmi is invalid.

Source Text
