As for the fourth, it is the indicator (al-dal) which is its pillar, and it is explicit and implicit. The explicit is 'you are like my mother's back' and 'from me' and 'with me' and 'with me' like 'upon' and I have not seen the ruling when someone says 'you are like my mother's back' without addition: that he is not a muzzahir, because of the possibility that he intended that she is like his mother's back regarding someone else, and 'I am from you a muzzahir' and it is befitting, and 'I have declared dhihar from you' are from the explicit. In al-TatarKhaniyya and from Abu Yusuf: if he said 'you are from me a muzzahara', that it is invalid. Its condition regarding the woman is that she be a wife, even if a slave, so it is not valid from his slave woman, nor from a divorced woman with irrevocable divorce, nor from a foreign woman, unless he adds it to marriage as will come. Regarding the man, he must be from among those eligible for kaffarah, so it is not valid from a dhimmi, a boy, or an insane person, because the disbeliever is not eligible for kaffarah. In al-TatarKhaniyya: the dhimmi is obligated the kaffarah of dhihar if he performs dhihar, and regarding its validity from Abu Yusuf there is a consideration; the scholars transmitted it only from al-Shafi'i. The summary is that Allah Most High restricted with His saying 'among you' in the first verse, which is His saying 'Those among you who declare dhihar of their wives as their mothers'... and when He began to explain the kaffarah He did not restrict it with 'among you'. But since he was not eligible for kaffarah, his dhihar is not valid. Some said: the wonder from al-Shafi'i is that he restricted the slave to belief and did not permit the disbeliever to own the believer, yet he validated his dhihar, so it was a contradiction. Some Shafi'is responded that we specifically assign his kaffarah as feeding, and the validity of dhihar does not require that the muzzahir be eligible for all types, as evidenced in our view that he is not eligible for other than fasting.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a definition and condition ruling for dhihar. The author first discusses the four pillars of dhihar: the person making the comparison (musabbih), the person being compared (mushabbah), the thing compared to (mushabbah bihi), and the wording (dal). The explicit wording includes phrases like 'you are like my mother's back'. Then the conditions are stated: the woman must be a wife (not a slave without marriage, not a divorced woman, not a stranger unless linked to marriage). The man must be legally capable of performing kaffarah, so dhihar from a dhimmi, child, or insane person is not valid. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf in al-TatarKhaniyya states that a dhimmi is obligated to perform kaffarah if he does dhihar, but its validity from him is considered problematic, as the scholars attribute this view to al-Shafi'i. The passage then delves into the Quranic evidence: the first verse restricts with 'among you' (minhum), implying dhihar is only valid for Muslims, but the second verse on kaffarah does not repeat this restriction, leading to disagreement. A Shafi'i objection is presented: they require the slave to be Muslim for kaffarah but do not require the muzzahir to be Muslim. The Hanafi response is that the kaffarah for a dhimmi is specifically feeding, not freeing a slave, and validity of dhihar does not require eligibility for all types of kaffarah, as the dhimmi is not eligible for fasting according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection.
أهل الكفارة (ahl al-kaffarah): Those eligible to perform kaffarah: free, adult, sane Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling regarding dhihar from a dhimmi?
A) It is valid and he must fast two months.
B) It is invalid and no kaffarah is required.
C) It is valid only if he feeds sixty poor.
D) It is valid only if his wife is also a dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school maintains that dhihar is valid only from a Muslim, due to the condition of eligibility for kaffarah.

Effect of Apostasy on Dhihar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether apostasy nullifies a prior dhihar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa holds that dhihar survives apostasy and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Apostasy does not erase a prohibition already established; the ruling of dhihar continues because the prohibition persists.

In this passage, we encounter an important intra-Hanafi dispute: does apostasy nullify an existing dhihar? While all agree that apostasy breaks the marriage bond, there is disagreement over whether the prohibition of intercourse established by a prior dhihar remains. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and the practical consequences for a returning apostate.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules: the dhihar remains valid even after apostasy, so if the man returns to Islam, he must perform kaffarah before intercourse.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that apostasy nullifies the dhihar, so upon return no kaffarah is needed.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Understand their reasoning: an apostate is not eligible for the ruling of dhihar because he cannot perform kaffarah (which requires faith).
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's response
See how Abu Hanifa counters: the ruling is about the prohibition (hurmah), not about kaffarah. The prohibition is continuous; kaffarah is contingent on return.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the difference: under Abu Hanifa, the returning apostate must still pay kaffarah; under Sahibayn, he may resume relations immediately.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو ظاهر المسلم ثم ارتد والعياذ بالله تعالى بقي ظهاره عند أبي حنيفة حتى لو أسلم لا يحل القربان إلا بالكفارة، وعندهما لا يبقى لأن المرتد ليس أهلاً لحكمه وهو الكفارة، وله أن الحال حال بقاء حكمه وهو الحرمة لا حال الانعقاد والكفر ليس بمنافٍ للحرمة وحكمه حرمة الوطء ودواعيه إلى غاية الكفارة.
And if a Muslim declares dhihar then apostatizes — may Allah protect us — his dhihar remains according to Abu Hanifa, so that even if he becomes Muslim, intercourse is not permissible except with kaffarah. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it does not remain because the apostate is not eligible for its ruling, which is kaffarah. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that the situation is one of continuation of its ruling, which is prohibition, not the state of initiation, and disbelief is not incompatible with the prohibition, and its ruling is the prohibition of intercourse and its preliminaries until the expiry of kaffarah.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of apostasy on an existing dhihar. The scenario: a Muslim man declares dhihar on his wife, then apostatizes from Islam. After apostasy, does his dhihar remain? According to Abu Hanifa, the dhihar remains valid, meaning the prohibition of intercourse continues, and even if he returns to Islam, he still must perform kaffarah before intercourse. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the dhihar is nullified by apostasy because the apostate is not eligible to be subject to the ruling of dhihar, which requires performance of kaffarah, and an apostate cannot perform kaffarah validly (since it requires faith). Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the prohibition of intercourse has already been established at the time of the dhihar. This prohibition is a continuous ruling that remains even after apostasy, because disbelief does not contradict the existence of a prohibition. The ruling is not about initiating the prohibition but about its continuation. The prohibition lasts until kaffarah is performed, which would be required upon return to Islam. This is an important ikhtilaf affecting whether a returning apostate can have relations with his wife without first performing kaffarah.

Key Terms
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy from Islam.
الظهار (al-dhihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce revived in Islam; a husband says to his wife 'You are to me as the back of my mother', creating a prohibition of intercourse until kaffarah is performed.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation required to remove the prohibition created by dhihar; options: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a dhihar if the husband apostatizes?
A) The dhihar is nullified and he can return to his wife without kaffarah.
B) The dhihar remains in effect, so he must still perform kaffarah when he returns to Islam.
C) The dhihar becomes a divorce.
D) The dhihar is suspended until he returns to Islam.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy does not automatically nullify a prior dhihar; according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, the prohibition of intercourse continues and kaffarah remains obligatory upon return to Islam.

Prohibition of Intercourse and Preliminaries in Dhihar
This passage explains the prohibition of intercourse and preliminaries in dhihar with Quranic evidence and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of intercourse and its preliminaries (dawa'i) in dhihar, explain the Quranic evidence, and distinguish which actions are permissible and which are prohibited based on intention and context.

Core Idea
In dhihar, not only intercourse but all direct preliminaries are haram, rooted in the literal meaning of 'tamass' in Quran 58:3.

This passage tackles a key fiqh question: what exactly becomes prohibited when a man declares dhihar? While the prohibition of intercourse is clear, the status of kissing, touching, and looking is debated. The Hanafi school uses the literal meaning of the Quranic phrase 'before they touch each other' to extend the prohibition to all direct preliminaries. However, there are exceptions based on context, such as fasting or menstruation, due to explicit prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is prohibited? Intercourse (al-wat') and its preliminaries (al-dawa'i). The ruling is haram until kaffarah is performed.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the Quranic verse (58:3): 'min qabli an yatamassa' (before they touch each other). The prohibition of intercourse is also from the Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'tamass' (touching) is literal and general, encompassing all forms of direct physical contact. Since the literal meaning is possible, it is taken as is, unless there is a contextual indicator to restrict it.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle: al-haqiqah tuqaddam 'ala al-majaz when possible.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on intention
Some scholars debate whether the phrase 'anti 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' automatically constitutes dhihar or requires the speaker's intention. The text discusses this.
Al-Nahr and al-Ramli offer different views on the necessity of niyyah.
5
Apply the principle of 'means to haram is haram' and its exceptions
The general rule is that the means (dawa'i) are also prohibited. However, this principle is relaxed in fasting and menstruation due to explicit prophetic practice and to avoid hardship. In dhihar, no such exception exists except for specific cases like kissing without desire on travel.
The text cites the Prophet kissing his wives while fasting and menstruating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (حرم الوطء ودواعيه بأنت علي كظهر أمي حتى يكفر) أما حرمة الوطء فبالكتاب والسنة، وأما حرمة الدواعي فإن دخولها تحت النص المفيد لحرمة الوطء وهو قوله تعالى من قبل أن يتماسا [المجادلة : ٣] لأنه لا موجب فيه للحمل على المجاز وهو الوطء لإمكان الحقيقة، ويحرم الجماع لأنه من أفراد التماس فيحرم الكل بالنص؛ كذا في فتح يصح توقيته بخلاف الطلاق يدفع الإشكال فلا تتعدى الحرمة من أمس إلى الطلاق والظهار من أنه اليوم وما بعده قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يكون مظاهراً قال في النهر : فيه نظر بل ينبغي أن يكون مظاهراً فتدبره ا هـ. وقال الرملي : لا يكون ظهاراً ما لم ينو الظهار لأن حذف الظرف عند العلم به جائز وإذا نواه صح تأمل قوله : ( فالتحقيق خلاف ما زعم أنه التحقيق أجاب في النهر بأن المس بغير شهوة حرم حرم القدير. وقد يقال إن الموجب للحمل على المجاز موجود وهو صدق التماس على المس بغير شهوة وليس بمحرم اتفاقاً فالتحقيق خلاف ما زعم أنه التحقيق وهو أن الأصل أن الوطء إذا ما كان داعياً إليه لأن طريق المحرم محرم وقد استمر هذا في الاستبراء والإحرام والاعتكاف، وخرج في الصوم والحيض عن هذا الأصل لنص صريح وهو أنه عليه السلام كان يقبل بعض نسائه وهو صائم وكان يقبلها وهي حائض، وحكمته لزوم الحرج لو حرمت الدواعي في الصوم والحيض لكثرة وقوعهما بخلاف غيرهما. وعن محمد للمظاهر تقبيلها إذا قدم من سفره بغير شهوة للشفقة والدواعي المباشرة والتقبيل واللمس عن شهوة والنظر إلى فرجها بشهوة كما في البدائع ولا يدخل فيها النظر إليها بشهوة وفي التتارخانية : ولا يحرم النظر إلى ظهرها وبطنها ولا إلى الشعر والصدر
His saying: (Intercourse and its preliminaries are forbidden by 'you are like my mother's back' until he performs kaffarah). As for the prohibition of intercourse, it is by the Book and Sunnah. As for the prohibition of preliminaries, they fall under the text that conveys the prohibition of intercourse, which is His saying 'before they touch each other' [58:3], because there is no cause to interpret it metaphorically to mean intercourse, since the literal meaning is possible. And intercourse is prohibited because it is a form of 'tamass' so the whole is prohibited by the text. This is in Fath. It is valid to time it contrary to divorce, it removes the problem so the prohibition does not extend from yesterday to talaq and dhihar from today and after. His saying: (And it is befitting that he should not be a muzzahir). He said in al-Nahr: there is consideration; rather it is befitting that he is a muzzahir, so ponder it. Al-Ramli said: It is not dhihar unless he intends dhihar, because the omission of the adverbial is permissible when it is known, and if he intends it, it is valid. Ponder. His saying: (The verification is contrary to what he claimed is the verification). He answered in al-Nahr that touching without desire is haram? The old? And it may be said that the cause for interpreting metaphorically exists, which is the truth of 'tamass' on touching without desire, and it is not prohibited by consensus, so the verification is contrary to what he claimed is the verification. And it is that the original principle is that the means to what is forbidden is also forbidden, and this principle is established in istibra', ihram, and i'tikaf. And it (the principle) is excluded in fasting and menstruation due to an explicit text, which is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss some of his wives while fasting and used to kiss her while she was menstruating. The wisdom is the resulting hardship if the preliminaries were prohibited in fasting and menstruation due to their frequent occurrence, unlike other cases. And from Muhammad: For the muzzahir, it is permissible to kiss her when he arrives from travel without desire out of compassion, and direct preliminaries, kissing and touching with desire, and looking at her private part with desire are forbidden, as in al-Bada'i'. And looking at her with desire is not included in the preliminaries? And in al-TatarKhaniyya: Looking at her back and belly and hair and chest is not prohibited.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the prohibition of intercourse and its preliminaries (dawa'i) in dhihar. The author of the sharh comments on the matn 'حرم الوطء ودواعيه'. He explains that the prohibition of intercourse is established by Qur'an and Sunnah. The prohibition of preliminaries is derived from the verse 'min qabli an yatamassa' (before they touch each other) because 'tamass' literally means touching, which includes all forms of direct physical contact, so all forms of touch that could lead to intercourse are prohibited. He addresses an objection that the verse might refer only to intercourse, but since the literal meaning of 'tamass' is possible, it is taken literally. The prohibition includes intercourse itself (al-jima') because it is an instance of tamass. He then discusses the issue of timing: dhihar can be timed to a specific period, unlike talaq (divorce) which is immediate. The discussion then shifts to a debate about the necessity of intention: some say the phrase 'أنت علي كظهر أمي' may only imply dhihar if the speaker intended dhihar, while others say it is explicit regardless. The commentator (al-Nahr and al-Ramli) discuss whether the phrase always constitutes dhihar or requires intention. Then the text returns to the principle that the means to what is prohibited is also prohibited, citing examples from istibra', ihram, and i'tikaf. However, this principle is excluded in the cases of fasting and menstruation because the Prophet himself kissed his wives while fasting and while menstruating, as an exception due to hardship. The passage then cites Imam Muhammad's opinion: a muzzahir may kiss his wife without desire when returning from travel, but kissing and touching with desire, and looking at the private part with desire are prohibited. Looking at other parts (back, belly, hair, chest) is not prohibited according to al-TatarKhaniyya. This lesson clarifies the fine line of what is allowed and prohibited regarding physical contact during dhihar.

Key Terms
الدواعي (al-dawa'i): The direct preliminaries to intercourse, such as kissing, touching with desire, and looking with desire.
التماس (al-tamass): Literally 'touching'; used in Quran 58:3 to refer to physical contact between spouses.
الظهار (al-dhihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'you are like my mother's back', which in Islam triggers a prohibition and requires kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is prohibited because it is a preliminary to intercourse.
B) It is permissible according to Imam Muhammad out of compassion.
C) It is obligatory as a form of kindness.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In dhihar, all direct physical preliminaries to intercourse are prohibited by the literal meaning of Quran 58:3, except where explicit exceptions exist (e.g., kissing without desire on travel).

The Explicit Phrase of Dhihar: Only Dhihar, Not Talaq
Definition ruling on the explicit dhihar phrase with historical expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the explicit phrase of dhihar and explain its historical relationship with pre-Islamic talaq.

Core Idea
The explicit phrase 'you are like my mother's back' creates dhihar, not talaq, even if divorce is intended.

The Hanafi school holds that the specific wording 'أنت علي كظهر أمي' (you are like my mother's back) establishes a legal relationship of dhihar, which is distinct from divorce (talaq). This ruling is rooted in the Quranic verse on dhihar and the understanding that this phrase cannot be used to effect a divorce, regardless of the speaker's intention. However, the historical background reveals that dhihar was a form of severe divorce in pre-Islamic times. This lesson examines the explicit phrase, its legal effect, and the historical transition from pre-Islamic practice to Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit phrase and its ruling
The explicit phrase is 'أنت علي كظهر أمي' (you are like my mother's back). According to al-Hidayah, this phrase only creates dhihar, not talaq, even if the speaker intended divorce.
Dhihar is a prohibited form of speech that requires expiation (kaffarah).
2
Understand the historical context
In pre-Islamic times (Jahiliyyah), dhihar was considered a severe form of divorce. The passage discusses whether this pre-Islamic ruling was carried into Islam or abrogated by the Quran.
Imam al-Razi notes that dhihar was among the strongest forms of divorce in Jahiliyyah.
3
Resolve the naskh question
If dhihar was a form of talaq in Jahiliyyah and also recognized as such in early Islam, then the Quranic verse on dhihar (Q. 58:2-4) would abrogate that practice. If not, the verse is not an abrogation but a new ruling. The passage suggests that evidence from the Prophet's statement indicates it was considered a prohibition, implying recognition.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq notes a contradiction in al-Hidayah's wording, which is resolved by al-Razi's analysis.
4
Apply the ruling to the present
The explicit phrase always produces dhihar. Even if the husband intended talaq, the effect is dhihar, not divorce. The historical debate confirms that the Islamic ruling is independent of the pre-Islamic practice.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الهداية أن اللفظ الصريح أعني - أنت علي كظهر أمي - لا يكون إلا ظهاراً ولو نوى به الطلاق لا لأنه يصح منسوخ فلا يتمكن من الإتيان به وهو يقتضي أن الظهار كان طلاقاً في الإسلام حتى يوصف بالنسخ مع أنه قال أولاً إنه كان طلاقاً في الجاهلية وهو يقتضي أن جعله ظهاراً ليس ناسخاً ولم أر أحداً من شراحها تعرض لذلك . وذكر الإمام فخر الدين الرازي في التفسير الكبير البحث الثاني أن الظهار كان من أشد طلاق الجاهلية لأنه في التحريم أوكد ما يمكن، فإن كان ذلك الحكم مقرراً في الشرع كانت الآية ناسخة له وإلا لم يعد ناسخاً في الشرع إلا في عادة الجاهلية لكن الذي روي أنه عليه السلام قال لها حرمت أو ما أراك إلا قد حرمت عليه كالدلالة على أنه كان شرعاً، فأما ما روي أنه توقف في الحكم فلا بدل على ذلك اهـ.
And in al-Hidayah: the explicit phrase, i.e. 'you are like my mother's back', is only dhihar, even if he intended divorce by it, because it is not valid as abrogated (divorce), so he cannot perform it with it. And this requires that dhihar was a divorce in Islam so that it could be described as abrogated, while he first said it was a divorce in Jahiliyyah, and this requires that making it dhihar is not an abrogation. And I have not seen any of its commentators address that. And Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi mentioned in al-Tafsir al-Kabir, the second investigation, that dhihar was among the severest forms of divorce in Jahiliyyah because it is the strongest possible in prohibition. If that ruling was established in the Shari'ah, then the verse abrogates it; otherwise, it is not considered an abrogation in the Shari'ah but only in the custom of Jahiliyyah. However, it is reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to her 'you have become forbidden' or 'I see that she has become forbidden to him', which indicates that it was (part of) the Shari'ah. As for what is reported that he refrained from giving a ruling, there is no evidence for that.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling discussing the explicit phrase of dhihar 'أنت علي كظهر أمي' and its historical background. The Hidayah states that this explicit phrase always creates dhihar (not talaq), even if the speaker intended divorce, because the phrase is specifically for dhihar and cannot be used for divorce (which is abrogated as a means? Actually the text says 'because it is not valid as abrogated' meaning talaq by that wording is not valid as it is considered abrogated, i.e., replaced by dhihar). The author notes an apparent contradiction: if dhihar was originally a form of talaq in Jahiliyyah, then making it dhihar in Islam would be an abrogation. But the Hidayah earlier says it was a form of talaq in Jahiliyyah, not in Islam. To resolve this, the author cites Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi who explains that dhihar was a severe type of talaq in pre-Islamic times. If that ruling was already established as part of the Shari'ah (i.e., before Islam), then the verse abrogates it. If not, then the verse is not an abrogation of a prior Islamic ruling but rather a reformation of a pre-Islamic practice. The mention of the Prophet's statement 'حرمت' indicates that at the time of the Prophet, it was considered a prohibition, implying it was recognized as a form of talaq or prohibition. This nuanced discussion is important for understanding the legal nature of dhihar in Islamic law: it is not a divorce but a separate institution, despite its origin in pre-Islamic divorce practices.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a previous ruling by a later one. In this passage, the discussion is about whether the Quranic verse on dhihar abrogates the pre-Islamic practice of dhihar being a form of talaq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, what is the ruling if a husband says 'antsi alaihi ka zahri ummi' intending divorce?
A) It is a valid divorce.
B) It is only dhihar, not divorce.
C) It is left to the intention of the husband.
D) It is considered an oath.

Key Takeaway
The explicit phrase of dhihar is exclusively for dhihar, not talaq; historical evidence confirms that the Quranic verse abrogated any prior status as divorce.

Persistence of Dhihar's Prohibition
Ruling with proof: persistence of dhihar prohibition and enforcement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the persistence of dhihar's prohibition after changes in marital status and apply the wife's right to compel kaffarah.

Core Idea
The prohibition of dhihar is not lifted by divorce, purchase, or apostasy—only kaffarah removes it.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author clarifies a key principle: the prohibition of intercourse after dhihar remains until kaffarah is performed. Even if the marriage ends and a new one begins, the obligation persists. Additionally, the wife has the right to demand kaffarah and the judge must enforce it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The prohibition of intercourse after dhihar remains until the husband performs kaffarah. This is the central rule.
The text emphasizes that only kaffarah lifts the prohibition.
2
Recognize scenarios that do not lift prohibition
The passage lists three specific changes that do not annul dhihar: (1) talaq ba'in followed by remarriage, (2) purchasing the wife after dhihar, (3) wife's apostasy and subsequent purchase. In all cases, kaffarah is still required.
This shows the obligation is attached to the act, not the marriage contract.
3
Understand the wife's right and judge's role
The wife can demand intercourse and must prevent her husband's enjoyment until kaffarah. The judge is obligated to compel the husband to perform kaffarah to remove hardship.
Consensus (ijma) is cited for this enforcement.
4
Analyze the commentary corrections
The author's qualification 'without desire' for the traveler is criticized in al-Nahr as a distortion—the ruling is general. Also, a discussion in al-Hidayah about whether dhihar is an abrogation is reconciled by considering it was originally a divorce in Jahiliyyah.
This shows the depth of Hanafi scholarly discourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أن هذه الحرمة لا ترتفع إلا بالكفارة فلا يبطل الظهار بزوال ملك النكاح ولا ببطلان حل المحلية حتى لو ظاهر منها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها لا يحل له وطؤها حتى يكفر، وكذا إذا كانت زوجته أمة وظاهر منها ثم اشتراها وكذا إذا كانت حرة فارتدت - والعياذ بالله تعالي عن الإسلام - ولحقت بدار الحرب فسبيت ثم اشتراها . وفي المحيط : أسلم زوج المجوسية فظاهر عرض الإسلام عليها صح لكونه من أهل الكفارة .اهـ. قالوا: وللمرأة أن تطالبه بالوطء وعليها أن تمنعه من الاستمتاع بها حتى يكفر وعلى القاضي أن يجبره على التكفير دفعاً خارج بالإجماع وكذا النظر إليها أو إلى نحو ظهرها بشهوة قوله : (بغير شهوة للشفقة) قال في النهر : تقييده بعدم الشهوة تحريف لأن ذلك لا يخص المسافر . من قبل قوله: (وهو يقتضي أن جعله ظهاراً ليس ناسخا أقول : فيه نظر لأنه يجوز أنه كان طلاقاً في الجاهلية والإسلام فجعله ظهاراً ثانياً يكون نسخاً وبه يحصل التوفيق بين كلامي الهداية، ولعله إنما ساق بعده عبارة التفسير الكبير للإشارة إلى الجواب بما قلنا فإن ذلك التوفيق يؤخذ منها قوله: (وعلى القاضي أن يجبره على التكفير الخ قال في حواشي مسكين : لا فائدة للإجبار على التكفير إلا الوطء
And the author indicated that this prohibition is not lifted except by kaffarah; so dhihar is not annulled by the termination of the marriage bond nor by the invalidation of permissible relationship, so that if he declared dhihar on her then divorced her irrevocably then married her, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her until he performs kaffarah. Likewise if his wife was a slave and he declared dhihar on her then bought her, and likewise if she was free and apostatized — may Allah protect us — and joined the land of war and was captured then he bought her. In al-Muhit: a husband of a Majusi wife became Muslim, then declared dhihar, presentation of Islam upon her, it is valid because he is from ahl al-kaffarah. They said: The woman has the right to demand intercourse from him, and she must prevent him from enjoying her until he performs kaffarah. And the judge is obligated to compel him to perform kaffarah to remove [harm] by consensus. And likewise looking at her or at the like of her back with desire. His saying: (without desire out of compassion). He said in al-Nahr: restricting it to without desire is a distortion, because that is not specific to the traveler. From before his saying: (And it requires that making it dhihar is not an abrogation). I say: there is consideration, because it is possible that it was a divorce in Jahiliyyah and Islam, so making it dhihar secondly would be an abrogation, and by this reconciliation between the two statements of al-Hidayah is achieved. Perhaps he cited the words of al-Tafsir al-Kabir afterwards to indicate the answer as we said, for that reconciliation is taken from it. His saying: (And the judge is obligated to compel him to perform kaffarah etc.) He said in the glosses of Miskin: There is no benefit in compelling to perform kaffarah except intercourse.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that the prohibition in dhihar is not lifted by any change in the marriage relationship except the performance of kaffarah. The author lists several scenarios: (1) if the woman is divorced irrevocably (talaq ba'in) and then remarried, (2) if the woman is a slave and after dhihar she is purchased by the husband, (3) if the woman apostatizes and leaves the land of Islam and is later captured and bought by the husband. In all these cases, the prohibition of intercourse remains until kaffarah is performed. The passage also discusses the wife's rights: she can demand intercourse and must withhold herself from her husband until he performs kaffarah. The judge is obligated to compel the husband to perform kaffarah to remove the hardship from the wife. The text also includes a correction from al-Nahr regarding the author's qualification of 'without desire' for the traveler: the ruling is not specific to travelers. Finally, there is a discussion reconciling statements in al-Hidayah about whether making dhihar is an abrogation, and a gloss from Miskin commenting on the judge's compulsion: the only benefit of compelling the kaffarah is to permit intercourse.

Key Terms
البائن (al-ba'in): Irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) that ends the marriage completely, unlike revocable divorce which allows remarriage without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband declares dhihar on his wife then divorces her irrevocably (talaq ba'in) and later re-marries her, what is the ruling on intercourse?
A) It is permissible because the marriage is new.
B) It remains prohibited until he performs kaffarah.
C) It is permissible only if he did not intend the dhihar.
D) It is prohibited and the marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of dhihar persists through changes in marital status; only kaffarah lifts it.

The Cause of Wajib Kaffarah in Zihar: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Explaining five Hanafi opinions on the sabab of kaffarah in zihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five Hanafi opinions on the cause (sabab) of wajib kaffarah in zihar and explain the thamarah al-khilaf for each.

Core Idea
Kaffarah in zihar is not automatic upon zihar alone; its cause is debated among Hanafis, with the majority requiring both zihar and 'awd.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq reveals a rich internal Hanafi debate about what exactly makes kaffarah obligatory in zihar. While all Hanafis agree that kaffarah is wajib, they differ on its legal cause (sabab). The author reports five positions transmitted from Al-Bada'i', each with distinct implications for when the obligation actually arises. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the correct legal reasoning in real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Zihar is a prohibited form of divorce-like speech. The Qur'an (58:3-4) prescribes kaffarah before resuming marital relations. The key term 'awd (return) is interpreted by Hanafis as the husband's determination ('azm) to have intercourse.
Other schools may interpret 'awd as actual intercourse, but this passage stays within Hanafi interpretation.
2
State the majority opinion and its proof
Al-'ammah (the majority) hold that the sabab is the combination of zihar and 'awd. Their dalil: the verse structure (fa' of sababiyya) and the dual nature of kaffarah (punishment + worship) requiring a dual cause.
The majority reasoning uses both linguistic and teleological arguments.
3
List the alternative opinions
Four other views are reported: (2) zihar as cause, 'awd as condition; (3) 'awd as cause, zihar as condition; (4) both as conditions, with a third cause; (5) each as both condition and cause.
Each view reflects a different method of relating the two elements.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a man pronounces zihar but never forms a determination to return, some opinions still obligate kaffarah (zihar alone as cause), while others do not (if 'awd is required). The majority requires both, so kaffarah is not wajib until 'awd occurs.
This directly affects when the husband must pay kaffarah before being allowed to resume relations.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text attributes the first view to 'al-'ammah (the general body), indicating it is the relied-upon position. The other views are transmitted but not given equal weight.
Later Hanafi fatwa works typically adopt the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعوده عزمه على وطئها) أي عود المظاهر المذكور في الآية عزمه على وطء المظاهر منها وهو بيان لسبب وجوب الكفارة. وقد اختلف فيه أصحابنا على أقوال محكية في البدائع ; فالعامة على أن السبب مجموع الظهار والعود لأنه المذكور قبل فاء السببية ولأن الكفارة دائرة بين العقوبة والعبادة فلا بد أن يكون سببها دائراً بين الحظر والاباحة حتى تتعلق العقوبة بالمحظور وهو الظهار والعبادة بالمباح وهو العزم على وطئها لأنه نقض للمنكر, وقيل الظهار سبب للإضافة والعود شرط وقيل عكسه, وقيل هما شرطان والسبب أمر ثالث وهو كون الكفارة طريقاً متعيناً لإيفاء حقها وكونه قادراً على إيفائه, وقيل كل منهما شرط وسبب ومن جعل السبب العزم أراد به العزم المؤكد حتى عزم ثم بدا له أن لا يطأها لا كفارة عليه لعدم العزم المؤكد لا أنها وجبت بنفس العزم ثم
His statement: (And his return is his determination to have intercourse with her) meaning the return of the mazhar mentioned in the verse is his determination to have intercourse with the one from whom he made zihar, and it is an explanation of the cause of the obligation of expiation. And our companions differed concerning it according to statements reported in al-Bada'i'; the general body is of the opinion that the cause is the combination of zihar and return because it is mentioned before the fa' of causality, and because expiation fluctuates between punishment and worship, so its cause must fluctuate between prohibition and permissibility, so that punishment attaches to the prohibited (which is zihar) and worship attaches to the permissible (which is determination to have intercourse with her) because it is a nullification of the reprehensible. And it was said that zihar is the cause of prohibition and return is a condition, and it was said the opposite. And it was said that both are conditions and the cause is a third thing, namely that expiation is a necessary way to fulfill her right and his ability to fulfill it. And it was said that each of them is both a condition and a cause. And whoever made the cause the determination intended the confirmed determination, so that if he determined then changed his mind and did not have intercourse with her, there is no expiation upon him due to the lack of confirmed determination, not that it was obligated by the determination itself.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the cause (sabab) that makes kaffarah obligatory in zihar. The author is explaining the word 'awd' (return) in the Qur'anic verse on zihar, which is interpreted as the husband's determination ('azm) to have intercourse with his wife after pronouncing zihar. The dispute is narrated from al-Bada'i'. The majority (al-'ammah) of Hanafi scholars hold that the cause is the combination of both zihar and 'awd. Their reasoning is that the word 'awd appears after the fa' of sababiyya in the verse, and kaffarah has a dual nature: punishment and worship. Therefore, its cause must also be dual: prohibition (zihar) and permission ('awd). Other opinions: (1) zihar is the cause of prohibition while 'awd is a condition, (2) the opposite, (3) both are conditions with a third cause—that kaffarah is the only means to fulfill the wife's right and the husband's ability, (4) each is both condition and cause. Those who make 'azm the cause mean a confirmed determination, so if he does not carry it out, no kaffarah. The text does not explicitly choose one view, but the first is attributed to the majority.

Key Terms
عود ('awd): In the verse of zihar, 'awd refers to the husband's determination ('azm) to have intercourse with his wife after pronouncing zihar, which triggers the obligation of kaffarah
سبب (sabab): The legal cause that directly triggers the obligation of kaffarah; different opinions on what constitutes the sabab
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for the cause to be effective, but is not itself the cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis in this passage, what is the cause (sabab) of wajib kaffarah in zihar?
A) Zihar alone
B) 'Awd (determination) alone
C) The combination of zihar and 'awd
D) A third factor external to both

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has multiple views on the sabab of kaffarah in zihar, but the majority holds that both zihar and 'awd (determination to resume) are required for the obligation to arise.

Ruling on Intercourse Before Expiation in Zihar
Ruling with proof on intercourse before expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse before expiation in zihar and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
No extra expiation for intercourse before expiation; one kaffarah suffices.

In zihar, the husband must expiate before resuming relations. But what if he has intercourse before completing expiation? The Hanafi school rules that no additional expiation is owed; the original kaffarah is enough, and he must seek forgiveness. This ruling is based on a hadith and the practice of Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intercourse before expiation of zihar. The ruling is that no additional kaffarah is wajib; only the original expiation is owed.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi: 'One expiation.' This shows that the original kaffarah suffices.
The hadith is a direct textual evidence.
3
Understand the secondary source
Seeking forgiveness (istighfar) is transmitted from Imam Malik in al-Muwatta', indicating that the act is a sin requiring repentance.
4
Note the consequence
No new obligation of kaffarah arises; the original kaffarah remains wajib, and istighfar is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو وطىء قبله استغفر ربه (فقط) أي لو وطىء قبل التكفير لا يجب عليه كفارة لأجل الوطء والواجب الكفارة الأولى لما رواه الترمذي في المظاهر يواقع قبل أن يكفر قال : كفارة واحدة. وأما الاستغفار فمنقول في الموطأ من قول مالك، والمراد منه التوبة من المعصية وهي حرمة الوطء قبل الكفارة قوله : ( وعوده عزمه على وطئها) أي عود المظاهر المذكور في الآية عزمه على وطء المظاهر منها وهو بيان لسبب وجوب الكفارة. وقد اختلف فيه أصحابنا على أقوال محكية في البدائع؛ فالعامة على أن السبب مجموع الظهار والعود لأنه المذكور قبل فاء السببية ولأن الكفارة دائرة بين العقوبة والعبادة فلا بد أن يكون سببها دائراً بين الحظر والاباحة حتى تتعلق العقوبة بالمحظور وهو الظهار والعبادة بالمباح وهو العزم على وطئها لأنه نقض للمنكر، وقيل الظهار سبب للإضافة والعود شرط وقيل عكسه، وقيل هما شرطان والسبب أمر ثالث وهو كون الكفارة طريقاً متعيناً لإيفاء حقها وكونه قادراً على إيفائه، وقيل كل منهما شرط وسبب ومن جعل السبب العزم أراد به العزم المؤكد حتى عزم ثم بدا له أن لا يطأها لا كفارة عليه لعدم العزم المؤكد لا أنها وجبت بنفس العزم ثم لو... والوطء لا يقضى به عليه إلا مرة واحدة في العمر كما مر في القسم ولهذا لو صار عنيناً بعد ما وطئها مرة لا يؤجل، واشتراط الأول لتكميل الصداق لاحتمال أن يرفع إلى من لا يرى التكميل بالخلوة. حموي عن الغاية قال : وفرض المسألة فيما إذا لم يطأها قبل الظهار أبداً بعيد. وقد يقال : فائدة الإجبار على التكفير رفع المعصية. قال الشلبي : ولا يجبر على شيء من الكفارات إلا كفارة الظهار ووجه عدم الجبر عليها أنها عبادة ا.هـ. قلت : وقد رأيت في البدائع ما يقرب ما استبعده وذلك حيث قال في بيان سبب الكفارة وقال بعضهم : كل واحد منهما - أي من الظهار والعود . شرط وسبب الوجوب أمر ثالث وهو كون الكفارة طريقاً متعيناً لإيفاء الواجب وكونه قادراً على الإيفاء لأن إيفاء حقها في الوطء واجب، ويجب عليه في الحكم إن كانت بكراً أو ثيباً ولم يطأها مرة، إن كانت ثيباً وقد وطئها مرة لا يجب فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى أيضاً لإيفاء حقها، وعند بعض أصحابنا يجب في الحكم أيضاً حتى يجبر عليه ولا يمكنه إيفاء الواجب إلا برفع الحرمة ولا ترتفع الحرمة إلا بالكفارة فتلزمه ضرورة إيفاء الواجب ا.هـ. والظاهر أن قوله لا يجب فيما بينه وبين تعالى صوابه يجب وأن (( لا زائدة من قلم الناسخ لما قالوا أنه يجب عليه ديانة أن يقصدها بالوطء أحياناً قوله : (وأما الاستغفار فمنقول في الموطأ) قال في الفتح وأما ذكر الاستغفار في الحديث فالله تعالى أعلم به وفي الموطأ من قول مالك ولفظه قال مالك فيمن يظاهر ثم يمسها قبل أن يكفر : يكف الله
سقطت كما قال بعضهم لأن الكفارة بعد سقوطها لا تعود إلا بسبب جديد؛ كذا في البدائع. لكن أورد على من جعل العود وحده سبباً أن الحكم يتكرر بتكرر سببه لا والكفارة تتكرر بتكرر الظهار لا العزم، وأنه لو قدمها على العزم صح ولو كان سبباً لم يصح، ولكن دفع الثاني بأنها إنما وجبت لرفع الحرمة الثابتة في الذات فتجوز بعد ثبوتها كما قلنا في الطهارة إنها جائزة قبل إرادة الصلاة مع أنها سببها لأنها شرعت لرفع الحدث فنجوز بعد وجوده، وأورد على من جعله الظهار فقط أن السبب ما دار بين محظور ومباح وهو محظور فقط فلا يصلح للسببية، وسنجيب عنه في الكفارة، ولم يظهر لي ثمرة الاختلاف بين الأقوال لاتفاقهم على جواز التكفير بعد الظهار قبل العزم، وعلى عدمه قبل الظهار، وعلى تكررها بتكرر الظهار وإن لم يتكرر العزم وعلى أنه لو عزم ثم ترك فلا إثم، وعلى عدم الكفارة لو أبانها بعده وبعد العزم، ومراد المشايخ من قولهم العزم على وطئها العزم على استباحة وطئها لا العزم على نفس الوطء لأنهم قالوا : المراد في الآية «ثم يعودون» بنقض ما قالوا رفعه وهو إنما يكون باستباحتها بعد تحريمها لكونه ضداً للحرمة لا نفس وطئها ولقد أبعد من قال إن المراد تكرار الظهار لأنه لو كان كذلك لقال تعالى ثم يعيدون ما قالوا من الإعادة لا من العود وتمام تحقيقه في التفسير الكبير للإمام فخر الدين .
His statement: 'So if he had intercourse before it, he seeks forgiveness from his Lord only' meaning if he had intercourse before expiation, no expiation is incumbent upon him for the intercourse, and the obligatory expiation is the first one, due to what al-Tirmidhi narrated about the one who makes zihar and then has intercourse before expiating: one expiation. As for seeking forgiveness, it is transmitted in al-Muwatta' from Malik's statement, and what is meant is repenting from the sin, which is the prohibition of intercourse before expiation. His statement: 'And his return is his determination to have intercourse with her' meaning the return of the one who makes zihar mentioned in the verse is his determination to have intercourse with her from whom he made zihar, and this is an explanation of the cause for the obligation of expiation. Our companions have differed on this, with opinions reported in al-Bada'i'; the general view is that the cause is the combination of zihar and the return because it is mentioned before the causative fa', and because expiation oscillates between punishment and worship, so its cause must oscillate between prohibition and permissibility, so that punishment is attached to the prohibited (zihar) and worship to the permissible (determination to have intercourse) because it is a nullification of the objectionable. It is said that zihar is the cause for the addition and the return is a condition, and it is said the opposite, and it is said both are conditions and the cause is a third thing: that expiation is the necessary path to fulfill her right and he is able to fulfill it. And it is said each of them is a condition and a cause. And whoever makes the cause the determination intends the emphasized determination; so if he determined then decided not to have intercourse, no expiation is upon him due to lack of emphasized determination, not that it became obligatory by the mere determination. Then... And intercourse is not required of him except once in a lifetime as mentioned in the chapter of division, so if he becomes impotent after having intercourse once, he is not given a delay. The first condition is for completing the dower due to the possibility that the case may be brought to someone who does not consider completion by seclusion. Himawi from al-Ghaya said: 'The assumption of the issue is when he has never had intercourse with her before zihar is far-fetched.' It may be said: The benefit of forcing expiation is removing the sin. Al-Shalabi said: 'He is not forced to any expiation except the expiation of zihar, and the reason for not forcing is that it is worship.' I (the commentator) say: I have seen in al-Bada'i' something close to what he considered far-fetched, for he said in explaining the cause of expiation: 'And some said: each of them (zihar and return) is a condition and the cause of obligation is a third thing: that expiation is the necessary path to fulfill the obligation and he is able to fulfill it, because fulfilling her right in intercourse is obligatory, and it is obligatory in legal ruling if she is a virgin or a non-virgin and he has not had intercourse with her once; if she is a non-virgin and he has had intercourse once, it is not required in what is between him and Allah Almighty also to fulfill her right. And according to some of our companions, it is required in legal ruling as well, so he is forced to do it, and he cannot fulfill the obligation except by removing the prohibition, and the prohibition is not removed except by expiation, so it becomes necessary for him by necessity of fulfilling the obligation.' And it appears that his statement 'not required in what is between him and Allah' should be 'required', and the 'not' is superfluous from the scribe's pen, because they said that it is required religiously that he intend her with intercourse occasionally. His statement: 'As for seeking forgiveness, it is transmitted in al-Muwatta'' — al-Fath said: 'As for the mention of seeking forgiveness in the hadith, Allah knows best. In al-Muwatta' from Malik's statement, its wording: Malik said about one who makes zihar then touches her before expiating: Allah will suffice...' It fell as some said because expiation after falling does not return except by a new cause; as in al-Bada'i'. But an objection was raised against those who make the return alone the cause: that the ruling is repeated by repetition of its cause, but expiation is repeated by repetition of zihar, not determination, and that if he performed it before determination, it would be valid, while if it were the cause it would not be valid. But the second [objection] is repelled by saying that it was only obligated to remove the prohibition established in the essence, so it is permissible after its establishment, as we said regarding purification that it is permissible before intending prayer although it is its cause because it was legislated to remove impurity, so it is permissible after its existence. And an objection was raised against those who make zihar alone the cause: that the cause is what revolves between prohibited and permissible, and it is only prohibited, so it is not suitable for causality, and we will answer it in the chapter of expiation. And the fruit of the difference between the opinions has not become clear to me, because they agree on the permissibility of expiation after zihar before determination, and on its impermissibility before zihar, and on its repetition by repetition of zihar even if determination does not repeat, and on that if he determines then leaves, there is no sin, and on the absence of expiation if he separates from her after it and after the determination. And the meaning of the elders' statement 'determination to have intercourse with her' is determination to make her permissible for intercourse, not determination on the actual intercourse itself, because they said: the meaning in the verse 'then they return' by nullifying what they said is its lifting, which is only by making her permissible after her prohibition, since it is the opposite of prohibition, not the actual intercourse. And far off is he who said that the meaning is repetition of zihar, because if it were so, Allah would have said 'then they repeat' what they said, from 'i'ada' not from 'awd. And its full verification is in al-Tafsir al-Kabir of Imam Fakhr al-Din.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the cause (sabab) that triggers the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) in zihar. The commentator, Zayla'i, first explains the matn: if a man has intercourse before expiating zihar, he only seeks forgiveness; no additional expiation is required. The one kaffarah suffices, based on a hadith from al-Tirmidhi. Seeking forgiveness is from Muwatta' Malik, meaning repentance from the sin of intercourse before expiation. Then the matn's phrase 'and his return is his determination to have intercourse' is explained as the 'awd mentioned in the Quran (Surah 58:3). This 'awd (determination) is the cause for kaffarah according to the popular view. The commentator then details the different Hanafi positions: (1) that the cause is the combination of zihar and 'awd, (2) zihar is the cause and 'awd is a condition, (3) 'awd is the cause and zihar is a condition, (4) both are conditions and the cause is a third element (the need to remove the prohibition to fulfill the obligation of marital rights), and (5) each is both condition and cause. The dispute is lengthy, with objections and responses. The commentator notes that despite the differences, they agree on practical outcomes: permissibility of expiation after zihar before determination, impermissibility before zihar, repetition of kaffarah with repeated zihar, no sin if one determines then abandons, and no kaffarah if divorced after determination. The key is that 'awd means determination to make her permissible, not actual intercourse. The author of al-Bada'i' is quoted. The passage ends with a reference to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's tafsir for full verification.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): Saying to one's wife 'you are like my mother's back' which prohibits intercourse and requires expiation.
عود (awd): The husband's determination to resume sexual relations with his wife after making zihar, as mentioned in the Quran (58:3).
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for zihar, consisting of freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct ruling if a man has intercourse before expiating zihar?
A) He must perform a second kaffarah for the intercourse.
B) He only seeks forgiveness and the original kaffarah suffices.
C) His original kaffarah is nullified and he must start over.
D) He must repeat the zihar declaration.

Key Takeaway
In zihar, intercourse before expiation does not create a second obligation of kaffarah; the original suffices, but repentance is required.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Cause of Kaffarah in Zihar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the cause of kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five positions on the cause of kaffarah in zihar and evaluate their practical consequences.

Core Idea
The cause of kaffarah is the combination of zihar and 'awd, but disagreement exists on the exact role of each.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi ikhtilaf on what exactly triggers the obligation of kaffarah in zihar. While the general view holds that the cause is the combination of zihar and 'awd (determination), other views elevate one or both to cause or condition. Remarkably, the dispute has no practical thamara, as all agree on outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is what makes kaffarah wajib in zihar: zihar alone, 'awd alone, combination, or something else.
2
List the five opinions
1) Combination of zihar and 'awd. 2) Zihar as cause, 'awd as condition. 3) 'Awd as cause, zihar as condition. 4) Both as conditions with a third cause. 5) Each as both condition and cause.
3
Examine the evidence for each
The combination view uses the Quranic causative 'fa' and the nature of kaffarah; objections are raised and answered.
4
Note the agreed thamara
All views agree on practical rulings: expiation valid after zihar before 'awd, repetition with zihar, no sin if determination abandoned, etc.
The commentator notes that the dispute has no practical fruit.
5
Understand the meaning of 'awd
'Awd means determination to make intercourse permissible, not the actual act of intercourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو وطىء قبله استغفر ربه (فقط) أي لو وطىء قبل التكفير لا يجب عليه كفارة لأجل الوطء والواجب الكفارة الأولى لما رواه الترمذي في المظاهر يواقع قبل أن يكفر قال : كفارة واحدة. وأما الاستغفار فمنقول في الموطأ من قول مالك، والمراد منه التوبة من المعصية وهي حرمة الوطء قبل الكفارة قوله : ( وعوده عزمه على وطئها) أي عود المظاهر المذكور في الآية عزمه على وطء المظاهر منها وهو بيان لسبب وجوب الكفارة. وقد اختلف فيه أصحابنا على أقوال محكية في البدائع؛ فالعامة على أن السبب مجموع الظهار والعود لأنه المذكور قبل فاء السببية ولأن الكفارة دائرة بين العقوبة والعبادة فلا بد أن يكون سببها دائراً بين الحظر والاباحة حتى تتعلق العقوبة بالمحظور وهو الظهار والعبادة بالمباح وهو العزم على وطئها لأنه نقض للمنكر، وقيل الظهار سبب للإضافة والعود شرط وقيل عكسه، وقيل هما شرطان والسبب أمر ثالث وهو كون الكفارة طريقاً متعيناً لإيفاء حقها وكونه قادراً على إيفائه، وقيل كل منهما شرط وسبب ومن جعل السبب العزم أراد به العزم المؤكد حتى عزم ثم بدا له أن لا يطأها لا كفارة عليه لعدم العزم المؤكد لا أنها وجبت بنفس العزم ثم لو... والوطء لا يقضى به عليه إلا مرة واحدة في العمر كما مر في القسم ولهذا لو صار عنيناً بعد ما وطئها مرة لا يؤجل، واشتراط الأول لتكميل الصداق لاحتمال أن يرفع إلى من لا يرى التكميل بالخلوة. حموي عن الغاية قال : وفرض المسألة فيما إذا لم يطأها قبل الظهار أبداً بعيد. وقد يقال : فائدة الإجبار على التكفير رفع المعصية. قال الشلبي : ولا يجبر على شيء من الكفارات إلا كفارة الظهار ووجه عدم الجبر عليها أنها عبادة ا.هـ. قلت : وقد رأيت في البدائع ما يقرب ما استبعده وذلك حيث قال في بيان سبب الكفارة وقال بعضهم : كل واحد منهما - أي من الظهار والعود . شرط وسبب الوجوب أمر ثالث وهو كون الكفارة طريقاً متعيناً لإيفاء الواجب وكونه قادراً على الإيفاء لأن إيفاء حقها في الوطء واجب، ويجب عليه في الحكم إن كانت بكراً أو ثيباً ولم يطأها مرة، إن كانت ثيباً وقد وطئها مرة لا يجب فيما بينه وبين الله تعالى أيضاً لإيفاء حقها، وعند بعض أصحابنا يجب في الحكم أيضاً حتى يجبر عليه ولا يمكنه إيفاء الواجب إلا برفع الحرمة ولا ترتفع الحرمة إلا بالكفارة فتلزمه ضرورة إيفاء الواجب ا.هـ. والظاهر أن قوله لا يجب فيما بينه وبين تعالى صوابه يجب وأن (( لا زائدة من قلم الناسخ لما قالوا أنه يجب عليه ديانة أن يقصدها بالوطء أحياناً قوله : (وأما الاستغفار فمنقول في الموطأ) قال في الفتح وأما ذكر الاستغفار في الحديث فالله تعالى أعلم به وفي الموطأ من قول مالك ولفظه قال مالك فيمن يظاهر ثم يمسها قبل أن يكفر : يكف الله
سقطت كما قال بعضهم لأن الكفارة بعد سقوطها لا تعود إلا بسبب جديد؛ كذا في البدائع. لكن أورد على من جعل العود وحده سبباً أن الحكم يتكرر بتكرر سببه لا والكفارة تتكرر بتكرر الظهار لا العزم، وأنه لو قدمها على العزم صح ولو كان سبباً لم يصح، ولكن دفع الثاني بأنها إنما وجبت لرفع الحرمة الثابتة في الذات فتجوز بعد ثبوتها كما قلنا في الطهارة إنها جائزة قبل إرادة الصلاة مع أنها سببها لأنها شرعت لرفع الحدث فنجوز بعد وجوده، وأورد على من جعله الظهار فقط أن السبب ما دار بين محظور ومباح وهو محظور فقط فلا يصلح للسببية، وسنجيب عنه في الكفارة، ولم يظهر لي ثمرة الاختلاف بين الأقوال لاتفاقهم على جواز التكفير بعد الظهار قبل العزم، وعلى عدمه قبل الظهار، وعلى تكررها بتكرر الظهار وإن لم يتكرر العزم وعلى أنه لو عزم ثم ترك فلا إثم، وعلى عدم الكفارة لو أبانها بعده وبعد العزم، ومراد المشايخ من قولهم العزم على وطئها العزم على استباحة وطئها لا العزم على نفس الوطء لأنهم قالوا : المراد في الآية «ثم يعودون» بنقض ما قالوا رفعه وهو إنما يكون باستباحتها بعد تحريمها لكونه ضداً للحرمة لا نفس وطئها ولقد أبعد من قال إن المراد تكرار الظهار لأنه لو كان كذلك لقال تعالى ثم يعيدون ما قالوا من الإعادة لا من العود وتمام تحقيقه في التفسير الكبير للإمام فخر الدين .
His statement: 'So if he had intercourse before it, he seeks forgiveness from his Lord only' meaning if he had intercourse before expiation, no expiation is incumbent upon him for the intercourse, and the obligatory expiation is the first one, due to what al-Tirmidhi narrated about the one who makes zihar and then has intercourse before expiating: one expiation. As for seeking forgiveness, it is transmitted in al-Muwatta' from Malik's statement, and what is meant is repenting from the sin, which is the prohibition of intercourse before expiation. His statement: 'And his return is his determination to have intercourse with her' meaning the return of the one who makes zihar mentioned in the verse is his determination to have intercourse with her from whom he made zihar, and this is an explanation of the cause for the obligation of expiation. Our companions have differed on this, with opinions reported in al-Bada'i'; the general view is that the cause is the combination of zihar and the return because it is mentioned before the causative fa', and because expiation oscillates between punishment and worship, so its cause must oscillate between prohibition and permissibility, so that punishment is attached to the prohibited (zihar) and worship to the permissible (determination to have intercourse) because it is a nullification of the objectionable. It is said that zihar is the cause for the addition and the return is a condition, and it is said the opposite, and it is said both are conditions and the cause is a third thing: that expiation is the necessary path to fulfill her right and he is able to fulfill it. And it is said each of them is a condition and a cause. And whoever makes the cause the determination intends the emphasized determination; so if he determined then decided not to have intercourse, no expiation is upon him due to lack of emphasized determination, not that it became obligatory by the mere determination. Then... And intercourse is not required of him except once in a lifetime as mentioned in the chapter of division, so if he becomes impotent after having intercourse once, he is not given a delay. The first condition is for completing the dower due to the possibility that the case may be brought to someone who does not consider completion by seclusion. Himawi from al-Ghaya said: 'The assumption of the issue is when he has never had intercourse with her before zihar is far-fetched.' It may be said: The benefit of forcing expiation is removing the sin. Al-Shalabi said: 'He is not forced to any expiation except the expiation of zihar, and the reason for not forcing is that it is worship.' I (the commentator) say: I have seen in al-Bada'i' something close to what he considered far-fetched, for he said in explaining the cause of expiation: 'And some said: each of them (zihar and return) is a condition and the cause of obligation is a third thing: that expiation is the necessary path to fulfill the obligation and he is able to fulfill it, because fulfilling her right in intercourse is obligatory, and it is obligatory in legal ruling if she is a virgin or a non-virgin and he has not had intercourse with her once; if she is a non-virgin and he has had intercourse once, it is not required in what is between him and Allah Almighty also to fulfill her right. And according to some of our companions, it is required in legal ruling as well, so he is forced to do it, and he cannot fulfill the obligation except by removing the prohibition, and the prohibition is not removed except by expiation, so it becomes necessary for him by necessity of fulfilling the obligation.' And it appears that his statement 'not required in what is between him and Allah' should be 'required', and the 'not' is superfluous from the scribe's pen, because they said that it is required religiously that he intend her with intercourse occasionally. His statement: 'As for seeking forgiveness, it is transmitted in al-Muwatta'' — al-Fath said: 'As for the mention of seeking forgiveness in the hadith, Allah knows best. In al-Muwatta' from Malik's statement, its wording: Malik said about one who makes zihar then touches her before expiating: Allah will suffice...' It fell as some said because expiation after falling does not return except by a new cause; as in al-Bada'i'. But an objection was raised against those who make the return alone the cause: that the ruling is repeated by repetition of its cause, but expiation is repeated by repetition of zihar, not determination, and that if he performed it before determination, it would be valid, while if it were the cause it would not be valid. But the second [objection] is repelled by saying that it was only obligated to remove the prohibition established in the essence, so it is permissible after its establishment, as we said regarding purification that it is permissible before intending prayer although it is its cause because it was legislated to remove impurity, so it is permissible after its existence. And an objection was raised against those who make zihar alone the cause: that the cause is what revolves between prohibited and permissible, and it is only prohibited, so it is not suitable for causality, and we will answer it in the chapter of expiation. And the fruit of the difference between the opinions has not become clear to me, because they agree on the permissibility of expiation after zihar before determination, and on its impermissibility before zihar, and on its repetition by repetition of zihar even if determination does not repeat, and on that if he determines then leaves, there is no sin, and on the absence of expiation if he separates from her after it and after the determination. And the meaning of the elders' statement 'determination to have intercourse with her' is determination to make her permissible for intercourse, not determination on the actual intercourse itself, because they said: the meaning in the verse 'then they return' by nullifying what they said is its lifting, which is only by making her permissible after her prohibition, since it is the opposite of prohibition, not the actual intercourse. And far off is he who said that the meaning is repetition of zihar, because if it were so, Allah would have said 'then they repeat' what they said, from 'i'ada' not from 'awd. And its full verification is in al-Tafsir al-Kabir of Imam Fakhr al-Din.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the cause (sabab) that triggers the obligation of kaffarah (expiation) in zihar. The commentator, Zayla'i, first explains the matn: if a man has intercourse before expiating zihar, he only seeks forgiveness; no additional expiation is required. The one kaffarah suffices, based on a hadith from al-Tirmidhi. Seeking forgiveness is from Muwatta' Malik, meaning repentance from the sin of intercourse before expiation. Then the matn's phrase 'and his return is his determination to have intercourse' is explained as the 'awd mentioned in the Quran (Surah 58:3). This 'awd (determination) is the cause for kaffarah according to the popular view. The commentator then details the different Hanafi positions: (1) that the cause is the combination of zihar and 'awd, (2) zihar is the cause and 'awd is a condition, (3) 'awd is the cause and zihar is a condition, (4) both are conditions and the cause is a third element (the need to remove the prohibition to fulfill the obligation of marital rights), and (5) each is both condition and cause. The dispute is lengthy, with objections and responses. The commentator notes that despite the differences, they agree on practical outcomes: permissibility of expiation after zihar before determination, impermissibility before zihar, repetition of kaffarah with repeated zihar, no sin if one determines then abandons, and no kaffarah if divorced after determination. The key is that 'awd means determination to make her permissible, not actual intercourse. The author of al-Bada'i' is quoted. The passage ends with a reference to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's tafsir for full verification.

ظهار (zihar): Saying to one's wife 'you are like my mother's back' which prohibits intercourse and requires expiation.
عود (awd): The husband's determination to resume sexual relations with his wife after making zihar, as mentioned in the Quran (58:3).

Conditions for Valid Zihar: Body Parts and Relatives
Commentary specifying which body parts and relatives make zihar effective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi conditions for a valid zihar and apply them to determine whether a given comparison is effective.

Core Idea
Zihar is valid only if the wife is compared to a permanently prohibited relative using a body part that is unlawful to look at.

In this lesson, we examine the specific conditions that make a zihar declaration effective according to the Hanafi school. The commentator explains which body parts and which relatives satisfy these conditions, excluding those that are permissible to look at or only temporarily prohibited. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly identifying a valid zihar.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two conditions from the text
Identify the first condition: the relative compared (mushabbah bih) must be a permanently unlawful female relative (muharramah mu'abbadah). The second condition: the body part mentioned must be one that is unlawful to look at from that relative.
The text explicitly mentions belly, thigh, private part as valid; hand, foot, side as invalid.
2
Define 'permanently unlawful relative'
A permanently unlawful relative is one whom the man can never marry, whether by lineage (nasab), marriage (sihr), or fosterage (rada'). Examples: mother, sister, aunt, foster mother.
Temporarily prohibited relatives like wife's sister, wife's aunt do not qualify.
3
Define the permissible body parts
The body part of the mushbah bih must be part of her 'awrah that it is not permissible to look at, even from a mahram. In Hanafi fiqh, the permissible parts to look at from a mahram are the face, hands, and feet; all else is 'awrah. Thus, belly, thigh, back, private parts are unlawful to look at; hand, foot, side are permissible.
The text adds that the knee is also considered unlawful to look at (from al-Khaniyya).
4
Apply conditions to examples
Test the examples: 'You are like my mother's knee' is valid (mother permanent, knee unlawful); 'Your thigh is like my mother's thigh' is invalid because the comparison is to the wife's thigh, not the mother's – the condition is on the body part of the mushabbah bih.
Also note: 'You are like the belly of my sister' valid; 'like the hand of my mother' invalid.
5
Distinguish invalid relatives
Relatives who are only temporarily prohibited (e.g., wife's sister, wife's aunt) do not satisfy the first condition, regardless of the body part.
The text explicitly excludes 'his wife's sister, her aunt, her maternal aunt'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبطنها وفخذها وفرجها كظهرها أي الأم وهي المشبه به وقدمنا أن المعتبر فيه عضو لا يحل النظر إليه من محرمة تأبيداً وهذه الأعضاء كذلك، فخرج عضو يحل النظر إليه كاليد والرجل والجنب فلا يكون ظهاراً. وفي الخانية : أنت علي كركبة أمي في القياس يكون مظاهراً، ولو قال فخذك كفخذ أمي لا يكون مظاهراً .اهـ. لفقد الشرط في الثانية من جهة المشبه قوله : (وأخته وعمته وأمه رضاعاً كأمه أي نسباً لما قدمنا أن المعتبر في المشبه به كونها محرمة تأبيداً نسباً أو صهراً أو رضاعاً، فخرج من لا تحرم تأبيداً كأخت امرأته وعمتها وخالتها
His statement: (And her belly, her thigh, and her private part are like her back) i.e., the mother, who is the object of comparison. And we have previously stated that the condition in it is a body part which it is not permissible to look at from a permanently unlawful female relative, and these body parts are such. Thus, a body part which it is permissible to look at, like the hand, the foot, and the side, is excluded, so it is not zihar. In al-Khaniyya: 'You are to me like the knee of my mother' by analogy he is a muzahir (one who makes zihar). And if he said 'Your thigh is like the thigh of my mother', he is not a muzahir because of the lack of the condition in the second from the aspect of the thing compared. His statement: (And his sister, his aunt, and his foster mother like his mother by lineage) because we have previously stated that the condition in the object of comparison is that she is permanently unlawful by lineage, marriage, or fosterage. Thus, one who is not permanently unlawful, like his wife's sister, her aunt, and her maternal aunt, is excluded.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement specifying which body parts and relatives are valid for making zihar. The commentator explains the matn's phrase 'her belly, her thigh, and her private part are like her back' — the standard is the mother, and the condition for a valid comparison is that the body part is one which it is not permissible to look at from a permanently unlawful female relative (muharramah mu'abbadah). These parts (belly, thigh, private part) meet that condition, whereas parts like the hand, foot, or side are permissible to look at and therefore do not constitute zihar. al-Khaniyya provides examples: saying 'you are like my mother's knee' makes one a muzahir, but 'your thigh is like my mother's thigh' does not, because the comparison must be to a body part of the female relative that is itself unlawful to look at. Then the matn adds sister, aunt, and foster mother: the condition for the relative compared (the mushabbah bih) is that she is permanently unlawful (muharramah mu'abbadah), whether by lineage, marriage (sihr), or fosterage. So relatives like a wife's sister, aunt, or maternal aunt, who are not permanently unlawful (they become unlawful only while married to their relative), do not count.

Key Terms
محرمة تأبيداً (muharramah mu'abbadah): A female relative who is permanently unlawful to marry, such as mother, sister, aunt, etc.
مشبه به (mushabbah bih): The person or thing to which another is compared in a statement of zihar (e.g., 'like my mother's back').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid comparison for zihar if a man says to his wife 'You are like ____'?
A) The hand of my mother
B) The thigh of my wife's sister
C) The belly of my sister
D) The foot of my aunt

Key Takeaway
Zihar is valid only when the wife is compared to a permanently unlawful female relative and the body part mentioned is one that is unlawful to look at from that relative.

Hadith of the Man Who Had Intercourse Before Expiating Zihar
Narration of a hadith as proof for seeking forgiveness after intercourse before expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for intercourse before zihar expiation and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A man who has intercourse before expiating zihar needs only to seek forgiveness, not perform an additional expiation.

This lesson examines a key hadith used by the Hanafi school to determine the ruling for a man who has intercourse with his wife after making zihar before performing the required expiation. The hadith, transmitted by Imam Muhammad in al-Asl and supported by other chains, provides clear guidance: the Prophet commanded only to seek forgiveness and not repeat the act until expiation is done. Understanding this proof strengthens the Hanafi position and illustrates the school's methodology of accepting well-supported mursal reports.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: if a man makes zihar and then has intercourse before expiating, he must seek forgiveness (istighfar) and refrain until he expiates; no additional kaffarah is required.
2
Identify the hadith and its transmission
Locate the primary source: Imam Muhammad's al-Asl via a balagh (mursal). Then note the connected chain via Abu Yusuf–Isma‘il ibn Muslim–Sulayman al-Ahwal–Tawus.
Hanafi scholars consider Imam Muhammad's balaghat as musnad due to his reliability.
3
Analyze the command (dalala)
Extract the legal implication: the Prophet 'commanded him to seek forgiveness from Allah and not to return until he expiates.' The absence of any additional expiation indicates that no extra kaffarah is due.
The imperative 'amara' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Evaluate the strength of the hadith (thubut)
Assess the transmission: the chain through Isma‘il ibn Muslim and Tawus is considered weak by some, but supporting narrations from the four Sunan and al-Bazzar strengthen it. Hanafis accept it as reliable proof.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qat‘i al-dalala).
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude: a person in this situation must repent (istighfar) and then perform the expiation for the original zihar. No additional penalty is incurred.
This ruling is consistent with the broader Hanafi principle of repenting from sin before fulfilling obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي حاشية نوح أفندي على الدرر قال الشيخ قاسم في تخريج أحاديث الاختيار ذكر الاستغفار فيه الإمام محمد بن الحسن في الأصل فقال باب الظهار : بلغنا عن رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أن رجلاً ظاهر من امرأته فوقع عليها قبل أن يكفر فبلغ ذلك النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فأمره أن يستغفر الله تعالى ولا يعود حتى يكفر. وبلاغات محمد مسندة لمن تتبعها وقد أسند هذا في كتاب الصوم عن أبي يوسف عن اسمعيل بن مسلم عن سليمان الأحول عن طاوس قال : ظاهر رجل من امرأته فأبصرها في القمر وعليها خلخال فضة فأعجبته فوقع عليها قبل أن يكفر فسأل عن ذلك رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فأمره أن يستغفر الله ولا يعود حتى يكفر. ووصله الحاكم بذكر ابن عباس واسمعيل بن مسلم وإن كان ضعيفاً فقد تابعه على الأصل من علمت في رواية الأربعة والبزار والله
And in the gloss of Nuh Afandi on al-Durar, al-Shaykh Qasim said in his Takhrij Ahadith al-Ikhtiyar: Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan mentioned seeking forgiveness in al-Asl and said in the chapter of zihar: It has reached us from the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) that a man made zihar of his wife and then had intercourse with her before he expiated. That reached the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he commanded him to seek forgiveness from Allah and not to return until he expiates. And the mursal narrations of Muhammad are considered musnad (connected) by those who investigate. And he narrated this in the Book of Fasting from Abu Yusuf from Isma'il ibn Muslim from Sulayman al-Ahwal from Tawus who said: A man made zihar of his wife, and he saw her in the moonlight with a silver anklet on her, and he was charmed by her, so he had intercourse with her before expiating. He asked about that, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded him to seek forgiveness from Allah and not to return until he expiates. And al-Hakim connected it with the mention of Ibn Abbas and Isma'il ibn Muslim, although it is weak, but it has been followed in the original by those known in the narration of the four and al-Bazzar. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narration presented as proof (dalil) for the ruling that one who has intercourse before expiating zihar must seek forgiveness. The hadith is cited from the gloss of Nuh Afandi on al-Durar, quoting al-Shaykh Qasim's work on hadith verification. The original source is Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, where he mentions a report (balagh) from the Prophet that a man who made zihar and had intercourse before expiation was commanded to seek forgiveness and not to repeat the act until he expiates. Imam Muhammad's balaghat (mursal reports) are considered connected (musnad) according to scholars who investigate. Then a second chain is provided: from Abu Yusuf from Isma'il ibn Muslim from Sulayman al-Ahwal from Tawus, giving the story of a man who saw his wife in moonlight and was attracted, then had intercourse before expiation. The Prophet commanded him to seek forgiveness and not do it again. Although al-Hakim's chain including Ibn Abbas and Isma'il ibn Muslim is considered weak, it has supporting narrations from the four (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah) and al-Bazzar. This hadith supports the ruling mentioned earlier that no additional kaffarah is required, only seeking forgiveness.

Key Terms
بلاغات محمد (balaghat Muhammad): Mursal reports transmitted by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani without a full chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet command the man who had intercourse before expiating zihar to do?
A) Perform an additional expiation
B) Seek forgiveness and not return until he expiates
C) Divorce his wife immediately
D) Fast for two months

Key Takeaway
When a man has intercourse before expiating zihar, the Prophet commanded only to seek forgiveness and not return until expiating—no additional expiation is required.
